56 stories, US-114 .. US-169, in five phases:
  A  US-114..115  screen layout (light button to the toolbar, map background)
  B  US-116..122  the map system (catalog, validator, step accrual, list, strip, detail, opponents)
  C  US-123..129  owning several Digimon (profile + migration, multi-state, freeze, party, drops)
  D  US-130..132  Jogress (data + validator, recipe authoring, performing one)
  E  US-133..169  roster wiring: 11 device trees, then 26 orphan sweeps

Measured baseline at the start of this wave (regenerate with Appendix B of the PRD):
  1025 roster entries; 868 playable, 157 dexOnly
  88 nodes in Resources/evolutions.json across 6 lines
  780 playable orphans - Digitama 51, Baby I 38, Baby II 42, Child 109,
                         Adult 168, Perfect 153, Ultimate 203, Armor-Hybrid 16
  57 Digitama sprites, 6 of them wired
---

## Codebase Patterns
- **THE SPRITE SLOT IS MEASURED BY THE MAP BAND, AND MUST BE RE-MEASURED WHENEVER A ROW IS ADDED **OR
  REMOVED** FROM `ContentView`'s VStack (US-219).** The map is painted off `SpriteSlotBoundsKey`, so the
  longest run of rows differing between a `-mapDemo=01_grassland` and a `-mapDemo=none` shot IS the play
  area, in screenshot px (halve for points @2x). **Threshold that run at 0.5 of the width, not 0.75** —
  dark rows of the asset differ in only ~73% and a higher cut truncates the band. `MainScreenLayoutTests`'
  pinned slot numbers are EVIDENCE; US-194's were arithmetic rather than measurement and six later
  row-deleting stories left them ~50% low with nothing failing. Measured 2026-07-24: flexible row
  63.5 / 66.5 / 76.0pt and 80% band 50 / 53 / 60pt on 41 / 42 / 46mm.
- **THE SIMULATOR BUNDLE ID IS `com.digivpet.DigiVPet` (US-214).** `simctl launch` with anything else
  fails as `FBSOpenApplicationServiceErrorDomain code=4`, which reads like a launch crash. The whole
  screenshot recipe, in ONE Bash call with `DEVELOPER_DIR` exported in it:
  `xcrun simctl bootstatus <id> -b` -> `install <id> <DerivedData>/.../DigiVPet.app` ->
  `launch <id> com.digivpet.DigiVPet -healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt -<demoFlag>` -> `sleep 20`
  -> `io <id> screenshot <path>`. Devices: 46mm `BA425DD4-8856-4933-8198-0E4B89960E48`, 42mm
  `F4A12A1C-1C5E-4B83-8278-341634CDE4F5`; both stay booted, so no shutdown/erase/boot cycle is needed
  (that costs ~30 s and forces a reinstall).
- **SCREENSHOT THE DEVICE BEFORE YOU LAUNCH ANYTHING ON IT (US-215).** A system permission alert left
  over from an earlier session survives `terminate`, `uninstall` AND a reinstall, and every screenshot
  after that photographs the alert rather than the app — `-noNotificationPrompt` cannot help, since
  the alert is already up. A bare `xcrun simctl io <id> screenshot /tmp/probe.png` costs a second and
  says which of the two watches is clean. Clearing one needs the full `shutdown` + `erase` + `boot`
  (~90 s, app reinstalled afterwards), so switching watches is usually the cheaper move.
- **NEVER JUDGE ON-SCREEN MOTION FROM A BURST OF SCREENSHOTS (US-216).** Back-to-back
  `xcrun simctl io <id> screenshot` calls starve the app's `TimelineView`, so an animation that runs
  perfectly delivers only a couple of frames per capture and reads as frozen or crawling. Put a
  `sleep 2` BEFORE each shot in the loop and the real pace appears. This bites hardest on anything
  with a catch-up cap (`MovementModel.maximumCatchUpSteps`), which by design cannot make up for the
  frames the screenshot load ate.
- **MEASURE "DID THE SPRITE MOVE" BY LIT-PIXEL CENTROID, NEVER BY BOUNDING BOX (US-217).** Every
  sprite here animates in place — the egg wobbles, the two walk frames differ in width — so
  `xmin`/`xmax` shift between frames with zero travel and a bbox comparison reports motion that is
  not there. Take the centroid of `luma > 40` over the sprite band only (rows 140-265 on the 42mm
  screenshot, which excludes the stats strip and the name line): it is stable to three decimals
  across a pose change and moves by exactly the travel. **numpy is NOT installed; PIL 12.3.0 is** —
  a plain `im.convert('L').load()` double loop over ~125 rows is well under a second per shot.
- **A GUARD ADDED "FIRST" STEALS AN OLDER GUARD'S MESSAGE, AND SOME TEST PINS THAT STRING (US-218).**
  A fixture can be in two refusing states at once — `DeathTests`' dead EGG is both dead and unhatched
  — so `grep -rn '<the old reason>' Tests` BEFORE putting a new guard ahead of the existing ones, and
  re-pin the assertion to the new reason with a comment rather than loosening it to "some block".
  The matching evidence pattern: a "spends nothing" criterion is ONE `Equatable` snapshot struct
  (`EggActionsTests.Ledger`, `@MainActor init(_ model:)` over meat, both charges, all four
  `EnergyType.allCases`, `careMistakeCount` and the three stage counters), compared before/after —
  not six assertions that each miss the currency the story forgot to name.
- **A DEMO SEED IS HOW YOU SCREENSHOT AN ACTION'S MESSAGE, BECAUSE `simctl` CANNOT TAP (US-218).**
  Fixed shape: a `#if DEBUG` `seedXDemoIfRequested()` called from the block at the end of
  `MainScreenModel.start()`, guarded on a `-xDemo` launch argument, ending in `actionDuration = 60`
  (the shipped 2s hold does not survive boot + install + launch + `sleep 20`) and then the REAL
  action call. Staging the outcome by hand would make the screenshot prove nothing.
- **THE CHEAPEST BEFORE/AFTER IS `git stash push -- Sources Tests`, REBUILD, CAPTURE, `stash pop`
  (US-217).** ~90 s per side, and it produces the only evidence that settles a "does it still X"
  criterion. Use `uninstall` + `install` when the story is about a FRESH save, or the previous run's
  hatched Digimon is still in the store.
- **A DERIVED-PER-DIGIMON VALUE USES A PINNED SEED FUNCTION, NEVER `hashValue` (US-214).** Swift seeds
  `Hasher` per process, so anything derived from it changes on every relaunch while still passing
  `XCTAssertEqual(f(id), f(id))`. `SleepRoutine.seed(for:)` is FNV-1a over the id's UTF-8 bytes, fed to
  `SeededGenerator` (SplitMix64) for the actual draws, and its tests pin LITERAL seeds — that literal
  is the only assertion that catches the relaunch drift. Copy it for any future per-Digimon flavour.
- **THREE SETS OF TOTALS EXIST AND THEY ARE NOT INTERCHANGEABLE (US-206).** `GameState.stage/lifetime
  MetricTotals` = the Digimon's life, what an EVOLUTION is gated on. `PlayerProfile.recorded(forMap:)`
  = progress toward a map's BOSS, which a flee/loss takes 500/1,000 off. `PlayerProfile.mapMetrics(
  forMap:)` = what was earned WHILE THAT MAP WAS SELECTED, what a map's EGG is gated on, and which
  only ever goes up. A new gate must pick one on purpose. The map-scoped set is read through
  `ConditionContext.mapScoped` (`Sources/MapScopedContext.swift`) and credited only via
  `MainScreenModel.creditMapMetrics` / `creditMapCare` / `profile.recordBattle(won:forMap:)` — all of
  which drop the tick when no map (or an unknown map) is selected.
- **SCOPING A CONDITION IS A NEW `ConditionContext` CONSTRUCTOR, NEVER A NEW `ConditionWindow`.**
  Adding a `.map` window would touch the validator, `answerableWindows`, every hint string and all
  authored JSON. Building the same context type off different counters changes nothing about the
  vocabulary — same `ConditionReveal`, same `ConditionEvaluator`, same authored conditions — which is
  why US-206 broke only 3 pre-existing tests.
- **A NEW PER-METRIC CONSUMER TAKES `MetricCreditor.credit`'s RETURN VALUE, IT NEVER CALLS
  `MetricLedger.claim`.** Second SPENDER of one claim = fine; second CLAIM of one reading = the
  double-count bug. Four consumers are wired this way (map steps, map-scoped counters, train charges,
  clean charges). See `docs/metric-accounting.md`.
- **THREE RECORDS OF "THE PLAYER HAS THIS EGG", ALSO NOT INTERCHANGEABLE (US-207).**
  `GameStore.dexIds()` = has EVER owned, never shrinks, survives death — `MapDetail.make(discovered:)`
  and `DigitamaSlotDetail.isRevealed`. `GameStore.heldDigitamaIds()` = in the BOX right now, empties
  on hatch — `MapDetail.make(held:)`, `isHeld`, and the drop engine's refusal to drop a duplicate.
  The slot's conditions being met = a third thing again. A held egg is always revealed; a revealed
  one need not be held.
- **AN EGG DROPS ONLY ON A BATTLE WON, AND ONLY AT A 50% ROLL (US-207).**
  `MainScreenModel.checkForDigitamaDrop()` has exactly ONE caller — `finishBattle()`, gated on
  `bout.report.playerWon`. Never re-add a call after a train, a refresh or a timer: "a drop is a
  reward for a thing the player did" is the rule, and a miss must consume nothing (draw the roll
  before `award`, write nothing until it passes). `DigitamaDropEngine.winDropChance` /
  `findsTheEgg(chance:using:)` hold the chance.
- **A MODEL TEST THAT HANGS OFF A BATTLE RESULT DECIDES THE FIGHT BY THE POWER GAP, NOT THE SEED.**
  `BossEncounterTests`' pattern: player `stage`/`strengthStat` against a fixed one-node pool
  (`.ultimate`/30 vs a Baby-I = sure win; `.babyI`/0 vs an Ultimate = sure loss), then ASSERT
  `bout.report.playerWon` so a seed regression fails loudly instead of testing the other branch.
  And `model.battle()` silently returns nil (so `finishBattleRound` does too) unless all three are
  stocked: `battleCharges > 0`, `stageEnergy[.strength]` >= `BattleCost.energy` (5), no other
  minigame pending.
- **A SEEDED GENERATOR FACTORY IS CALLED ONCE PER CHECK, SO TWO OUTCOMES IN ONE RUN NEED A SEED
  QUEUE.** `makeDropGenerator: () -> SeededGenerator` hands back a FRESH generator every time, so one
  seed = one repeated outcome. A small class the escaping closure advances (see `SeedQueue` in
  `Tests/DigitamaDropTests.swift`) is how "miss this one, hit the next" is said. Measured for
  `Double.random(in: 0..<1)`: seed 1 -> 0.318, seed 2 -> 0.757.
- **CONSUMPTION WAVE: A "SPENDABLE CHARGE" HAS FIVE SEAMS, COPY THE BATTLE CHARGE (US-176) FOR EACH.**
  (1) GameState optional storage `xChargesStorage`/`xProgressStorage` + computed getters (nil reads 0)
  + `creditXCharges(amount:per:maxCharges:)` — the while-loop-with-remainder-dropped-at-cap shape;
  (2) ConsumptionConfig `maxXCharges` in the struct AND consumption.json AND the `caps` validator list
  AND ConsumptionConfigTests' 4 constructors; (3) refresh() claims the day-total off `MetricLedger`
  via `metricLedger.claim(.healthMetric, dayTotal:, now:, calendar:)` — the SHARED delta, read from
  `dayReadings.quantities[.<QuantityMetric>]` (steps/activeEnergy/exercise), never a second HealthKit
  read; (4) a `DashBar(...dashHeight:5)` added to ContentView's currency HStack — SAME row, so sprite
  scale (US-172/US-174) is untouched; (5) `model.xCharges`/`xChargeCap` computed off `state`/config.
  US-177 (train charge from active calories) mirrored all five off US-176.
- **CHANGING AN ACTION'S CURRENCY RIPPLES TO EVERY TEST THAT FUNDED IT.** US-177 moved training off
  Strength/Stamina energy onto a charge; ~12 test files seeded strength energy to fund training and
  had to seed `trainCharges` instead — the 0-charge default silently BLOCKS the round, and a blocked
  round counts no session, so `stageTrainingSessions` assertions flip too. grep
  `TrainAction.begin|TrainAction.train(|\.train()` before assuming a fixture is unaffected. Same trap
  will hit feeding/cleaning if their currency is ever repriced.
- **WHEN ACTION A BORROWS ACTION B's CONSTANTS AND B CHANGES, DECOUPLE A FIRST.** `BattleCost`
  borrowed `TrainAction.energyCostPerTraining`/`payableWith`/`insufficientEnergyReason`; US-177
  removed those from `TrainAction`, breaking Battle.swift's compile. Gave BattleCost its own copies.
  `BackgroundRefreshTests`' refresh-level class is named `ClosedAppRecomputeTests` (not the file name).
- **PHASE E, ULTIMATE SWEEP: RE-RUN `xcodegen generate` AFTER WRITING THE NEW TEST FILE, OR IT NEVER
  RUNS.** US-166 ran `xcodegen generate` FIRST (to pick up the JSON) then wrote
  `UltimateSweepIToMTests.swift` — the project glob had already been captured, so `build-for-testing`
  compiled the whole target GREEN and the suite went 0 failures while the new class was simply not in
  the bundle (its Test Suite line never appeared, test count did not rise). Generate AGAIN after the
  file exists; confirm with `grep -c <ClassName> DigiVPet.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj` and by seeing the
  count climb.
- **PHASE E, ULTIMATE RUNG: A JOGRESS-RESULT ULTIMATE IS WIRED UNLESS A DEVICE TREE RESERVES IT TO
  NO-NODE (the Cernumon precedent, US-164).** `jogress.json` naming a result is NOT a reason to skip
  it — `cernumon`, `aegisdramon`, `millenniumon` are all jogress results AND wired nodes. What makes
  C-D set Chaosdramon/Chaosmon aside is that `DMCVersion5/4TreeTests` and `PendulumMetalEmpireTreeTests`
  pin them to NO evolution node. US-166 wired Mastemon (directly off Angewomon, both jogress parents
  being Perfects) and Mitamamon (Cernumon shape, off Garudamon, its jogress parents both Ultimates)
  because no tree reserved either. `UltimateSweepCToDTests.jogressReachable` is the set of the C-D
  results left unwired, and its "true remainder" assertions (64->37 here) are relative to the whole
  current bucket, so every later sweep moves them.
- **PHASE E, ULTIMATE RUNG: A LATER SWEEP THAT FORKS A PERFECT AN EARLIER SWEEP TREATED AS A LEAF
  BREAKS TWO SHAPES, NOT ONE.** US-166 branched Megalo Growmon, which US-163/A-B had cleared as a
  LEAF (its only edge the isDefault climb to Breakdramon). That fails `UltimateSweepAToBTests`
  `testEveryEarnedBranchCarriesCriteriaAndEveryLeafClimbDoesNot` (`evolutions.count == 1` — special-
  case it) AND `testTheFiveClearedLeavesClimbForADigimonThatEarnedNothing`, which read the climb as
  `evolutions.first` — that is now an EARNED branch, so change it to `first(where: \.isDefault)`. Grep
  every UltimateSweep file's `leafParents` for a parent you intend to branch, not just the PerfectSweep
  `branchedBySweeps` dicts.
- **PHASE E, ULTIMATE RUNG: ONE ORPHAN COSTS ONE NODE, AND THAT IS THE WHOLE STORY.** The rung is
  TERMINAL, so no out-edge is owed; `EvolutionCriteriaTests.branchingNodes` is Child and Adult only,
  so a forked Perfect owes no junk floor; and every line but `algomon` already has a Perfect, so
  none can be opened. US-163 wired thirty orphans with thirty nodes. The cost is entirely knock-on.
- **PHASE E: FORKING A PERFECT IS THE NEW BREAKAGE, AND TWO GREPS FIND IT.** Every Perfect carried
  exactly one `isDefault` climb until US-163; six `PerfectSweep*Tests` assert `evolutions.count == 1`
  over their `swept` list and four device-tree files assert an exact `targets(of:)` list. Run
  `grep -n "is not a single climb" Tests` and `grep -rn 'XCTAssertEqual(try targets(of:' Tests` for
  every parent BEFORE authoring, and read a climb as `first(where: \.isDefault)`, never as `first`.
- **`SeedRosterTests.earnedPath` PREFERS THE EARNED EDGE, SO BRANCHING A PERFECT ON US-002's NAMED
  LINES SILENTLY REDIRECTS THEM.** `lilimon` and `metalgreymon` are both walked by
  `testTheThreeNamedLinesAreTheOnesShipped`; an earned branch on either moves the line's endpoint
  away from Rosemon / WarGreymon. US-163 lost its BOLDED parent for BanchoLilimon to this and took
  Lilamon (the sister form, cited on the same page) instead. Grep the test before branching on
  `palmon`, `dmc-v1` or `dmc-v2`.
- **A LEAF'S FIRST IN-EDGE IS ITS `isDefault` CLIMB AND SO CARRIES NO CRITERIA.**
  `SeedRosterTests.testEveryNonTerminalNodeHasExactlyOneDefaultEdge` fails a node with edges and no
  fallback. That is also the standing reading of "no edge is unconditional": the AC binds the EARNED
  edges, because US-020 takes an `isDefault` edge whatever its gates say.
- **A LINE CAN BE CLOSED TO A NODE BY ART RATHER THAN BY SHAPE.** Armagemon belongs on `diablomon`
  and cannot go there: its bolded parent Kuramon is a Baby I (`invalidStageTransition`) and BOTH
  Perfect rungs the Kuramon swarm climbs through, Chrysalimon and Infermon, are idle-only
  (`edgeToDexOnlyNode`) — and the Perfect rung closed in US-162, so nothing can be authored into it.
  Check the cited line's Perfect rung for dexOnly art before assuming a thematic home is available.
- **AN X-ANTIBODY MEGA'S WHOLE `Evolves From` IS USUALLY ULTIMATES, SO THE STRONG VARIANT RULE IS
  THE ONLY READING — AND IT IS FREE.** Hang it on the Perfect its base form hangs on, with a
  distinct `requiredEnergy`. Barbamon X, Beelzebumon X and Belphemon X all landed that way.
- **WIKIMON: USE `opensearch` BEFORE CONCLUDING A DIGIMON HAS NO PAGE.**
  `curl -s "https://wikimon.net/api.php?action=opensearch&search=<name>&limit=50&format=json"`.
  A raw fetch of a wrong title returns an EMPTY BODY, not a 404. `Agumon YnK` is
  `Agumon -Yuki no Kizuna-`; `BlackWarGreymon X` is `Black War Greymon (X-Antibody)`.
- **PHASE E: A LINE'S RUNG OPENS UNDER ITS JUNK CHAMPION, AND THAT IS WHAT PROMOTES ITS EGGS.**
  US-161 left `adventure02` closed because XV-mon carries only one of the line's two eggs; US-162
  branched Nise Drimogemon instead — the junk Adult that takes the `isDefault` fall of ALL THREE
  Children — and promoted both at once. Same for `commandramon`'s Damemon. **Look at which Champion
  every Child of the line falls into before looking at which Champion is cited**; US-133's Scumon
  rule already makes an earned branch off a junk Adult legal, and the junk one is reachable from
  every thread by construction.
- **PHASE E: A LINE CAN BE PERMANENTLY UNOPENABLE — CHECK `reachesUltimate` FROM ITS OWN EGGS
  FIRST.** `algomon`'s Ghost Digitama reaches only Algomon (Adult), Mimicmon and Witchmon; the
  Labramon -> Siesamon thread that every citation points at hangs off `paomon`, one of the thirteen
  Baby I no Digitama can reach. Opening the rung there breaks US-159's "no unraisable egg on a line
  that HAS a Perfect rung" invariant — which is asserted in ANOTHER story's file
  (`PerfectSweepNToRTests.testVitalsFiveDigitamaWereAllPromotedAtOnce`), so it is easy to miss until
  the suite is red.
- **PHASE E: BEFORE AUTHORING, GREP FOR EVERY CLIMB TARGET AND EVERY PARENT.** `grep -rn
  'Set(graph.parents' Tests` and `grep -rn 'evolutions.count,' Tests` are now the two greps that
  matter most: US-162 broke seven parent-set ledgers and six `evolutions.count` claims across nine
  files. Fix each by NAMING the new parent or with a named exception — never by loosening to a
  superset or a `>=`. A "still owed" pin can also live in THREE files at once (the three Saiyu
  Warriors Perfects), so `grep -rn '<the id>' Tests` for every orphan in the band as well.
- **PHASE E: A JUNK FLOOR CAN BE UNCITED, AND THEN THE COMMENT MUST SAY THE WORD FLAVOUR.** Every
  floor US-157..US-161 authored was on its Champion's own Wikimon `Evolves To`; US-162's two are
  not, because none of `commandramon`'s or `adventure02`'s Champions cites a junk Perfect at all.
  `RosterTests`' alias list and `EvolutionCriteriaTests.junkIds` move either way.
- **`penc-sw` IS THE ONLY LINE WHERE EVERY NODE'S COMMENT MUST NAME ITS DEVICE** ("Saiyu Warriors").
  Three files enforce it — `ChildSweepAToFTests`, `BabyIISweepTests`, `DigitamaSweepBabyITests` —
  and the rule is invisible from the node you are writing.
- **PHASE E: A JUNK FLOOR IS PER-LINE, NOT PER-CHAMPION, AND A FLOOR THAT ALREADY CLIMBS IS THE
  ONLY FREE ONE.** US-161 opened `vital` with ten leaf Champions and bought ONE alias
  (`vital_darumamon`) that served every one of them — do not multiply the alias cost by the number
  of leaf parents when pricing a rung. Among floors that already exist, prefer one with an
  out-edge: `locomon` (-> GrandLocomon) cost `penc-me` nothing, while CatchMamemon and Karakurumon
  are terminal and each adds a dead end to `ChildSweepAToFTests`' ledger. Check `junkIds` in
  `EvolutionCriteriaTests` and the candidate's own `evolutions` before choosing.
- **PHASE E: WRITE A SWEEP TEST'S `intersection`/`subtracting` LEDGERS FROM THE FINISHED TABLES,
  LAST.** Every sweep since US-157 carries a pair of lines partitioning "authored by me" from
  "already there". US-161's was written from the plan (two pre-existing floors) and not re-counted
  after a third was chosen during authoring — the only failure in 2322 tests. When a sweep's own
  new test fails on a set-difference of its own tables, suspect the TABLE, not `evolutions.json`.
- **PHASE E: THE JUNK-FLAVOURED SHEETS RAN OUT AT US-160 — A NEW JUNK FLOOR IS NOW A LINE-SCOPED
  ALIAS AND REMOVES NO ORPHAN.** US-148/151/157 each spent an unused gag sheet (Numemon X,
  CatchMamemon, Karakurumon, Pandamon); by US-160 not one of the 58 Perfect still orphaned was a
  gag Digimon, so `diablomon`'s floor draws the Gerbemon sheet under `diablomon_gerbemon`, the
  `dmcv2_vademon` pattern. Price the consequences BEFORE authoring: no orphan removed, `RosterTests`'
  alias list moves, and `EvolutionCriteriaTests.junkIds` gains a scoped name. The five lines still
  without a Perfect rung — `xros`, `vital`, `adventure02`, `algomon`, `commandramon` — all pay this.
- **PHASE E: THE VARIANT RULE HAS A STRONGER FORM — SAME PARENT, NOT JUST SAME LINE — AND AT THE
  PERFECT RUNG IT IS USUALLY FREE.** Six of US-160's nine variants hang off the very Champion their
  base form hangs off, which costs no argument and makes the climb the base form's own Mega for
  nothing. **Read `graph.parents(of: base)` BEFORE the variant's own `Evolves From`.** The limit:
  a base form's line can hold the cited CLIMB and no cited PARENT (MetalMamemon on `dmc-v2`), and
  then the variant follows a cited parent elsewhere — `ChildSweepMToZTests.
  testEveryVariantSitsWithItsBaseFormOrFollowsACitedParent`'s escape hatch. Check BOTH ends.
- **PHASE E: WIKIMON'S X-ANTIBODY PAGE TITLES ARE SPACED, AND THE UNSPACED GUESS RETURNS AN EMPTY
  BODY RATHER THAN A REDIRECT.** `MegaSeadramon (X-Antibody)` is 0 bytes; `Mega Seadramon
  (X-Antibody)` is the page. Same for Megalo Growmon, Metal Greymon (Virus), Metal Mamemon, Metal
  Tyranomon. Treat a zero-length body as "try the other spacing", never as "no page" — plain forms
  redirect, parenthesised ones do not.
- **PHASE E: AN EARLIER SWEEP'S `evolutions.count == 2` CLAIM BREAKS THE MOMENT YOU BRANCH THAT
  CHAMPION AGAIN, AND SO DOES ITS `authoredUltimates` PARENT SET.** US-160 broke three of the first
  (Gaogamon, ShimaUnimon, its own Meicoomon) and two of the second (ChaosDukemon, AncientVolcamon).
  Fix with a NAMED exception (`parent == "gaogamon" ? 3 : 2`) or a named extra parent, never by
  loosening to `>=` or to a superset. Add `grep -n "evolutions.count, 2" Tests` and
  `grep -n authoredUltimates Tests` to the pre-flight list beside `inLine.count` and `sweepEggs`.
- **PHASE E: A BOLDED PARENT IS WORTH SPENDING ON THE CLAIMANT WHOSE ALTERNATIVES COST A WHOLE
  RUNG.** US-160 gave `tamers`' last leaf Growmon to Manticoremon rather than to its own bolded
  child MegaloGrowmon Orange: the Orange form was pinned to Growmon (Orange) by the variant rule
  anyway, and every other reading of Manticoremon opened a Perfect rung, a junk floor and a Mega on
  a line that had none. One leaf bought two nodes and Dukemon with it. Say so in the node comment.
- **PHASE E: A BOLDED PARENT CAN BE UNDRAWABLE FOR A REASON OF SHAPE, NOT OF ART — CHECK ITS STAGE.**
  Lucemon Falldown's sole bolded `Evolves From` is Lucemon, a CHILD, and
  `GraphValidationError.invalidStageTransition` refuses a Child -> Perfect edge. Every earlier
  "cannot" in this series was dexOnly art or a missing sheet. Price the STAGE of a bolded parent
  before pricing anything else, and when the canonical arrow is illegal say so in the node comment —
  US-159's tests grep for it.
- **PHASE E: WHEN A RANGE HOLDS A BASE FORM AND ITS X, SOLVE THE X FIRST — ITS ONE POSSIBLE PARENT
  DECIDES BOTH LINES.** LadyDevimon has forty cited parents across nine lines; LadyDevimon X has
  exactly one usable one anywhere (Numemon X, `tamers`), because its bolded parent is the base form
  itself — a Perfect, never an in-edge. Choosing the base form's line off its OWN citations would
  have split the pair and broken the variant rule.
- **PHASE E: A JUNK CHAMPION IS A LEGAL PARENT FOR AN EARNED BRANCH, AND SOMETIMES THE ONLY ONE.**
  Numemon X, Raremon and Scumon all carry one. Prove it in BOTH directions through the engine — the
  earned branch for a raised Digimon, the junk fall for a neglected one — rather than reasoning about
  it. Watch the knock-on: a Child whose ONLY onward edge is the junk fall (Terriermon) then reaches a
  Mega only by being neglected, which moves `EggHatchingTests`.
- **PHASE E, PERFECT RUNG AND ABOVE: the cheapest in-edge is one that ALSO clears a dead end, and
  every leaf you branch costs a junk-floor edge in the same breath.** A Champion sweep only ever
  added leaves; a Perfect sweep removes them, because a Perfect needs a Champion beneath it and after
  six Adult sweeps most Champions are leaves. US-157 cleared nine and the ledger in
  `ChildSweepAToFTests` fell for the first time in Phase E (105 -> 97). The catch:
  `EvolutionCriteriaTests` fails any branching Champion with no `isDefault` edge onto a junk Perfect
  of its OWN line, so the fallback has to be written in the same edit as the earned branch.
- **A PERFECT'S CLIMB IS A SINGLE `isDefault` EDGE — `minEnergy` 150, `maxCareMistakes` 2, NO
  conditions — and that is legal because `EvolutionCriteriaTests.branchingNodes` filters to Child and
  Adult.** The 2..5 ceiling and the junk-floor rule do not reach this rung. The AC's "no edge is
  unconditional" binds the EARNED edges; a condition on an `isDefault` edge is data that lies,
  because US-020 takes it whatever the gates say.
- **`Roster.bundled` reads `Resources/roster.json` (one entry per SHEET); Appendix B reads
  `roster.generated.json` (which mirrors `evolutions.json`, aliases and all).** A range test written
  off `roster.entries` will disagree with the orphan count by exactly the number of line-scoped
  aliases in the band — three in A-C. Both numbers are right; say which is which in the test.
- **Opening a line's TOP rung promotes its eggs.** `MainScreenModel.startingDigitamaId` filters on
  `graph.reachesUltimate`, so US-157's first four `tamers` Ultimates turned five Digitama from
  unraisable into legal starting eggs and moved BOTH lists in `EggHatchingTests`. `wanyamon` is the
  last line with Perfects and no Mega — expect the same there.
- **A DEMO FLAG THAT PUSHES A SCREEN MUST ALSO SEED IT — ONE FLAG, NOT TWO (US-213).** `simctl`
  cannot tap, so every screen behind a grid button is photographed by a `-xxxDemo` flag that pushes it
  onto `ContentView`'s stack. If the screen's CONTENT comes from a separate seed
  (`MainScreenModel.seed...IfRequested`), add the new flag to that seed's guard rather than expecting
  the two to be passed together: a push flag alone photographs an empty screen and reads like the
  feature is broken. `-sleepTimeDemo` pushes AND banks the 6 hours `-sleepBarDemo` banks.
- **Deleting a view means grepping its NAME through comments, not just its call sites (US-213).**
  Nothing warns about a doc comment pointing at a deleted type. `MainReadingBars`/`MainReadingBarLayout`
  were cited by five comments in four other files. Repoint them at whatever the deleted type itself
  cited — a chain of reasons is worth keeping unbroken.
- **Author a multi-node edit with a script, after proving the JSON round-trips.**
  `json.dumps(d, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False)` reproduces `evolutions.json`, `elements.json` and
  `moves.json` byte-for-byte (no trailing newline). US-157 added 29 nodes across three files that
  way; see `scripts/us157_author.py`. And check `moves.json` `signatureName` against the WHOLE file —
  it is unique globally while `projectileSymbol|tint` is unique only per line, and a variant naturally
  wants to reuse its base form's attack name.
- **PHASE E: a "no sheet for this name" claim from an EARLIER story can be a SPELLING miss — check
  the roster before inheriting it.** `DMCVersion1TreeTests` recorded since US-133 that the Version 1
  document's Tyranomon had "no colour sheet at all, only `Black and White Sprites/Adult/
  Tyranomon.png`". The pack writes the colour sheet with TWO n's — `Adult/Tyrannomon.png`, roster id
  `tyrannomon`, playable — so an arrow the seed tree called undrawable had been drawable the whole
  time, and US-155 drew it. Wikimon's spelling and the sprite pack's differ often enough (Tyranomon/
  Tyrannomon, Ex-Tyranomon/extyranomon) that "no entry for `<wikimon spelling>`" proves nothing.
  Resolve a name through `roster.entries` by DISPLAY NAME normalised, never by guessing the id.
- **PHASE E: "this parent is FULL" IS A CLAIM ABOUT ENERGIES, AND IT CAN BE OFF BY ONE — RE-COUNT
  THE EARNED BRANCHES BEFORE INHERITING IT.** US-153 wrote that Gammamon was full and handed
  WezenGammamon a Gabumon stand-in; US-154 and US-155 both passed that advice on unchecked, and it
  was wrong for three stories. Gammamon carried BetelGammamon (spirit), GulusGammamon (strength) and
  KausGammamon (stamina) plus a junk edge to Turuiemon that SHARES spirit with the first — so
  `Set(node.evolutions.compactMap(\.requiredEnergy)).count` read 3-of-4-looking-closed while the
  count that actually matters, `evolutions.filter { !$0.isDefault }.count`, was 3 with vitality free.
  **Count EARNED branches against `EnergyType.allCases`, never distinct energies over ALL edges** —
  the junk fallback is allowed to share, which is exactly what makes the two counts disagree. US-156
  drew the bolded arrow it was told was impossible and left Gabumon its energy. Same shape as
  US-155's Tyranomon spelling: an inherited "cannot" is worth ten minutes of checking.

- **PHASE E ADULT SWEEPS: the four-Rookie ceiling is reached from BELOW, and a sweep can spend three
  of them at once.** US-155 filled Agumon, Bakumon and Muchomon — each took its LAST free energy —
  because the cheap placements all hung off Rookies that already had three earned branches. That is
  the normal shape late in the rung, not a warning sign: a Child with one energy left is exactly the
  Child whose line already holds both ends. But it closes the node for good, so say which Rookies a
  story filled in a test (`testTheThreeRookiesThisStoryFilledHaveAnEnergyForEveryEarnedBranch`) and
  expect the knock-on to reach the SEED tests — `SeedRosterTests`, `EnergyBarsTests`,
  `DexScreenTests`, `ConditionRevealTests` and `EvolutionTreeTests` all pin Agumon's branch list.
- **PHASE E: the `SeedRosterTests` per-line "verified-available set" is APPENDED to, never widened.**
  `patamonLineVerifiedSet` and `piyomonLineVerifiedSet` are closed lists of display names that every
  Adult-and-up node on `dmc-v3`/`dmc-v4` must be in. US-148 through US-151 each added their names
  with a comment saying which sweep and why; US-155 did the same. Do not relax the containment
  check — the list IS the record of which sheets were eyeballed.
- **PHASE E: grep the WHOLE tree markdown before spending an orphan on an invented junk node.** A
  later device section may draw it as an earned branch (US-140 lost WaruMonzaemon to US-142's V5
  section this way). The same grep is what the story's own "this name is not in the document" test
  does — write it before authoring, not after.
- **PHASE E: a missing rung is a REHOME, not a dropped thread — including a missing MIDDLE one.**
  Fetch the Wikimon page for the rung above the gap and the rung below it and intersect their
  Evolves From / Evolves To lists; a stand-in that appears in both sits on the same thread the
  document draws. US-140 did this for a missing bottom, US-141 for a missing middle (Deramon ->
  Blossomon) and a missing top (Crossmon -> Rafflesimon). Cite the page in the node `comment` — a
  test greps for "Wikimon".
- **PHASE E: two of a document's names can be ONE Digimon.** The V0 section draws HolyAngemon over
  Angemon and MagnaAngemon over Wizardmon; they are the same Digimon under a JP and a dub name,
  with one sheet between them, so US-143 wired one node with two parents and two children rather
  than inventing a second id on the same art. Do not diff the bullet list by eye — sweep every
  `*mon` word out of the section's own text and assert each resolves to a playable roster entry,
  under its own spelling or a recorded substitution. That sweep is what turns "a name is missing"
  into "a name is a duplicate", and it is a test, not a one-off grep.
- **PHASE E: `elements.json` and `moves.json` need a `lineDefaults` entry for a NEW LINE**, not
  only the per-id rows — `ElementCatalogTests.testEveryGraphLineHasALineDefault` and its moves
  twin. Missed by US-143's first pass; it is a ninth place on the knock-on list, and it only
  applies when the story opens a line rather than adding to one.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: a sweep authors ONE RUNG, so two invariants the device trees had are gone.**
  US-144 broke both on purpose and pinned each as a claim rather than letting it rot:
  (a) **a line may have SEVERAL Digitama** — an alternate egg hangs off the line whose species it
  belongs to rather than opening a one-node line, so `dmc-v2` has three eggs; the "one egg per
  line" assertion in ALL SIX tree-test files became a pinned egg LIST, and every
  `...IsReachableFromItsDigitama` seeds its BFS from every egg of the line.
  (b) **a node below Ultimate may be a dead end** — the Baby I an egg hatches into has to exist
  before the Baby II above it does. The replacement for "zero dead ends" is a LEDGER
  (`DigitamaSweepTests.testTheOnlyDeadEndsBelowUltimateAreTheOnesThisSweepOpened`) that fails in
  BOTH directions: a ninth dead end fails it, and so does wiring one of the eight onward. The next
  sweep is meant to edit that list down and is told to rather than having to notice.
- **PHASE E ADULT SWEEPS: intersect the orphan's Wikimon `Evolves From` AND `Evolves To` against the
  graph BEFORE choosing its line.** Choosing the line off the parent alone is what forces a new
  Perfect rung later; choosing it off both ends at once is why US-152 wired five Champions for five
  nodes while US-151 needed eleven for seven. Seven lines still owe a Perfect rung, so the saving is
  real every time it lands.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: intersect the story's OWN orphans' `Evolves To` lists WITH EACH OTHER before
  opening a rung above.** When every cited target of a range is a sheet with no node — which is the
  normal case for the `tamers` X-Antibody thread — the orphan-by-orphan intersection against the
  graph finds nothing and the rung above HAS to open. US-154 paid two nodes for four Champions
  instead of four, because Grademon is in both Meramon X's and Pegasmon X's `Evolves To` (Digital
  Monster X Ver.3) and Mametyramon is Bx-43, the card that fuses Monochromon X and Pteranomon X.
  And a line that ALREADY has a junk Perfect makes each new one cost ONE node, not the two US-151
  paid: no floor, and `EvolutionCriteriaTests.junkIds` does not move.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: an energy shared with the JUNK fallback is legal; one shared with another EARNED
  branch is not.** US-154's Musyamon took the only energy Pico Devimon had left, strength, which its
  junk edge to Gokimon is also gated on. That is the Scumon arrangement US-133 recorded — the earned
  edge asks 60 and the junk one 0, so each wins exactly when it should. Prove it through the engine
  in both directions rather than reasoning about it; `AdultSweepMToRTests.testMusyamonSharesStrength
  WithPicoDevimonsJunkEdgeAndStillWins` is the shape.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: `testEveryNodeInTheLineIsReachableFromItsDigitama` CARRIES ITS OWN
  `inLine.count`, and it is NOT the `sweepEggs` test.** Four device-tree files failed on this second,
  separate count after US-154's data landed. `grep -n 'inLine.count' Tests` alongside
  `grep -n sweepEggs Tests` — the knock-on list needs both.
- **PHASE E: derive a handover's RANGE from the roster, not from the letter band you remember.**
  US-153 handed WezenGammamon to US-154 as an "M-R orphan"; its display name starts with W, so it is
  US-156's. The advice attached to it was still right and still needed — re-pin it in the new story
  rather than letting it fall between two ranges.
- **PHASE E ADULT SWEEPS: when TWO lines are both cited, the tiebreak is which one already has the
  rung above.** US-153's Kinkakumon had a Saiyu Warriors reading (Fujamon/Takinmon, `penc-sw`) and a
  Vital Bracelet BE one (Jellymon -> Zudomon, `penc-ds`); both are real citations, the first is the
  better theme, and the second cost two fewer nodes because `penc-sw` still has no Perfect rung.
  Take the cheap one, but write the rejected reading into the node `comment` AND pin both halves as
  a test ("the `penc-sw` Children still do not reach it" + "`penc-sw` still has no Perfect"), so the
  story that opens that rung is told Kinkakumon is a rehome candidate instead of having to notice.
- **PHASE E: a Child is FULL at three earned branches plus the junk fallback**, because
  `EvolutionEngine` picks on dominant energy first and there are four energy types. US-153 took
  Gammamon to the ceiling (spirit/strength/stamina + junk). When a sweep fills a Child, say so in a
  test rather than in a comment — the next sweep needs another parent, not a fourth branch, and
  `ChildSweepGToLTests`' `branchedByALaterSweep` entry for it can never move again.
- **PHASE E: when the BOLDED Wikimon parent is `dexOnly`, read further down the SAME Evolves From
  before calling the rung unwireable.** `edgeToDexOnlyNode` forbids the edge, but the next cited
  parent is usually already on a line the file holds - US-152's Gawappamon took Gomamon three
  bullets below the idle-only Kamemon and kept its citation, where US-151's Burgamon had to be
  rehomed on a line argument because every one of its parents was unusable.
- **PHASE E: a handover claim written as a test FLIPS when the next story honours it; it does not
  die.** US-151 asserted `graph.node(id: "flarelizamon") == nil` to hand FlareLizamon to US-152.
  US-152 wired it and rewrote the same test as MegaloGrowmon's exact parent set. Same fact, other
  side, still fails on a parent nobody wrote down. Leave the next sweep a claim of that shape.
- **PHASE E: `Set(graph.parents(of:))` EQUALITY is the assertion an Adult sweep breaks.** Three exist
  - HolyAngemon (two -> three -> four parents over US-143/151/152), Andromon in
  `PendulumMetalEmpireTreeTests`, MegaloGrowmon in `AdultSweepAToDTests`. Fix by NAMING the new
  parent and which arrow it is, never by loosening to a superset. `grep -rn 'Set(graph.parents'
  Tests` before choosing an out-edge target.
- **PHASE E: a device tree's closing "the N orphans this story removed" test has a `sweepEggs`
  escape hatch, and that - not the count - is where a later story's node goes.** It keeps the tree's
  claim about its OWN nodes true. Every device line touched by a sweep wants an entry.
- **PHASE E ADULT SWEEPS: an Adult's out-edge must land on a Perfect of its OWN line, and NINE
  lines have no Perfect rung at all.** `testNoEdgeCrossesALine` plus a per-line boundary test in
  every device-tree file make a cross-line edge impossible, and `EvolutionCriteriaTests` demands a
  junk fallback drawn from `junkIds` - so opening a line's Perfect rung costs TWO nodes, the earned
  branch and the junk floor under it, and the floor has to be added to `junkIds`. US-151 opened
  `wanyamon` and `tamers`; `xros`, `vital`, `adventure02`, `algomon`, `commandramon`, `diablomon`
  and `penc-sw` are still owed one. This is the same problem US-148/US-149 solved one rung down.
- **`Roster.bundled` is `Resources/roster.json` (1,022 entries); `roster.generated.json` (1,025) is
  the Appendix B mirror and carries three line-scoped aliases the shipped file does not.** Count a
  story's RANGE off the shipped roster when the number goes into a test, and its ORPHAN COUNT off
  the generated one. They disagree, and US-151 wrote 46 where the test wanted 41.
- **Fetch Wikimon as wikitext, never as a summarised page:**
  `curl -s "https://wikimon.net/index.php?title=<Page>&action=raw"`. The rendered-page fetch drops
  and invents Evolves From / Evolves To entries. Redirects come back as `#REDIRECT [[Real Page]]`.
- **A rung can be UNWIREABLE rather than missing, and then the argument is "which line already holds
  this family".** All three of Burgamon Adult's Wikimon parents are idle-only or absent, and
  `edgeToDexOnlyNode` forbids an edge to an idle-only Digimon, so no stand-in intersection existed.
  US-151 put both Burgermon on `dmc-v4` because Torikara Ballmon - whose only canon relatives are
  those two - is already a Baby II there and Digitamamon, a cited Evolves To, is its Perfect.
- **A class-level Wikimon citation ("Any Blue Lv.3 Digimon from the DCG") is a real citation and is
  checkable.** Deckerdramon has nothing else; its out-edge takes the "also Evolves from Cyborg
  Lv.4" clause onto Andromon, which this line really does reach from Guardromon, and the test
  asserts that parent edge. Say in the `comment` which half is cited and which is flavour.
- **The shared `met` "did everything right" context CANNOT take an `atMost` edge.** Copy
  `AdultSweepAToDTests.context(for:)`, which derives the context from the edge's own conditions,
  rather than loosening a criterion to fit the fixture.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: THE DIGITAMA ARE SPENT AS OF US-145 — all 57 carry their one hatch edge.** A
  Baby I's only possible in-edge is an egg, so **13 playable Baby I can never be reached** and no
  later story can author that away. The count and the "no unspent egg" half are pinned by
  `DigitamaSweepLToZTests.testTheBabyIStillOrphanedCannotBeReachedByAnyRemainingEgg`. Read it
  before promising an in-edge at Baby I.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: 45 free Digitama and 33 free Baby I is the allocation the whole phase rests on.**
  `EggHatcher.hatchTarget` reads `node.evolutions.first`, so an egg has exactly ONE hatch edge and a
  later story CANNOT give a new Baby I an in-edge by adding a second edge to an already-spent egg.
  So an egg either pairs 1:1 with a Baby I it opens, or doubles up onto an existing one — and
  US-144/US-145 between them decide, for good, which Baby I ever get an in-edge. US-144 spent 22
  eggs: 12 doubled up (their species was already wired, or is dexOnly/absent so no thread could
  reach it), 10 opened a Baby I. That leaves US-145 23 eggs for 25 still-orphaned Baby I, so
  **US-145 must double up as little as it can** or some Baby I can never be reached.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: THE GLOBAL REACHABILITY TEST LIVES IN `EvolutionCriteriaTests`, not in
  `EvolutionGraphTests`, and every device line has its OWN twin.** `testEveryNonEggNodeIsReachable
  FromSomeDigitama` was a global zero from US-008 until US-146; each of the six `Pendulum*TreeTests`
  and five `DMC*TreeTests` also asserts "every node on this line is reachable from one of its eggs".
  So a node with no in-edge breaks the test of WHATEVER LINE you put it on. Grep for both BEFORE
  choosing a line, and when a node genuinely cannot be reached, pin it by NAME rather than relaxing
  the check — US-146 turned the global one into a 21-name list that still fails on a 22nd, and
  proved separately that each stranded Baby II has no reachable parent so the list cannot absorb a
  node nobody bothered to wire.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: A BABY II'S ONLY POSSIBLE PARENT IS A BABY I, AND A CHILD'S IS A BABY II.**
  US-147 spent the "every Baby I has exactly one edge" invariant to give twelve parentless Baby II
  an in-edge: nine Baby I gained a conditional second edge beside their unconditional fallback.
  The same move is the only one available at every rung above, so expect to branch the rung below
  and to edit the newest sweep's "who branches, and for which orphan" test rather than adding a
  branch quietly. An in-edge also FORCES THE LINE — `testNoEdgeCrossesALine` — so the parent, not
  flavour, is what decides where a sweep node lives.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: an egg's promise is a BFS, and it is worth running before you author.**
  US-144/145 hung 57 eggs on threads; a thread that never arrives at the egg's own species is a
  promise the file does not keep, and `BabyIISweepTests.testTheEggsWhoseSpeciesThisRungReachesNowArriveAtIt`
  caught exactly that on `lala_digitama`. Decide which parent gets a Child by asking which egg is
  owed it.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: a rung's scope is the RUNG, not the names still orphaned when you start.** A
  sweep AC asks for an in-edge AND an out-edge; an earlier sweep may have met only one of them for
  most of the range. US-144/US-145 de-orphaned 25 Baby I with in-edges alone, so US-146's real job
  was 33 out-edges, not 13 nodes. Check which criterion the earlier story met before scoping.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: fetch the Wikimon page of a Digimon that is NOT on disk.** Wikimon has pages
  the sprite pack lacks, so `curl wikimon.net/Gurimon` still gives "Evolves To: Koemon" — and the
  stand-in is whichever rung ON DISK shares that target. One sweep of ~37 `curl`s over every orphan
  at the stage above, parsed for `Evolves_From`/`Evolves_To`, answers every pairing question in a
  sweep at once and is reusable by the next one. Beware: an `Evolves To` at Baby I can be a DigiXros
  FUSION list and not an evolution at all (Bombmon's is), in which case say FLAVOUR in the comment
  and let a test grep for the word.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: the graph has more nodes at a rung than the roster has playable Digimon.**
  `graph.nodes(at: .babyI)` is 45; `roster.entries` playable Baby I is 43 — `piyo_yuramon` and
  `pencnsp_botamon` are line-scoped aliases with no roster entry. Assert a rung's SHAPE over graph
  nodes and its COVERAGE over roster entries; iterating roster entries silently skips every alias.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: the eleven-file knock-on list for a rung-sized story.** Node count in BOTH
  `ElementCatalogTests` and `EvolutionGraphValidatorTests`; line sizes in `EvolutionGraphTests`;
  the game -> [lines] literal in `MinigameAssignmentTests`; `MoveCatalogTests` wants a unique
  symbol|tint WITHIN a line and a globally unique `signatureName`;
  `ElementCatalogTests.testElementsVaryWithinALine` forbids a single-element line, which any 2-node
  line trips; and `EggHatchingTests`' two starting-egg lists move whenever a thread newly reaches an
  Ultimate. Plus `lineDefaults` in elements.json AND moves.json, `DexModel.lineTitles` and
  `MinigameAssignment.byLine` for each new line.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: a new game must not start on an unfinished thread.**
  `MainScreenModel.startingDigitamaId` filters candidates through
  `EvolutionGraph.reachesUltimate(from:)` (US-144). Without it a fresh install could land on
  `guil_digitama`, hatch Jyarimon and stop there. A sweep that opens a thread does NOT need to do
  anything for this; it is automatic. But a sweep that FINISHES one silently adds a starting egg,
  and `EggHatchingTests.testTheDefaultChooserPicksARandomDigitama` pins both halves of the split.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: Wikimon two hops down is how you find a species' Baby I.** Fetch the CHILD's
  page, read `Evolves From` for its Baby II, then that Baby II's `Evolves From`. Better still,
  fetch every free Baby I and read its `Evolves To` once — 33 curl calls gave US-144 the whole
  Baby I -> Baby II map in two minutes, and US-146/US-147 can reuse the same sweep. **`curl` works
  and Python's `urllib` HANGS** in this sandbox; shell out. The parse is
  `re.split(r'<h2[^>]*>', html)` then `<span class="mw-headline" id="...">` for the section name.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: a dexOnly or ABSENT species cannot be given a thread, so its egg doubles up.**
  Betamon, Kamemon, Kudamon and Kudamon 2006 are idle-only; **Espimon has no sheet at all**, not
  even an idle frame. Their eggs went onto the device line whose In-Training Wikimon draws that
  species from (Betamon and Kamemon both from Pukamon -> `penc-ds`, Espimon from Caprimon ->
  `penc-me`). Where even that is absent, say so in the comment and call it a flavour choice rather
  than dressing it as a citation — `kuda_digitama`'s comment does exactly that.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: `roster.generated.json` HAS THE LINE-SCOPED ALIASES IN IT AND
  `Roster.bundled.entries` DOES NOT.** Scope a rung's ORPHAN count off the generated file (it
  mirrors the graph, which is what Appendix B needs) and a story's RANGE off `Roster.bundled`, or
  the range over-counts by every alias — US-149 read 45 G-L Children where the test saw 43.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: a device tree pins its own In-Training's branch LIST and edge COUNT.** Hanging
  one more Child off a device-tree Baby II breaks tests that have nothing to do with counts or
  lines: US-149 tripped `SeedRosterTests`' Pagumon target list and Nightmare Soldiers' "the
  In-Training rung is unconditioned" claim, which a sweep's earned branch necessarily violates.
  `grep -rn '<parent-id>' Tests` BEFORE choosing that parent. The fix for the second kind is to
  scope the tree's claim to the edges the TREE draws, not to relax it.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: the "every Champion of this line falls to the junk Perfect" loop needs
  `&& !$0.evolutions.isEmpty` in every device-tree file a sweep touches** — US-148 fixed Nightmare
  Soldiers, US-149 Virus Busters and Metal Empire. Wind Guardians and Deep Savers still carry the
  unguarded version and fail the moment a sweep puts an Adult on them.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: check `EvolutionCriteriaTests`' stranded lists BEFORE choosing a parent, not
  after.** US-149 moved Gammamon from Pusurimon (stranded) to Hiyarimon — same line, equally free,
  reachable — and kept two nodes off the list for nothing. Where every Baby II of a line is stranded
  (`xros`, `penc-sw`: no Digitama, and all 57 eggs were spent in US-144/145) the arithmetic is
  inherited and the honest move is to add to the list with the parent that explains it.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: the four-energy ceiling decides where a VARIANT lives, but "its base form's
  LINE" is far easier to satisfy than "its base form's PARENT".** Check the line for a SECOND
  In-Training before rehoming — US-149's Kokuwamon X kept `penc-me` through Kozenimon when Caprimon
  was full, while Gomamon X could not, because `penc-ds` has exactly one Baby II in the whole line.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: a historical claim stops being checkable once a later story writes to the same
  file.** `ChildSweepAToFTests`' "this line had no Champion before" was checked as "every Adult here
  is one US-148 authored"; US-149 added sixteen to `tamers` alone. Replace such an assertion with
  the half that stays true and say why in the comment — do not delete it, and do not let it rot.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: `care.battleCount` is answerable ONLY over the `lifetime` window; every other
  `care.*` counter ONLY over `stage`.** `ConditionContext.careValue` hands back `.unknown` for
  `(.careBattleCount, .stage)`, so such an edge is UNREACHABLE rather than merely hard — and the
  validator has no opinion about windows, so only the engine tests catch it. US-150 shipped four of
  them into a first draft; `ChildSweepMToZTests.testNoBattleCriterionAsksForAWindowTheContextCannot
  Answer` now pins the rule over `evolutions.json`. It does NOT cover `maps.json`, where US-128
  recorded the same trap in 12 Digitama slots and left it alone on purpose — that is a data story,
  and this pattern is why it is worth doing.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: re-run the egg BFS when a sweep WIRES a species an earlier egg doubled up for.**
  US-145 parked three eggs on someone else's Baby I because their own species had no node. US-150
  gave all three a node and let that decide one placement — Phascomon went to its CITED line's
  second In-Training rather than to a free one on flavour — so every one of the three now arrives.
  `DigitamaSweepLToZTests`' "the species is still unwired" guards exist to make you notice.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: prefer a SECOND CITATION over a rehome when the first-choice parent is full.**
  US-149's Gomamon X had to be rehomed by flavour; US-150's Shakomon X hit the identical trap
  (`penc-ds` has one In-Training and it is full) and instead followed the other parent Wikimon
  names for it. A citation is checkable in a test; a rehome is only a comment.
- **PHASE E: a substring search misses a letter INSIDE a name.** `Jureimon` is not a substring of
  `Jyureimon`, so the document's own bracketed spelling does not find its own sheet. Search a
  PREFIX, not the whole name, before calling anything absent.
- **PHASE E: a document name with no `find -iname` hit is usually a DUB name, not an absent
  Digimon.** Try the Japanese one: Mammothmon/`Mammon`, Wizardmon/`Wizarmon`, Pumpkinmon/`Pumpmon`,
  Piedmon/`Piemon`, Myotismon/`Vamdemon`, Candlemon/`Candmon`, Apemon/`Hanumon`. Also check the
  roster by SUBSTRING and read every hit's `dexOnly` — a playable twin can hide behind an
  idle-only one under the document's own spelling (Octomon/`Octmon`).
- **`care.battleWinRatio` must not gate a CHILD's earned edge.** The shared reachability fixture
  (`ConditionContext` with `battlesLifetime:`) cannot express a win ratio, so the branch is
  unreachable in tests. Fine at Adult, where nothing walks it.
- SIMULATOR SCREENSHOTS: `export DEVELOPER_DIR=/Applications/Xcode_26_4_1.app/Contents/Developer`,
  build once against Series 11 (46mm, watchOS 26.4), then `simctl install` the SAME .app onto the
  41mm Series 9 (watchOS 10.4) — deployment target is 10.0 and Series 9 is not a usable
  `xcodebuild -destination`. Sim UDIDs: 46mm BA425DD4-8856-4933-8198-0E4B89960E48,
  41mm FB045EDB-DEB9-40AA-B8FB-819E9E742517.
- Launch flags for a screenshot: `-healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt` plus the demo flag. If a
  notification alert is already queued it SURVIVES terminate+uninstall and eats every shot;
  `simctl erase` on the device is the only fix (then `-healthAnswered` is required or you land on
  onboarding). Cost 10 minutes again this iteration.
- To photograph a pre-story build for a before/after: `git stash push -u`, rebuild, copy the .app
  out of DerivedData FIRST (both builds land on the same path), then `git stash pop`.
- MEASURE screenshots, do not eyeball them. Throwaway CoreGraphics tools compiled with
  `xcrun swiftc` are the pattern (see US-114's /tmp/us114/measure.swift, peak.swift — not
  committed, they hard-code this screen's bands). Two that keep earning their keep:
  a "lit in EVERY frame vs lit in ANY frame" pass over a burst separates static chrome from the
  moving sprite, and a peak/mean-luma pass over a band proves a dim is exactly `dimOpacity`.
- The scrim is invisible over a black background, so it cannot be measured directly. Measure what
  it DIMS instead: the sprite's peak luma with the light on vs off.
- NEVER diff a single screenshot per build when the sprite is in shot. The walk1/walk2 alternation
  is driven by a TimelineView that runs whether or not the sprite translates, so two shots taken
  seconds apart routinely catch opposite frames and read as a large bogus diff. Take a BURST of ~6
  per configuration, compare every pair, and use the pair that agrees — a matched pair goes to 100%
  byte identity while a mismatched one sticks at the ~50% the two poses share.
- Demo flags that write to the SAVE persist across launches, and several have no inverse
  (`-lightOffDemo` has no `-lightOnDemo`). Order the screenshot pass so the default state is
  photographed FIRST, or `simctl erase` between runs — a poisoned shot still looks plausible.
- To prove a constant (an opacity, a scale) is really what the screen paints: render the source
  asset yourself with the same layout math into the measured slot over black, then divide the
  Simulator's band by it. Turns "it looks about right" into a number.
- **THE MAIN SCREEN'S VERTICAL BUDGET IS NOW SPENT — genuinely, as of US-120.** `SpriteScale.fitting`
  floors `slotHeight / 16`, and on a hatched Child the slot lands at **49.5pt on 41mm** (a 48pt
  Digimon, **0.5pt of slack**) and **64.0pt on 46mm** (a 64pt Digimon, **0.0pt of slack**).
  **Any row added to `ContentView`'s VStack costs the Digimon a whole scale step, however thin** —
  US-120 measured a 13.5pt row taking 48 -> 32pt and 64 -> 48pt before it paid for itself. Measure
  the slot BEFORE designing a row. What is left to pay with, in order of preference:
  - **Nothing cheap.** US-120 already spent the five 1pt VStack gaps, `ActionControls`' 2pt top
    padding, the energy bars' row spacing, and took the name line and the stats values to 9pt.
    `MainScreenTypography` holds those two sizes and a test fails if they grow.
  - The bottom safe area — 26pt on 41mm, 36pt on 46mm, real and unused, verified with an
    `.ignoresSafeArea(.container, edges: .bottom)` probe — but spending it puts the action row's
    outer circles inside the display's corner arc, which is what the inset is for.
  - The top band holds the clock and BOTH toolbar buttons (US-114's light, the Dex). Not reclaimable.
  - **Price a trade before declining it.** US-120's first iteration set the chrome trim aside as "a
    screen-wide legibility regression"; measured, half of it was pure whitespace costing nothing.
- To measure the sprite SLOT in one command: the map band under `-mapDemo=<asset>` IS the slot,
  exactly, so diff that shot against a `-mapDemo=none` one — **but only count a row as slot if
  >=75% of the WIDTH differs.** The map band is full width (344 of 352px on 41mm); `-mapDemo=none`
  also flips the map strip to its prompt state and nudges the name row, so a naive "differs at all"
  diff swallows those two text rows and over-reports the slot by ~23pt. To measure the sprite SCALE:
  a brand-new save is a Digitama whose sheet yields no frames, so `DigimonSpriteView.placeholder`
  draws a stroked box of exactly `16 x scale` points — a free ruler that needs no matched walk frame.
  On a HATCHED save use the sprite's ink WIDTH, not its height: height changes with the walk frame.
- **A demo flag's "inverse" is rarely a pure inverse** — `-mapDemo=none` undoes US-115's background
  AND changes US-120's strip. When a before/after rests on one flag, check what else that flag
  reaches, or the diff attributes every change to the thing you were testing.
- **Build a pre-story baseline in a `git worktree`, not a `git stash`.** The two builds land in
  different DerivedData directories, so there is no copy-the-app-out-first race and the working tree
  is never disturbed. `git worktree add /tmp/<name> <commit>`, then `git worktree remove --force`.
  A baseline that reproduces the previous iteration's published numbers is what makes a
  before/after worth anything — check that it does before trusting the "after".
- `xcodegen generate` is required for a NEW source file even though `project.yml` globs `Sources`.
  The symptom is "cannot find type 'X' in scope" on a file that plainly exists.
- **`Roster` and `EvolutionGraph` are DIFFERENT sets: 1025 entries vs 88 authored nodes.** Data
  authored against the roster (map opponent pools, Digitama slots) CANNOT be resolved through the
  graph — it silently comes back empty and the caller falls through to whatever its fallback is.
  US-122 shipped a whole story doing nothing for one build because of this. Until Phase E wires the
  780 orphans, anything meaning "any Digimon" goes through `Roster`. `EvolutionNode` is
  constructible from a `RosterEntry` with an empty `line`, and both `MoveCatalog` and
  `ElementCatalog` degrade gracefully through an empty line — that is the bridge (`MapOpponentBand.nodes`).
- **A test that asserts "something came back" cannot catch a silent fallback.** Assert that what
  came back is FROM the set you asked about. In US-122 that one line was the difference between a
  false pass and finding the bug.
- **Anything under `Tests/Fixtures/` is globbed into the test target — including files a TOOL leaves
  behind.** Even a read-only `sqlite3 ... "select ..."` on the committed `.store` creates `-wal` and
  `-shm` sidecars, and the next `xcodegen generate` bakes them in; the build then fails with
  `The file "pre-us123.store-shm" couldn't be opened`. Delete the sidecars AND re-run `xcodegen`.
- **`sqlite3` on a store is the way to check what a `@Model` change actually WROTE**, and it is what
  separates "the value read back" from "the value was persisted": a computed accessor with a `nil`
  default returns the same answer either way. `pragma table_info(ZGAMESTATE)` for the columns,
  `select` for the rows. Copy the fixture out first (see above).
- **An optional-backed storage property is the house pattern for adding a field to an
  already-shipped `@Model`**, and the reason belongs on the STORAGE property: SwiftData will not
  migrate a non-optional attribute into an existing store without a default — it opens, then the
  next save fails with "is a required value". Choose the `nil` reading in the direction that is SAFE
  for an old save, not merely convenient (US-124: `isActive` reads `nil` as ACTIVE, because the only
  record that can carry one is the single Digimon of a pre-box store).
- **A one-shot migration guarded by "does X exist yet" does not run for a player who already ran the
  build that created X.** US-124's `isActive` stamp lives inside `loadOrCreateProfile`, which
  returns early once there is a profile — so it needs the `nil`-default backstop as well. When
  adding a migration, ask which SHIPPED build the player is coming from, not just which schema.
- **NEVER chain a `GameStore` temporary into a `@Model` read in a test:
  `try GameStore(url: url).loadOrCreateProfile()` CRASHES the whole test host.** ARC releases the
  store the instant the call returns, a released store's `ModelContext` is reset, and the returned
  `PlayerProfile`/`GameState` is destroyed with it — the next assertion trips
  `SwiftData/BackingData.swift:835: Fatal error: This model instance was destroyed by calling
  ModelContext.reset`. Bind the store to a local first (`let store = try GameStore(url: url)`), and
  keep it alive for as long as anything it handed out is read. Cost a full test run in US-129.
- **A crashed test host makes `xcodebuild test` LIE about the total, and the lie looks like a pass.**
  It relaunches and the final summary counts only the tests since the relaunch — US-129 saw
  `Executed 962 tests, with 0 failures` from a suite of 1623, with `** TEST FAILED **` the only
  signal, and that came bundled with an unrelated `xcrun: error: unable to find utility "simctl"`
  from diagnostics collection. ALWAYS compare the summary against
  `grep -rcE '^\s+func test' Tests/*.swift`; if it is short, grep the log for `Fatal error` and
  `Restarting after unexpected exit`. A trailing `simctl` diagnostics error on its own is
  environmental and does NOT mean a test failed — read the Executed line.
- **When a story splits "the machinery" from "the data" (US-130/US-131 for Jogress, and every one of
  Phase E's authoring stories), the machinery story's "validator reports zero findings over the
  shipped file" test is VACUOUS — say so, and buy back what it cannot prove.** An empty
  `{"recipes": []}` exercises no field name, so a typo in a key survives the story and surfaces as a
  `fatalError` at launch in the next one (every `bundled` here traps by design). Two cheap fixes,
  both used in US-130: decode a LITERAL in the authored shape through the real `JSONDecoder`, and
  leave an explicit `...UntilUS1NN` marker test that FAILS the day the data lands, so the next
  iteration is told rather than having to notice.
- **A Digimon's RUNG comes from the sprite FOLDER, not from the source tree** — `import_roster.py`
  reads the stage off `16x16 Digimon Sprites/<Stage>/`, and a graph node whose `stage` disagrees
  resolves to no art and fails the validator's `missingSprite`. The device trees do NOT always
  agree: US-134's Whamon is a Champion in the Digital Monster V2 document and a `Perfect/` sheet
  here. So "the art exists" is only half the check — `find -iname` tells you the folder too, and
  a name at the wrong rung has to be rehomed (US-134 put Whamon beside its Perfect rather than
  beneath it) rather than authored where the document puts it.
- **Before removing or repointing an edge, check whether it is the target's ONLY in-edge**
  (`graph.parents(of:)`). US-134's V2 tree left no room for Gabumon's old junk fallback, and
  deleting that edge would have left Geremon reachable from nothing — a shipped Digimon quietly
  turned back into an orphan by the very story that removes them. Rehome it; a test should pin the
  new parent.
- **A device slug line renames in exactly six places, and the list has not changed across three
  trees now (US-133/134/135).** `elements.json` `lineDefaults`, `moves.json` `lineDefaults`,
  `MinigameAssignment.byLine`, `DexModel.lineTitles` (ADD, the others MOVE), plus
  `EvolutionGraphTests`' per-line count dictionary and any `$0.line == "<old>"` filter in
  `SeedRosterTests`. `perl -pi -e 's/"line": "old"/"line": "dmc-vN"/g'` on `evolutions.json` does
  the data half; then `grep -rn "<old>" Sources Tests docs Resources scripts` and read every hit —
  a node id equal to the old line key (`patamon`, `gabumon`) means most hits must NOT change.
- **`-dexLineDemo=<line>` does nothing without `-dexDemo`.** The line flag is read inside `DexView`;
  `-dexDemo` is what pushes the Dex at launch from `ContentView`. Alone it lands you on the main
  screen and the shot looks like the flag was ignored. The bundle id is `com.digivpet.DigiVPet`,
  NOT `...watchkitapp` — `simctl launch` fails with FBSOpenApplicationServiceErrorDomain code 4 if
  you guess it.
- **A device tree's junk Champion is the one BOTH of its Rookies fall to** — Numemon in Ver.1,
  Vegimon in Ver.2, Scumon in Ver.3, Nanimon in Ver.4, Raremon in Ver.5. That is the `isDefault`
  edge, and `EvolutionCriteriaTests.junkIds` has to name it or the junk-fallback test fails.
- **Raise a ceiling ONE step, to what the file now holds, never to what a later story will need.**
  US-133 raised the out-degree ceiling to four and wrote that four was what the whole document
  fits in; US-134 found Gabumon five-wide, and V4's Palmon and V5's Gizamon are SIX. Read the
  source document yourself rather than trusting the previous story's summary of it — and leave the
  guard as tight as the data, since a ceiling looser than the file it guards catches nothing.
- **To screenshot the MIDDLE of a scrolling sheet, shorten what is below it rather than hunting for
  a scroll anchor.** `-dexTreeLinkDemo` lands at the very bottom and the candidate grid is then off
  the top; `-dexWidestDetailDemo -dexBranchDemo` selects one branch, which cuts the hint list from
  eight rows to two and brings the grid back onto the same screen. `simctl` has no scroll command,
  so the demo flags ARE the scrollbar.
- **Update `prd.json` with `python3` + `json.load`/`json.dump(..., indent=2, ensure_ascii=False)`,
  then re-add the trailing newline.** It round-trips the existing formatting exactly — the diff for
  a `passes`/`notes` update is 2 lines — so a 1,000-line JSON file never has to be hand-edited.
  Check with `git diff --stat prd.json` before committing.
- **Price a ceiling raise off the DRAWABLE row, not the document's row.** US-136's Palmon was
  billed by two earlier stories as six-wide and needing a raise; both of that section's
  art-absent names were in that very row, so the real row was four and no ceiling moved. `ls`
  first, then decide. US-137's Gizamon went the same way even though US-136 HAD run `ls`
  and still predicted a raise: **in every device tree the junk Champion is itself a name in the
  row**, so a Rookie's edge count simply IS its drawable count — six named minus one absent is
  five edges, not six. Four earned is the hard limit regardless (distinct energies, four types).
  No ceiling has moved since US-134.
- **A device-slug rename touches a seventh place the six-place list misses: OTHER stories' tree
  tests.** US-134 scoped `dmcv2_vademon`/`dmcv2_ebemon` AROUND the `gazimon` line, so
  `DMCVersion2TreeTests` asserted `shared.line == "gazimon"` and that two node `comment`s contained
  that word. `grep -rn '<old-slug>' Sources Tests docs Resources scripts` and read every hit — and
  remember the slug is usually also a real node id, so most hits must NOT change.
- **AC9 of every Phase E story ("every edge has at least one condition with a non-empty hint")
  cannot be met literally — say which reading you took.** `EvolutionCriteriaTests`
  requires the `isDefault` junk edge to carry NO criteria (US-020's fallback ignores an edge's
  gates, so a gated junk edge lies about how it is taken), and the Digitama/Baby rungs are
  unconditioned for the same reason. The reading that IS true and worth asserting, as three
  claims: every EARNED edge at Child-and-up is conditioned, every condition in the whole file has
  a non-blank hint, every junk edge is unconditioned.
- **Prose in `docs/` is not a test, and it drifts ahead of the data.** The schema doc had described
  the V5 line's Rookies as "five Champions apiece, four of them shared" since US-046 — true of the
  source document, false of `evolutions.json`, where both had three, until US-137. If a claim about
  shipped data matters, put it in an assertion; a doc bullet will be read as fact and cost a story
  its estimate.
- **A line-scoped alias node (`piyo_yuramon`, `dmcv4_palmon`) needs THREE data entries**: a node in
  `evolutions.json`, an `elements.json` entry and a `moves.json` entry — and the move's
  `signatureName` must be globally UNIQUE (`MoveCatalogTests`), so it cannot be copied from the
  Digimon it aliases. Give it a second real attack of that Digimon's.
- **A Phase E story may legitimately remove ZERO orphans**, when everything in its section was
  already wired and the only new node is an alias. Count it with Appendix B both ways — regenerate
  `roster.generated.json` AND re-run the count against `git show HEAD:Resources/evolutions.json` —
  and ASSERT the zero in a test, or the next reader reads it as a slip.
- **A test that needs "something OUTSIDE the graph" must DERIVE it, never name it.** Phase E is
  pulling the whole roster into `evolutions.json`, so every hard-coded "roster-only" example is on
  a timer: US-138 ate `megaseadramon`, which three tests used as their keyword-tier/stage-tier
  example. `roster.entries.first { graph.node(id: $0.id) == nil }` survives the next sweep.
- **A story that ADDS a line, rather than renaming a seed, touches six whole-file facts the
  rename stories never did**: `EvolutionGraphTests`' per-line count dict, `graph.nodes.count` in
  `ElementCatalogTests` AND `EvolutionGraphValidatorTests`, `EggHatchingTests`' seeded-Digitama set
  (a new line means a new starting egg), `SeedRosterTests.seedLines`, and `RosterTests`' exact
  alias list. Budget for them before writing data. Relatedly: **a "this story added no nodes" test
  must count its OWN LINE** — US-137's counted the file and US-138 broke it from another tree.
- **A new line's Digitama must be a real ROSTER Digitama id, never a line-scoped alias.**
  `maps.json` grants eggs by roster id and `Resources/roster.json` excludes alias ids, so an alias
  egg can never drop and the line is unstartable however well it is wired. Prefer an orphan egg
  belonging to one of the tree's own Rookies; it buys an orphan too.
- **An alias node removes NO orphan** — it shares a roster entry that was already wired. Count
  removals as "new nodes carrying a plain roster id", and assert the split.
- **A dexOnly ROOKIE is far more expensive than a dexOnly leaf**: its whole subtree has to be
  rehomed onto a sibling Rookie or it is stranded. Prefer a pairing the shipped file ALREADY
  makes, which turns an invention into a precedent.
- **PHASE E: a name can be BOTH present and unusable, and `find` alone gets it wrong.** US-142's
  Machmon is in the roster AND on disk - under `Idle Frame Only/`, so `dexOnly`. Run both checks on
  every name: does a 48x64 sheet exist, and is the roster entry playable. Either alone is half a
  search (US-139's Octomon/Octmon, US-141's garbamon, US-142's Machmon).
- **PHASE E: grep a junk pick against the SECTION and against the WHOLE FILE - they answer
  different questions.** A name an EARLIER section drew may still be fine (it is just an alias:
  US-142's `pencme_raremon`). A name a LATER section draws must not be spent (US-142 left
  Chaosdramon alone; `jogress.json` was the second reason). Doing only the whole-file grep rejects
  good picks; doing only the section grep steals a later tree's node.
- **PHASE E: a hard-coded COUNT is on the same timer as a hard-coded example.** Phase E moves the
  orphan total every story, so `> 800` in `DexScreenTests` became exactly 800 in US-142. Assert a
  PROPORTION of whatever the roster holds, not a literal.
- **PHASE E: leave a marker test that FAILS the day the next story lands.** US-140 left
  `XCTAssertNil(graph.node(id: "warumonzaemon"))` with a comment naming US-142. It fired on the
  first run, explained itself, and was rewritten into the claim it was guarding. Cheaper and
  louder than a note.
- **A Perfect MAY branch.** The 2..5 out-degree rule and the junk-fallback rule are both scoped to
  Child and Adult; above that all a node needs is exactly one `isDefault` edge. US-142's
  `pencme_andromon` has two parents and two children because the document draws Andromon twice.
- **`Resources/*.md` is bundled with the app**, so a test can read the source evolution-tree
  markdown at run time and assert what the document does and does NOT say — that is how an
  invented junk chain becomes an assertion instead of a comment.
- **A source-document name with "no sprite" usually has ANOTHER SPELLING — searching the document's
  spelling is half a search.** US-139 found six in one section: four with nothing at all under the
  document's name and a real 48x64 sheet under a romanization or dub name the pack uses
  (Pichimon/`Pitchmon`, Bukamon/`Pukamon`, Syakomon/`Shakomon`, Dragomon/`Dagomon`), and two with a
  **dexOnly TWIN** — the roster holds BOTH `octomon` (idle-only) and `octmon` (animated), and both
  `marinedevimon` and `marindevimon`. The twin is the nastier shape: the file exists and the roster
  entry exists, and only `dexOnly` says it is unusable. **Search the roster by SUBSTRING of the
  display name and check every hit's `dexOnly` before calling a name absent** — otherwise a story
  rehomes or drops a subtree it never needed to.
- **Adding a LINE is an eight-place knock-on**, in the order they fail: `EvolutionGraphTests`'
  per-line count dict; `graph.nodes.count` in `ElementCatalogTests` AND
  `EvolutionGraphValidatorTests`; `EggHatchingTests`' seeded-Digitama set; `SeedRosterTests`'
  `seedLines`; `RosterTests`' exact alias list; `EvolutionCriteriaTests.junkIds` (the new tree's
  invented Child-rung and Adult-rung junk targets); and `MinigameAssignmentTests`' sharer map.
  Budget for all eight before writing data.
- **`json.dump` cannot rewrite `Resources/evolutions.json` — the file is mixed-encoding.** Comments
  written before US-136 hold `—` escapes and later ones hold literal em dashes, so neither
  `ensure_ascii` setting round-trips and any dump reformats ~30 unrelated lines. Append new nodes
  TEXTUALLY: `json.dumps` each node with `indent=2`, indent every line four spaces, splice before
  the final `\n  ]\n}`. Do `elements.json` / `moves.json` by string insertion too — their entries
  are one-line objects a dump would explode. Keep non-ASCII out of new comments.
- **The app's bundle id for `simctl` is `com.digivpet.DigiVPet`** (`project.yml`). A wrong id fails
  `simctl launch` with an opaque FBSOpenApplicationServiceErrorDomain code=4 while
  `simctl io screenshot` still writes a plausible PNG of the watch face — which reads as the very
  black-screen bug the Phase E screenshot exists to catch.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: THE FOUR ENERGIES ARE A HARD CEILING OF FOUR BRANCHES PER PARENT.**
  `EvolutionEngine` filters on `dominant == requiredEnergy` and the rung sweeps assert distinct
  energies per node, so a Baby II can carry at most FOUR edges, ever. Koromon and Pyocomon were both
  already full in US-148, which is why Agumon 2006 could not go on Agumon's own line and Elecmon
  Violet could not go on its only cited parent's. Compute `{vitality,strength,spirit,stamina} -
  used` over every candidate parent BEFORE promising a placement.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: A CHILD-OR-ABOVE SWEEP IS THREE RUNGS OF WORK.** An in-edge branches the rung
  below; an out-edge needs TWO edges (`EvolutionCriteriaTests` wants 2..5 at Child and Adult) and
  one of them must land on a JUNK node of the same line. Six lines opened by the Digitama sweeps had
  no Champion rung at all, so US-148 had to invent a junk floor for each before any of their
  Children could branch. Check `graph.nodes.filter { $0.line == L && $0.stage == <rung above> }`
  before estimating a sweep.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: TAKE JUNK NODES OUT OF THE ORPHAN POOL, NOT OUT OF AN ALIAS.** `junkIds` is a
  TEST's list, not a validator rule, and US-138/139/140/143 already set the precedent of picking a
  thematically-junk unused sheet. US-148 found six (Numemon X, Manekimon, Mimicmon, Troopmon,
  Damemon, Tsuchidarumon), so six junk floors removed six orphans instead of the zero a
  line-scoped alias removes. Search the orphan pool by flavour first.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: A JUNK EDGE SHARES ITS EARNED SIBLING'S ENERGY and sits below it on
  `minEnergy`** — the Agumon/Numemon shape from US-061. The distinct-energy rule is scoped to EARNED
  edges, so a two-edge Child needs only one energy; giving the junk edge its own would make it
  unreachable whenever the player's dominant type is the other one.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: CHECK THE STRANDED LISTS WHILE PICKING A PARENT, NOT AFTERWARDS.** An in-edge
  from a stranded parent strands the child and everything above it. US-148 moved Funbeemon off
  Puroromon (stranded) onto Tanemon — equally cited by Wikimon — and kept a whole thread reachable
  for free; only Fujamon's two Champions were unavoidable, because `penc-sw` has no Digitama at all.
- **PHASE E SWEEPS: hold the whole story as DATA in a throwaway authoring script that REFUSES TO
  WRITE until it has self-checked.** `/tmp/us148/author.py` verified in one pass: no id already a
  node, no edge crossing a line, no parent branching twice on one energy, no repeated symbol|tint
  within a line, no repeated `signatureName` globally, no digit in any hint. It caught three
  duplicate signature names before a byte hit the repo. Splice `evolutions.json` textually (US-136);
  a leaf node authored by the previous sweep is matched on its literal `"evolutions": []` line.
- **PHASE E: AN APPENDIX B "ORPHAN" CAN BE A DIGIMON ALREADY ON SCREEN — GREP THE GRAPH FOR ITS
  `spriteFile` BEFORE AUTHORING A NODE.** `roster.generated.json` carries the SHEET id from disk
  AND the graph's id, so a node whose id does not match its own sheet leaves the sheet counting as
  an orphan while its art renders. US-158 found `ex-tyranomon` that way: `dmc-v5` had drawn it
  since US-137 as `extyranomon`, and the fix was a RENAME (node id, three in-edges, the
  `elements.json` and `moves.json` rows) rather than a node. Careful — `hiandromon`/`hi-andromon`
  is the opposite case and is DELIBERATE: two real sheets, one node, pinned by `RosterTests`.
- **PHASE E, PERFECT RUNG: `projectileSymbol|tint` COLLISIONS ARE THE NORMAL CASE NOW, AND THE
  CHECK BELONGS BEFORE THE EDIT.** Eight of US-158's twenty-one first-draft moves collided — the
  pair is unique PER LINE and a big line already holds 49 rows, so `flame.fill` on `penc-nso` had
  two free tints left. Changing the SYMBOL beats reaching for an odd tint. `signatureName` is the
  global one and still bites on variants named after their base form.
