- **PHASE E: `linesWithAPerfect.subtracting(linesWithAnUltimate)` IS EMPTY AS OF US-158, AND EGG
  PROMOTIONS NOW COME FROM THE MIDDLE OF A THREAD.** `wanyamon` was the last line with Perfects and
  no Mega; opening it promoted all four of its Digitama at once, because
  `MainScreenModel.startingDigitamaId` filters on `graph.reachesUltimate`. Any sweep that opens a
  Perfect rung on one of the six lines that still have none — `xros`, `vital`, `adventure02`,
  `algomon`, `commandramon`, `diablomon` — owes an Ultimate over it in the same story or it
  re-opens the gap, and should grep `reachesUltimate` before assuming `EggHatchingTests` is inert.
- **PHASE E: ONE DIGIMON WITH TWO SHEETS IS TWO NODES; ONE SHEET WITH TWO NAMES IS ONE NODE.**
  US-143 merged HolyAngemon and MagnaAngemon because one sheet served both; US-158 gave Fantomon
  and Phantomon a node each because the pack ships both PNGs and the roster is one entry per SHEET.
  The rule that keeps it honest either way: no single Champion may reach the same Digimon twice
  under two spellings, so hang the second sheet off a DIFFERENT parent of the same line and pin
  that the two parent sets are disjoint.
- **SCREENSHOT STORIES: A STALE `simctl` SYSTEM ALERT CAN SURVIVE UNINSTALL/REINSTALL AND HIDE THE
  SCREEN — REBOOT THE SIM TO CLEAR IT.** US-172's first four screenshots (both sizes, both builds)
  all landed on the notification-permission alert DESPITE `-noNotificationPrompt`, which does work.
  The alert was a SpringBoard-level modal left over from an earlier session; `simctl terminate` +
  `uninstall` + reinstall + relaunch did NOT dismiss it, and `simctl` cannot tap it. `xcrun simctl
  shutdown <id> && boot <id>` (then reinstall) clears it. If a main-screen screenshot comes back as
  a full-screen system sheet, suspect a stale alert before you suspect your launch flags.
- **A DEMO FLAG THAT BANKS MAP STEPS MUST MOVE THAT MAP'S `encounterMarker` TOO (US-212).** US-201
  raises a wild encounter every 500 recorded steps and `checkForWildEncounter` runs on appear, so any
  flag that credits a realistic walk screenshots as "A wild <foe>!" over the whole action area — the
  flag hides the thing it seeds, and `simctl` cannot tap Flee. `profile.setEncounterMarker(<the same
  total>, forMap:)` is what a RESOLVED encounter does, so the save is left in a state the game itself
  can reach. `-mapListDemo` / `-mapListPartialDemo` still have this (they also push the map list, so
  neither can stand in for a main-screen shot); `-chargesDemo` is the corrected pattern.
- **SCREENSHOT STORIES: MEASURE THE MAP SLOT BY A CONTIGUOUS FULL-WIDTH SCAN DOWN FROM ITS FIXED TOP
  EDGE, NOT BY COLOUR.** The map fills the slot full width; the name/strip/bars below it are centred
  with black side margins. Scan rows down from just under the stats strip while >80% of the width is
  non-black (lum>18), stop after ~4 black rows. This reproduced US-120's independently-measured
  49.0pt (41mm) / 64.0pt (46mm) baseline to the point, which is what makes a growth number
  trustworthy. Colour/green detection and edge-column probes both leak into the sprite or the energy
  bars and gave wrong answers. Screenshots are @2x: divide px by 2 for pt. 41mm frame 352x430,
  46mm 416x496.

## 2026-07-22 — US-114: The light button moves to the top-left toolbar
- `LightButton` is now `ToolbarItem(placement: .topBarLeading)` in ContentView, the mirror of the
  Dex book at `.topBarTrailing`. `LightLayer` lost its `cycle` closure and draws the scrim ONLY;
  `LightButtonLayout.inset` is deleted; the button lost the `Circle` disc behind its glyph, which
  only ever existed to keep it legible through the 0.85 scrim it no longer stands in.
- Files: Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/LightSwitchView.swift, Tests/LightSwitchTests.swift,
  Tests/MainScreenLayoutTests.swift (the last two are doc comments made true again, no new asserts —
  nothing in the suite ever referenced `inset` or the closure, so nothing broke).
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1324 tests, with 0 failures` (unchanged; this story adds none).
- PASSED, MEASURED on BOTH screens, pre-story build vs post-story build, fresh install each,
  `-healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt -wanderDemo`. Screenshots + throwaway measurers in
  /tmp/us114 (NOT committed). All boxes are screenshot pixels, i.e. @2x.
  - THE LAMP LEFT THE ROOM. Its old home — the slot's top-leading corner, 48x48px = 24x24pt,
    exactly `diameter` — is x8-55 y137-184 on 41mm and x8-55 y153-200 on 46mm in the pre-story
    shots, and in the post-story shots that whole band is EMPTY: zero pixels over a threshold of
    30, across 150 frames, on both screens. Not "darker" — nothing is drawn there at all.
  - THE LAMP IS OUTSIDE THE SLOT ENTIRELY. Post-story glyph box: 41mm x47-62 y47-73, 46mm
    x57-72 y58-84. The pre-story lamp sat at `slot.minY` exactly (its offset had no y inset), so
    those pre-story boxes READ OFF the slot's top edge: y137 on 41mm, y153 on 46mm. The new glyph
    clears it by 64px on 41mm and 69px on 46mm. That is AC8's "no button overlaps the sprite at
    any walk offset" proved for ALL offsets rather than for the ones sampled — the sprite cannot
    leave the slot, and the button is no longer in it.
  - THE SPRITE DID NOT MOVE OR SHRINK. Its box is pixel-identical pre- and post-story: 41mm
    x152-199 y156-203, 46mm x172-243 y177-248. The Dex button is identical too (41mm x260-328
    y28-127, peak 147, mean 23.59 to the hundredth in both).
  - US-112 IS UNCHANGED (AC3). Light on -> off, post-story: sprite peak 255 -> 38 on both screens,
    and 255 x 0.15 = 38.25, the same 38 the pre-story build gives. Action row identical on and off
    and identical between builds (41mm mean 37.82 both, 46mm 28.09 both).
  - THE TOOLBAR LAMP IS NEVER DIMMED (AC4). With the light OFF its peak is still 255, on both
    screens — and AC5's icon still tracks the state: rgb(255,214,10) `lightbulb.fill` lit,
    rgb(255,255,255) `lightbulb.slash` out.
- HONEST CORRECTION TO AC6/AC8, and the one thing the story asked for that is NOT true:
  **the sprite's reachable area is NOT wider after this change, because `LightButtonLayout.inset`
  was never subtracted from anything the sprite could reach.** The PRD says "the sprite's usable
  rect grows by that inset"; in fact `inset` appeared in exactly one expression — the button's own
  `.offset` inside `LightLayer` — and `git show HEAD:Sources/ContentView.swift | grep inset` is
  empty. The walk bound is `max((screenWidth - side) / 2 - 4, 0)` in `WanderingSpriteView` and
  reads only the device width and the sprite's own size, so it is unchanged, which the identical
  sprite boxes above confirm. What grew is the UNOBSTRUCTED area, and by the button's whole 24x24pt
  footprint rather than by the 2pt inset. Marked passing on that reading: the story's goal — the
  switch is out of the room and never covers the Digimon — is met and measured.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - TRAP, PRE-EXISTING AND NOT CAUSED BY THIS STORY, and US-115 will hit it first: with
    `-wanderDemo` the Digimon ANIMATES but DOES NOT WALK on either simulator. Over 150 frames /
    60s, and again over a 40-frame burst taken as fast as `simctl` will go, the sprite box never
    left x152-199 (41mm) / x172-243 (46mm) — dead centre, `facing` never flipped, so
    `advanceOneStep()` was never reached. The walk1/walk2 alternation is the INNER `TimelineView`
    in `DigimonSpriteView`; the OUTER one in `WanderingSpriteView` is what drives the position, and
    it is that one that looks dead. Ruled out: the pose really is `.idle` (the two frames on screen
    match sheet indices 0 and 1 pixel for pixel, and `.sleep`'s 4/5 are a crouch that is plainly
    not what is drawn), and `bound` is not 0 (41mm scale 2 -> 68pt, 46mm scale 3 -> 76pt).
    IDENTICAL in the pre-story build, so this is not a regression from US-114 — but the last wave
    DID photograph the sprite at both walls, so something between then and now broke it. Anyone
    screenshotting a walk needs to find this first.
  - A pre-story build is only comparable on a FRESH INSTALL: a save that has spent a battle draws
    an extra caption line under the action row and that costs the sprite a whole scale step.
  - `.topBarLeading` on watchOS puts the item BESIDE the time, not under it — the 41mm glyph lands
    at y47-73 and the clock is untouched. No layout budget was spent to gain it.
- REMAINS: US-115 onward (1/56 passing).

## 2026-07-22 — US-115: The selected map draws behind the Digimon
- `MapBackgroundView` draws the selected map's asset at `MapBackgroundLayout.opacity` (0.35),
  `.resizable().scaledToFill()`, installed as a **`backgroundPreferenceValue`** off the SAME
  `SpriteSlotBoundsKey` anchor the scrim reads, sized to that slot, `.clipped()` and `.offset` into
  place. Background rather than overlay is the whole design: the layer is painted before the VStack,
  so the sprite and every row are drawn on top of it and `LightLayer` — an overlay — is painted
  after all of them. The map being dimmed by the scrim is therefore structural, not arithmetic.
- `MainScreenModel.selectedMapAsset` is the seam: nil for every real save today (the catalog is
  US-116, the persisted pick is US-119), set only by the new DEBUG `-mapDemo=<asset>` flag.
- Files: Sources/MapBackgroundView.swift (new), Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Tests/MapBackgroundTests.swift (new, 7 tests).
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1331 tests, with 0 failures` (1324 + the 7 new).
- PASSED, MEASURED on 46mm, clean install per build, `-healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt
  -wanderDemo`. Screenshots + throwaway measurers in /tmp/us115 (NOT committed). Boxes are
  screenshot pixels, i.e. @2x on a 416x496 shot.
  - THE MAP IS CONFINED TO THE ROOM (AC1, AC3). Diffing the no-map shot against the map shot from
    the SAME build: the screen changes in **x4-411 y153-259 and nowhere else**, one contiguous band,
    identically for 01_grassland, 14_farmland and 16_iceland. The stats strip above it, the name
    line, the energy bars, the action row and the whole toolbar are byte-identical — so the map is
    behind none of them, and it grew layout in neither axis.
  - THE MAP IS BEHIND THE DIGIMON, not over it. On matched walk frames, **all 2916 pixels the
    sprite paints are byte-identical with a map behind them**, on all three maps. First run of this
    read 1512/2916 on farmland and that was a FALSE ALARM — see the walk-frame trap below.
  - THE SCRIM COVERS THE MAP (AC5). Map band mean luma 63.485 with the light on -> 31.721 at semi
    (x0.4997) -> 9.480 at off (x0.1493); peak 244.1 -> 122.6 -> 36.3. That is exactly
    `LightState.dimOpacity` applied to the map, which is what "inside the scrimmed region, painted
    below the scrim" means in numbers. Chrome above (rows 100-150) and below (265-495) the slot is
    identical to three decimals with the light on and out. Reproduced twice, on two installs.
  - THE OPACITY ON SCREEN IS THE AUTHORED ONE (AC2). Rendering each asset with the same
    scaledToFill math into the same 416x107 slot over black, then dividing the Simulator's band by
    it, recovers **0.339 / 0.339 / 0.342** for grassland / farmland / iceland against the authored
    0.35. (The ~3% shortfall is the reference render's own colour handling and the display's
    rounded corners, both included in the divisor; it settles 0.35 vs 0.5 or 1.0 beyond doubt.)
  - NO MAP SELECTED IS US-114's SCREEN (AC6). Pre-story build vs post-story build, both fresh
    installs, no map: the ONLY differing pixels on the entire 416x496 screen are **x175-240 y39-62,
    the clock digits**, because the minute rolled between the two runs. Everything else — lamp, Dex
    book, stats strip, sprite, name line, bars, action row, caption — is byte-identical.
  - THE DIGIMON STAYS LEGIBLE (AC7). Over the three brightest assets: the sprite's mean luma is
    190.3 and its **dimmest** pixel is 146.3, while the **brightest** map pixel beside it is 88.4
    (grassland 85.9, farmland 87.0, iceland 88.4). The two ranges do not overlap at all — no pixel
    of the Digimon is ever as dark as the brightest pixel of the brightest map. Mean-vs-mean
    contrast is 2.93:1 / 3.16:1 / 3.01:1.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **THE WALK-FRAME TRAP, and it will bite any story that diffs the sprite between two builds.**
    A single screenshot from each build is NOT comparable: the inner `TimelineView` in
    `DigimonSpriteView` alternates walk1/walk2 regardless of whether the sprite translates, so two
    shots taken seconds apart routinely catch opposite frames and read as a large bogus diff.
    Fix: take a BURST of ~6 shots per configuration and compare every pair, then use the pair that
    agrees. The frames are trivially separable by lit-pixel count (here 1476 vs 1620 under a scrim,
    2916 vs 2916-with-different-geometry lit) and the matching pair goes to 100% identity while a
    mismatched pair sticks at the ~50% both poses share. Four hypotheses were burned before this
    was the answer.
  - **THE LIGHT STATE PERSISTS ACROSS LAUNCHES AND POISONS LATER SCREENSHOTS.** `-lightOffDemo`
    writes `.off` to the save, and there is no `-lightOnDemo` to undo it, so every subsequent run
    on that container is photographed under a 0.85 scrim — silently, since the shot still looks
    plausible. Always take the light-on shots FIRST, or `simctl erase` between. Lost a burst to it.
  - `.backgroundPreferenceValue` is the mirror of the `.overlayPreferenceValue` already on this
    VStack and costs the sprite nothing: a background is sized by the view it is behind and never
    proposes a size back, so no asset can grow the layout however large it is. Reading the SAME
    anchor as the scrim is what makes "the map is inside the scrimmed region" true by construction
    rather than by two rects happening to agree.
  - Recovering a constant like an opacity from a screenshot works and is worth the twenty lines:
    render the source asset yourself with the same fill math into the measured slot over black,
    then divide. It is the difference between "the map looks faint" and "the screen is painting
    0.339".
  - The pre-existing US-114 trap is unchanged and did NOT block this story: `-wanderDemo` still
    animates without translating. The sprite's fixed position is actually what made the
    byte-identity test above easy, so nobody needs to fix it before US-116.
  - Do NOT put `.interpolation(.none)` on the map backgrounds. The sprite rule exists to stop 16x16
    art being smoothed UP; these are 822x330 assets drawn DOWN into a ~208pt slot, where
    nearest-neighbour drops rows and columns unevenly.
- REMAINS: US-116 onward (2/56 passing). Phase A is done; Phase B starts with the map catalog.
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-116: Map catalog data file and model
- `Resources/maps.json` (16 maps) and `Sources/MapCatalog.swift` — `AdventureMap` (id, displayName,
  assetName, tier, totalSteps, unlockedBy, opponentPool, digitamaSlots), `DigitamaSlot`
  (digitamaId + `[EvolutionCondition]`), and `MapCatalog` in the `Roster` shape: private id index,
  hand-written decoder, `load(from:)` for tests, `bundled` that fatalErrors on bad data.
- `DigitamaSlot` reuses `EvolutionCondition` wholesale rather than getting a parallel type. That is
  what lets US-121 draw a `?` slot's hints through the Dex's own `ConditionReveal`, and it means
  US-117's blank-hint rule is the same rule the graph validator already has.
- Files: Resources/maps.json (new), Sources/MapCatalog.swift (new), Tests/MapCatalogTests.swift
  (new, 17 tests). NO project.yml change — the `Resources` folder is already a `resources` build
  phase, so the file is picked up by existing config.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1348 tests, with 0 failures` (1331 + the 17 new).
- PASSED, checked rather than assumed:
  - BUNDLED FOR REAL. `ls` on the built product shows `DigiVPet.app/maps.json`, 28,644 bytes, and
    every test loads it through `MapCatalog.load()` off `Bundle.main` rather than off a fixture.
  - ART RESOLVES. All 16 `assetName`s return a non-nil `UIImage(named:)` at runtime, which is the
    same lookup `Image(_:)` does, and all 16 pass `MapBackgroundLayout.shouldDraw`. The 16
    imagesets were confirmed with `ls Resources/Assets.xcassets` before a name was written.
  - THE FR-6 TABLE IS SPELLED OUT IN THE TEST, not derived from the file — a test that read the
    order and totals back out of `maps.json` would agree with whatever the file said, which is the
    one thing it must not do. Order, tier and totalSteps all match; totals also strictly increase
    and tiers never drop.
  - THE CHAIN IS LINEAR AND COMPLETE. Map 1 has no `unlockedBy`, every other names its predecessor,
    exactly one map has none, and walking the chain forward from `startingMap` reaches all 16 —
    the second test catches a strand that the pairwise one would not.
- SCOPE CALL, deliberate and worth knowing: **`opponentPool` and `digitamaSlots` are authored here,
  not left empty.** No later story authors them, and US-121 (detail view), US-122 (opponent picks)
  and US-128 (drop engine) all consume them — empty lists would have made those untestable. 170
  opponent ids and all 57 Digitama are placed.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **AUTHOR ROSTER-REFERENCING DATA FROM DISPLAY NAMES THROUGH A RESOLVER SCRIPT, NEVER BY TYPING
    IDS.** /tmp/us116/build_maps.py (throwaway, NOT committed) holds the 16 maps as display names
    and resolves each against `roster.json`, hard-failing on an unknown name, an AMBIGUOUS name, or
    a `dexOnly` entry, then emits the JSON. Every Phase E story has this same problem at ten times
    the scale and should do the same. It earned its keep immediately: `Rapidmon` is TWO roster
    entries — `rapidmon` (Perfect) and `rapidmon_armor` (Armor-Hybrid) — so a hand-typed
    `"rapidmon"` would have been a coin flip nobody would have noticed. Display names are not
    unique in this roster; ids are.
  - The same script asserts the whole-file invariants at authoring time (all 57 Digitama placed,
    none placed twice), so the test suite confirms them rather than discovering them.
  - `Roster.bundled.entries(at: .digitama)` is the clean way to enumerate eggs; there are exactly
    57 and NONE is dexOnly, so every egg on disk is placeable.
  - CONDITION UNITS, read off `HealthMetricReader` rather than guessed — steps: count;
    `health.sleep`: MINUTES (evolutions.json uses 1400–1800 over a stage); `health.activeEnergy`:
    kilocalories; `health.exerciseMinutes` / `health.standTime` / `health.mindfulMinutes`: minutes;
    `health.distanceWalkingRunning`: METRES; `health.standHours` / `health.flightsClimbed` /
    `health.workouts`: counts. Authoring "8 km" as `8` would have shipped a slot that drops on the
    first step.
  - The empty-on-hardware metric family (handwashing, toothbrushing, water, daylight, audio
    exposure) is a real trap for DROP slots specifically: an evolution edge gated on one can be a
    bonus branch beside a reachable one, but a Digitama slot is the ONLY route to that egg, so any
    such gate makes it unobtainable. FR-13 names `health.handwashing` for 06_industrial/Pulse, so
    it is authored as asked but PAIRED with a steps condition to satisfy US-128's "never solely"
    rule; every other slot avoids the family. If US-128 wants a stronger rule than "not solely",
    Pulse is the one slot to revisit.
- REMAINS: US-117 onward (3/56 passing). US-117 now has real data to validate — 16 assetNames,
  170 opponent ids, 57 Digitama slots and a 16-long unlock chain.

## 2026-07-22 — US-117: Map catalog validator
- `Sources/MapCatalogValidator.swift` in the `EvolutionGraphValidator` shape, deliberately down to
  the details: a `MapValidationError` enum (8 cases, `Equatable` + `CustomStringConvertible`), an
  `extension MapCatalog` with `validate(roster:assetExists:)` that RETURNS findings and never
  throws, and an injectable `MapCatalog.AssetExistsCheck` / `MapCatalog.assetExists()` mirroring
  `EvolutionGraph.SpriteExistsCheck` / `spriteExists(in:)`. Findings come back in map order with
  the unlock cycles appended last.
- Files: Sources/MapCatalogValidator.swift (new), Tests/MapCatalogValidatorTests.swift (new, 15
  tests). No project.yml change — `Sources` and `Tests` are directory globs.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1363 tests, with 0 failures` (1348 + the 15 new).
- PASSED, every rejection rule fired on its own fixture. Each fixture is the sound two-map catalog
  with EXACTLY ONE thing broken, so a reported error can only be the thing that was broken, and a
  control test asserts the sound catalog reports `[]`:
  `missingAsset` (an unknown imageset, and separately an empty `assetName` through the REAL
  check), `unknownOpponent`, `dexOnlyOpponent`, `unknownDigitama`, `notADigitama` (a Child in an
  egg slot), `unknownUnlockedBy`, `unlockCycle` (a 3-map loop, a map that unlocks ITSELF, and a
  loop three maps hang off — reported ONCE), `emptyConditionHint` (whitespace-only).
- PASSED, AC8 against the REAL data rather than a stub: `MapCatalog.load().validate()` reports
  ZERO findings over the shipped 16 maps, 170 opponent ids and 57 Digitama slots, using
  `Roster.bundled` and `UIImage(named:)`. The assertion's failure message joins the findings'
  `description`s, so the day someone retunes a map the test names the map and the id.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **A "the shipped file is clean" test is worthless without a companion test that the CHECK is a
    check.** `assetExists` is injected, so a green real-file run is also what you get from a stub
    that says yes to everything. `testTheRealAssetCheckDistinguishesShippedArtFromMissingArt`
    pins `01_grassland` true / `17_moonbase` false / `""` false. Any later validator with an
    injected world-touching check wants the same pair of tests.
  - **Order the rules so one mistake does not hide another.** A slot's blank-hint findings are
    collected BEFORE its roster lookup, so a slot with a bad id AND a blank hint reports both and
    the author fixes them in one run rather than two — the same reason `EvolutionGraphValidator`
    validates conditions before resolving the edge target. A test pins it.
  - **Cycle detection walks up from EVERY map, not from the roots.** A cycle that no other map
    hangs off is reachable from no root, so a "walk forward from `startingMap`" check — which is
    what US-116's reachability test does — cannot see it. Each cycle is keyed on its sorted
    members so the same loop found from four maps is one finding, not four.
  - `UIImage(named:)` works in the test bundle because the tests run in the app as TEST_HOST, so
    `.main` is the app bundle. Do NOT reach for `Bundle(for:)` for asset-catalog art — that is the
    XCTest bundle and has none of it. (`MapCatalogTests` already relied on this; it is now pinned.)
  - The validator takes `roster: Roster = .bundled` as a PARAMETER rather than reading the global
    inside, which is what let all nine fixture tests run against a 3-entry roster (one egg, one
    playable, one dexOnly) instead of hunting the real one for an id with the right shape. US-130's
    Jogress validator has the identical problem and should copy this signature.
- REMAINS: US-118 onward (4/56 passing). The map data is now guarded end to end — US-118 starts
  the behaviour half of Phase B by accruing steps to the selected map.
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-118: Steps accrue to the selected map
- `Sources/MapProgress.swift` (new): `@Model MapProgress` — ONE global record holding
  `selectedMapId`, `[mapId: recordedSteps]` and `[mapId: finishedAt]`, in `MetricLedger`'s
  dictionary shape — plus `MapStepCreditor.credit(steps:to:catalog:now:)` beside `EnergyCreditor`
  and `MetricCreditor`. Sixteen rows that are only ever read together are not sixteen records.
- `Sources/MetricLedger.swift`: new `MetricLedger.claim(_:dayTotal:now:calendar:)` and `rollDay`.
  `MetricCreditor` was refactored onto them, so the day-roll and the `max(0, total - baseline)`
  rule now live in exactly ONE place and the map spends the same delta any later metric consumer
  will. This is AC3 made structural rather than promised.
- `Sources/EnergyLedger.swift`: new `HealthDayReadings` + `HealthEnergySource.dayReadings(now:)`,
  keeping one read in both shapes — `byEnergyType` for energy, `quantities[.steps]` for the map.
  `readings(now:)` is now a one-line wrapper, so every existing caller and fixture is untouched.
- `Sources/GameStore.swift`: `MapProgress` added to `schema` + `loadOrCreateMapProgress()`.
- `Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`: holds `metricLedger` and `mapProgress`, takes `maps:` (injected
  like `graph`/`roster`), and gains `selectMap(_:)` and `creditMapSteps(_:)`. `selectedMapAsset` is
  now published FROM the saved selection through the catalog — the US-115 seam, repointed as that
  story predicted, with the view unchanged.
- Files: Sources/MapProgress.swift (new), Sources/MetricLedger.swift, Sources/EnergyLedger.swift,
  Sources/GameStore.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Tests/MapProgressTests.swift (new, 23
  tests). No project.yml change — `Sources` and `Tests` are directory globs.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1386 tests, with 0 failures` (1363 + the 23 new). All 23 were also
  observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped rather than inferred.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion:
  - AC4, THE ONE THAT MATTERS: 1,000 steps read twice through the real `refresh()` credits the map
    1,000. A day that grew to 1,600 credits 600 more, not 1,600 more.
  - AC2/AC5: 600 steps on `first`, switch, 400 more -> `first` still 600 and `second` 400. Steps
    walked BEFORE any map was chosen credit nothing.
  - AC6: 999 does not finish a 1,000-step map and 1,000 does; a second and a third crossing keep
    the FIRST stamp. AC7: the counter runs on to 4,500 on that same 1,000-step map.
  - AC1: a second `MainScreenModel` over the same store file — which is what a cold launch is —
    reads back the steps, the stamp and the selection, and publishes `01_grassland` behind the
    Digimon again.
  - AC8: the clock is injected, every reading comes from a `FixtureSampleFetcher`, nothing waits.
  - Extra, not asked for but cheap: map progress survives a `rebirth`, because `resetGame` deletes
    only the `GameState`. US-123/129 both depend on that staying true.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **`MetricCreditor` HAS NEVER BEEN WIRED INTO THE APP, and that is a real bug waiting for a
    story.** US-058 built `MetricLedger`/`MetricCreditor` and deliberately left the wiring to a
    "which metrics are worth reading every refresh" story that was never written. Nothing in
    `Sources/` calls `MetricCreditor.credit` — so `state.stageMetricTotals` is permanently zero in
    the shipped app, and the **78 `window: "stage"` conditions in evolutions.json** (15 of them on
    `health.steps`) can never be satisfied by a real player. It was left alone here ON PURPOSE:
    wiring it changes evolution eligibility across the entire game and belongs in its own story
    with its own regression pass, not inside a map-accrual story. Whoever takes it: credit through
    `MetricLedger.claim` and have `creditMapSteps` read `credited[.healthSteps]` instead of
    claiming for itself — that is a two-line change and the doc comments on both point at it.
    Do NOT bank `health.sleep` through the same day-roll without thinking: its window is 18:00
    yesterday to noon today, not the local day `rollDay` keys on.
  - **A delta is SPENT once it is claimed, so decide deliberately who claims it.** With no map
    selected this story claims the step delta and DROPS it. The alternative — not claiming — would
    let a player who picks a map at 18:00 retroactively bank the whole day into it, which is
    exactly what "only steps read while that map is selected accrue to it" forbids. Six of the new
    tests failed on the first run because of this and they were RIGHT to: `start()` performs a
    refresh, so a fixture walked before `start()` is already banked by the time a test selects a
    map. Select the map first, then walk.
  - **Do not derive a raw measurement back out of an energy figure.** `readings[.strength]` is
    steps ÷ 100, capped by `EnergyRates.dailyCapPerEnergyType` — it is not a number of steps and
    cannot be turned back into one. That is why `dayReadings` exists; the alternative, a second
    HealthKit read for the map, would be two answers about one day taken microseconds apart with
    no reason to agree.
  - **A demo flag that writes to the SAVE needs its inverse in the same commit.** `-mapDemo=` now
    persists the selection, so it would have poisoned every later screenshot on that container the
    way `-lightOffDemo` did to US-115. `-mapDemo=none` clears it. The Codebase Patterns entry
    above was written from that exact bruise; this is the first flag to obey it up front.
  - `MapProgress` is one record with three properties and no relationships specifically so US-123
    can MOVE those fields onto `PlayerProfile` rather than rewrite them. It is already the thing
    US-123's AC describes.
- REMAINS: US-119 onward (5/56 passing). Phase B's data and accrual are done; US-119 is the first
  screen that reads them, and `MapProgress.recordedByMap` + `finishedAt(forMap:)` are what it
  wants. `MainScreenModel.selectMap(_:)` is already the call US-120's list makes.
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-119: Map list screen
- `Sources/MapListView.swift` (new): `MapListRow` — a pure value built from `MapCatalog` +
  `MapProgress`, carrying the name, the art, the floored counter, both marks, the lock, the unlock
  line and `contents` — plus `MapListMarks` (the three glyph names), `MapListSelector` (what a tap
  does to the selection) and `MapListView` itself. The view is a layout of those fields and holds
  no rule of its own, which is the only reason 30 tests can reach this screen at all.
- `Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`: `mapRows` (computed off the INJECTED catalog, like
  `selectedMapAsset`), and `seedMapListDemoIfRequested`.
- `Sources/ContentView.swift`: `MapListView` pushed onto the app's one `NavigationStack`, beside
  the Dex, so it keeps a back button and US-121 can push a detail on top of it.
- `Sources/MapProgress.swift`: `clearForDemo()`, DEBUG-only.
- Files: Sources/MapListView.swift (new), Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Sources/MapProgress.swift, Tests/MapListTests.swift (new, 30 tests). No project.yml change —
  `Sources` and `Tests` are directory globs.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1416 tests, with 0 failures` (1386 + the 30 new). All 30 were also
  observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped rather than inferred.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion:
  - AC2/AC3: one row per map in catalog order (which is tier order, asserted as an invariant over
    the real file rather than as sixteen re-typed strings), and `progressText` is exactly
    `1222 / 25000`.
  - AC4: `checkmark.seal.fill`/green vs `figure.walk.circle.fill`/orange — different on BOTH
    channels, asserted pairwise and photographed together on one row.
  - AC5: a locked row's `contents` is nil and its line is `Finish <previous displayName>`; all 15
    locked rows over the shipped chain name a real map.
  - AC6: `MapListSelector` hands `current` back unchanged for a locked row, and the view disables
    the button as well.
  - AC7: `50000 / 50000` in full on 41mm and 46mm, no truncation, no ellipsis.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **NEVER FORMAT A COUNT WITH `NumberFormatter` WHEN THE CRITERION NAMES AN EXACT STRING.** It is
    locale-dependent: `25000` renders as `25,000` in en_US, `25.000` in de_DE and `25 000` (with a
    NON-BREAKING space) in fr_FR — three strings for one AC, and the third would pass a naive
    `contains(",")` check. String interpolation is the whole answer here. The test asserts the
    absence of `,`, `.` and `\u{00A0}` for exactly that reason.
  - **A DEMO FLAG THAT WRITES TO THE SAVE MUST BE IDEMPOTENT, not just reversible.** The Codebase
    Patterns rule above says give it an inverse, and US-118 obeyed it — but that is not enough:
    `-mapListDemo` credited a full map's worth on EVERY launch, so the second run photographed
    `100000 / 50000` and the third would have shown 150000. A doubled counter looks completely
    plausible in a screenshot. The seed now calls `clearForDemo()` first, so N launches and one
    launch produce the same screen. Add "clears before it seeds" to the rule.
  - That accident was worth something on its own: `100000 / 50000` — six digits over five — did not
    truncate on 41mm either, so the layout has more headroom than the AC asks for.
  - **`simctl` cannot scroll, so any list longer than a screen needs a `ScrollViewReader` +
    `-...BottomDemo` hook or its far end can never be photographed.** Third time this project has
    needed one (`-dexScrollDemo`, `-settingsBottomDemo`, now `-mapListBottomDemo`) and the 500ms
    sleep before `scrollTo` is needed every time — `.task` runs before the rows are measured, and
    scrolling to an unmeasured row lands short of it.
  - The queued-notification trap bit again on the 46mm sim and cost another ~5 minutes:
    `-noNotificationPrompt` does NOT dismiss an alert queued by an EARLIER build, so the first shot
    came back as the permission sheet in Chinese. `simctl erase` on the device is still the only
    fix, and `-healthAnswered` is mandatory afterwards or you land on onboarding.
  - **Lock rule is deliberately ONE STEP — "is my predecessor finished" — not a walk up the whole
    chain.** They agree on real data (a map cannot be finished without being selectable), and where
    they differ the one-step answer is the one the row's own "Finish <previous>" sentence promises.
    A lock that contradicts the line printed beside it is worse than a lock that opens early.
  - `isFinished` comes off the finish STAMP rather than `recorded >= total`. The difference bites
    the day a map is retuned longer in an update: the player really did cross the old line, and a
    derived flag would take it back off them. Same reasoning as `MapProgress.markFinished`'s
    once-only stamp, and US-121/122 should read the stamp too.
  - `Int(x.rounded(.down))` for the counter, never `Int(x.rounded())`: a rounded 2999.6 would print
    `3000 / 3000` on a map that is not finished, which is a screen contradicting itself.
- REMAINS: US-120 onward (6/56 passing). `MapListView(rows: model.mapRows) { model.selectMap($0) }`
  is exactly the expression US-120's strip needs to push, and the view already calls `dismiss()`
  after a selection, which is that story's "pops back to the main screen".

## 2026-07-22 — US-120: Map strip on the main screen, and switching maps — NOT PASSING (AC4)
- `Sources/MapStripView.swift` (new): `MapStrip` — a pure value carrying the map name, the counter,
  the map id and `isPrompt` — plus `MapStripMarks` (three glyphs), `MapStripLayout` (the font, the
  icon size, the disabled fade and `isPartyReachable`) and `MapStripView` itself, which is a
  `NavigationLink` to `MapListView` beside a faded, unreachable party button. Same split as
  `MapListRow`/`MapListView`: every rule is in the value, the view is a layout of its fields.
- `Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`: `mapStrip`, computed off the injected catalog and `MapProgress`
  exactly as `mapRows` is, so the strip and the list cannot drift; plus `-mapStripWidestDemo`.
- `Sources/ContentView.swift`: one row directly above the energy bars.
- Files: Sources/MapStripView.swift (new), Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Tests/MapStripTests.swift (new, 19 tests). No project.yml change — `Sources` and `Tests` are
  directory globs, but `xcodegen generate` IS still needed for a NEW file or the build cannot see it.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1435 tests, with 0 failures` (1416 + the 19 new). All 19 also
  observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped rather than inferred.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion — everything except AC4:
  - AC1: one row, two controls — a wide leading `NavigationLink` labelled with the selected map's
    name and `recorded / total`, and a trailing party icon.
  - AC2: the party button is BOTH unreachable (`MapStripLayout.isPartyReachable == false`, so it is
    an `Image` and not a `Button` — it has no tap target at all) AND faded to 0.3. Either alone
    would be the half-measure the criterion forbids.
  - AC3: one line. Measured on screen: 13.5pt on 41mm, 14.0pt on 46mm.
  - AC5: a selection made through `selectMap(_:)` moves the strip's text and US-115's background
    together and SURVIVES A RELAUNCH — a second `MainScreenModel` over the same store file, which is
    what a cold launch is, reads back `Second` / `02_river`. `MapListView` already calls `dismiss()`,
    which is the "pops back".
  - AC6: with nothing selected the strip names map one as a prompt (folded-map glyph, secondary
    tint, `mapId` nil rather than "first" — the strip NAMES a map, it does not claim you are there),
    and the game is fully playable: `phase == .playing`, a presentation, energy bars, no gate.
  - AC7, MEASURED on both screens with `-mapStripWidestDemo`, which finishes every map and selects
    the LAST one, so the row reads `Cyberpunk 50000 / 50000` — the longest name beside the widest
    figure this row can ever carry. On 41mm the ink runs: glyph x7-20, "Cyberpunk" x31-137,
    "50000" x147-203, "/" x210-216, "50000" x223-280, an 18.0pt CLEAR GAP, party icon x317-344,
    3.5pt right margin. Nothing truncates: both five-digit runs are full width (57px and 58px) and
    there is no ellipsis. And nothing SHRANK either — "Cyberpunk" is 107px on 41mm and 107px on
    46mm, so `minimumScaleFactor(0.7)` never fired on the narrow screen. The two controls are
    18.0pt apart on 41mm and 49.5pt on 46mm, and the link's `contentShape` stops before the icon.
- **FAILED — AC4, and it is the only one. The sprite slot sits at EXACTLY the scale boundary on
  both watch sizes, so ANY row of ANY height costs the Digimon a whole scale step.**
  `SpriteScale.fitting` floors `slotHeight / 16`. Measured pre-story, hatched Child, map behind
  (`-battleAffordableDemo -mapDemo=01_grassland`, fresh install, both sims):
  - 41mm slot **49.0pt** -> floor(49/16) = 3 -> a 48pt Digimon. Slack: **1.0pt**.
  - 46mm slot **64.0pt** -> floor(64/16) = 4 -> a 64pt Digimon. Slack: **0.0pt**.
  Post-story, same command, same containers:
  - 41mm slot 49.0 -> **35.5pt**, Digimon 48 -> **32pt**.
  - 46mm slot 64.0 -> **50.0pt**, Digimon 64 -> **48pt**.
  On a FRESH INSTALL — the state AC4 actually names, "measured against a US-114 screenshot" — the
  Digimon does NOT shrink: the slot is already 27.5pt (41mm) / 42.5pt (46mm), below
  `SpriteScale.minimum`, so the sprite is pinned at 32.0pt in both builds and the `?` placeholder
  box (which is exactly `16 x scale` and so a perfect ruler) is byte-identical — x144-207 y137-200
  on 41mm, x176-239 on 46mm, before and after. But the SLOT still loses 13.5pt / 14.0pt
  (41mm 27.5 -> 14.0, 46mm 42.5 -> 28.5, measured by diffing a `-mapDemo=01_grassland` shot against
  a `-mapDemo=none` one), and the sprite's existing overflow grows until **the name line runs
  straight through the Digimon on 41mm** — photographed, the "?" spans y137-200 and
  "Agu Digitama · Digitama" now sits at y173-194 on top of it, where before it was at y200-221.
  Both readings of AC4 fail: the slot is smaller in every state, and the Digimon is a full scale
  step smaller in the state a real player spends the game in.
- **EVERY WAY OF PAYING FOR THE ROW WAS MEASURED, and none of them is this story's to spend:**
  - **The bottom safe area is real, unused, and enough** — 26pt on 41mm, 36pt on 46mm, below the
    action row. Proved with a throwaway `.ignoresSafeArea(.container, edges: .bottom)` probe build:
    the slot went 49 -> **75pt** on 41mm and 64 -> **100pt** on 46mm. **But claiming it slides the
    action row's five 30pt circles to within 12pt of the display's bottom edge, and the outer two
    sit 5pt from the side edges — that is inside the corner arc, which is what the inset is for.**
    Half of it is no better: at 12pt up, a ~35-40pt corner radius cuts in ~9-11pt horizontally.
  - **Shrinking the surrounding chrome adds up to about 14pt** — name 12 -> 9pt (3.6), stats 11 ->
    9pt (2.4), `ActionControls`' `.padding(.top, 2)` (2.0), `VStack(spacing: 1)` -> 0 (5.0), energy
    bars spacing (1.0). It would work. It is also a screen-wide legibility regression bought with
    one row, unrequested by this story, and it leaves the layout with zero breathing room for the
    next one.
  - **Merging the strip into the name/stage row does not fit.** At its widest the strip's own ink
    already runs x7-344 of 352 on 41mm; "Agu Digitama · Digitama" needs ~140pt more.
  - Shrinking the strip itself buys nothing: with 1.0pt and 0.0pt of slack, a 9pt row fails too.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **THE MAIN SCREEN HAS NO VERTICAL BUDGET LEFT — it is at the scale boundary to the point, on
    both watch sizes.** 49.0pt and 64.0pt against a 16pt quantum. Any story that adds a row to
    `ContentView`'s VStack costs the Digimon a third (41mm) or a quarter (46mm) of its size, and no
    amount of making the row thin avoids it. Measure the slot BEFORE designing the row; the map
    band under `-mapDemo=<asset>` is the slot, exactly, and diffing it against `-mapDemo=none`
    isolates it in one command.
  - **The `?` placeholder is a free ruler.** `DigimonSpriteView.placeholder` is a stroked rounded
    rect at exactly `16 x scale` points, and a brand-new save is a Digitama whose sheet yields no
    frames, so a fresh install draws a box whose width IS the sprite scale. Far easier to measure
    than a Digimon's silhouette, and it needs no matched walk frame.
  - **The bottom 26pt/36pt of this screen is safe-area inset, not slack** — verified, not assumed.
    If a later story truly needs a line, that is where it is, and the price is the action row's
    corners.
  - Two screenshot traps bit again, both already in Codebase Patterns and both still worth the
    minutes they cost: `xcodegen generate` is needed for a NEW source file even though `Sources` is
    a glob (the build failed with "cannot find type 'MapStrip' in scope" until it was re-run), and
    the queued notification alert survived into the 46mm run in Chinese and ate a whole screenshot
    pass — `simctl erase` on the device, then `-healthAnswered`, is still the only fix.
  - `-mapStripWidestDemo` is the third mode of `seedMapListDemoIfRequested` and obeys the same two
    rules the others learned the hard way: it clears before it seeds (idempotent), and
    `-mapProgressResetDemo` is its inverse. Both containers were reset and erased after the pass.
- REMAINS: US-120 (6/56 passing, unchanged). The strip itself is finished, tested and photographed;
  what is open is a layout-budget decision that belongs to a person, not to a measurement — accept
  a one-step smaller Digimon, or free a full line first and say which of the three ways above.

## 2026-07-22 — US-120: Map strip on the main screen, and switching maps — NOW PASSING
- The previous iteration left AC4 as the only failure and framed it as a decision rather than a
  measurement: accept a one-step smaller Digimon, or free a full line first. **This iteration freed
  the line.** No change to `MapStripView`, `MainScreenModel` or the strip's own tests — the strip was
  already finished. What changed is who pays for its ~13.5pt.
- **The five trims, and why each is the cheapest point on the screen:**
  - `ContentView`'s `VStack(spacing: 1)` -> `0` — **5.0pt**, five gaps. Every row here is already a
    self-contained band of text or controls, so the gaps bought air between things that do not touch.
  - The name/stage line `12` -> `9pt` — **3.6pt**. 9 is already this screen's small size: the stats
    labels and the action row's caption are both 9. The name is also the one thing a glance does not
    need — the sprite says which Digimon it is, and a 48pt sprite says it better than a 12pt caption.
  - `StatsStrip`'s values `11` -> `9pt` — **2.4pt**. The strip's height is its tallest element and
    the values were it. They keep their semibold weight and their tint, which is what separated them
    from the labels; the size was not doing that work.
  - `ActionControls`' `.padding(.top, 2)` — **2.0pt**. The circles are 30pt discs with their own
    visual margin.
  - `EnergyBarsView`'s bar-row spacing `2` -> `1` — **1.0pt**. The hatch caption below keeps its gap;
    text against bars is the one place the separation does real work.
- Files: Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/EnergyBarsView.swift, Tests/MainScreenLayoutTests.swift.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1436 tests, with 0 failures` (1435 + 1 new), the new one also
  observed passing on its own with `-only-testing`.
- **AC4 PASSED, MEASURED — the criterion that cost two iterations.** Pre- vs post-story, both watch
  sizes, fresh install, identical script and identical launch command. The baseline is a REAL BUILD
  of `858fa43` (US-119, the last commit before the strip) made in a `git worktree` — and it
  reproduced the previous iteration's numbers to the point, 49.0pt on 41mm and 64.0pt on 46mm, which
  is what makes the comparison worth anything.
  - **SLOT: 41mm 49.0 -> 49.5pt. 46mm 64.0 -> 64.0pt.** Not smaller on either.
  - **SPRITE**, measured directly as ink on black inside the slot: 41mm **78x72px in BOTH** builds,
    the same size at a different walk offset; 46mm **104px wide in BOTH**. Scale 3 on 41mm and 4 on
    46mm before and after. (The 46mm 104 vs 96 HEIGHT is the walk1/walk2 confound — width is the
    honest signal, and 78/104 = 3/4 confirms both scales independently.)
  - The name line no longer runs through the Digimon, which is the defect the previous iteration
    photographed: sprite ink ends y221 and the name starts y233 on 41mm (6.0pt clear), y266 and y279
    on 46mm (6.5pt clear).
- **A MEASUREMENT BUG THAT NEARLY PRODUCED A FALSE PASS — in the generous direction, which is the
  dangerous one.** Diffing `-mapDemo=<asset>` against `-mapDemo=none` on "rows that differ at all"
  reported the slot as **72.0pt / 87.5pt** — a ~23pt gain from ~14pt of trims, which is what gave it
  away. `-mapDemo=none` does not only remove the map: it flips the strip to its PROMPT state (grey
  folded-map glyph for the orange walk glyph) and nudges the name row, so those two text rows differ
  for reasons that have nothing to do with the background. Fix: the map band is FULL WIDTH (344 of
  352px on 41mm) and a text row differs over at most half of it, so require **>=75% of the width**
  to differ. The band then comes out contiguous on all four shots and lands on the real numbers.
- AC7 re-verified on the new build with `-mapStripWidestDemo`, since the fonts around the strip
  moved: 41mm glyph x7-19, "Cyberpunk" x31-137, "50000" x147-202, "/" x210-216, "50000" x224-279, an
  **18.5pt clear gap**, party icon x317-343, 4.5pt right margin. Both five-digit runs are the full
  56px with no ellipsis, and "Cyberpunk" is 107px on BOTH screens, so `minimumScaleFactor(0.7)` never
  fired on the narrow one. US-115 is intact: the map band is exactly the slot on both sizes.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **The screen's vertical budget was not exhausted — it was unaudited.** The previous iteration
    priced the chrome trim at "about 14pt" and set it aside as "a screen-wide legibility regression
    bought with one row". Measured, **7 of those 14 points are pure whitespace** (five 1pt VStack
    gaps and a 2pt padding) and cost no legibility at all, and the other ~6 move two labels onto a
    size the same screen already uses in three other places. Price a trade before declining it.
  - **A demo flag's inverse is rarely a pure inverse.** `-mapDemo=none` was built as US-115's undo,
    but it also drives the strip's prompt state — so it changes two things and a diff attributes
    both to the map. When a before/after rests on one flag, check what ELSE that flag reaches.
  - **A result that beats its own arithmetic is a bug report.** +23pt from 14pt of trims was not good
    news, it was a broken measurement. The estimate was right the whole time.
  - Build the pre-story baseline in a **`git worktree`**, not a `git stash`: the two builds land in
    different DerivedData directories, so there is no copy-the-app-out-first race, and the working
    tree is never disturbed. `git worktree remove --force` when done.
- REMAINS: US-121 onward (7/56 passing). Phase B has two stories left, US-121 (map detail) and
  US-122 (opponents from the map); both consume `opponentPool` and `digitamaSlots`, which US-116
  already authored.

## 2026-07-22 — US-121: Map detail shows opponents and Digitama with progressive hints
- `Sources/MapDetailView.swift`: `MapDetail` — a pure value built from the catalog, the roster, the
  Dex and the player's counters — plus `MapDetailView`, pushed from `MapListView` with
  `navigationDestination(item:)`. `MainScreenModel` gains `discoveredDigimonIds` and
  `mapDetail(for:)`; `ConditionHintRow` in `DexView.swift` stopped being `private`.
- Files: Sources/MapDetailView.swift (new), Sources/MapListView.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift,
  Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/DexView.swift, Tests/MapDetailTests.swift (new).
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1466 tests, with 0 failures` (1436 + 30 new), and all 30 also
  observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped rather than inferred.
- **THE NAVIGATION CHANGED, and it is the one decision in this story worth a second reader.**
  US-119 made a row tap select the map and pop back. AC1 here says a tap opens the detail. Both
  cannot be a tap on the same row, so travelling moved one step deeper: the row opens the detail,
  and the detail carries a **"Travel here"** button that selects through `MapListSelector` and drops
  BOTH levels. Everything US-120 AC5 asked of a selection still holds of it — made through the
  selector, persisted, moves the US-115 background and the strip, ends on the main screen — and what
  the player gains is seeing what is in a map before committing their steps to it. `MapListSelector`
  and every US-119 test are untouched, because they were always pure functions of `(row, current)`.
  **NOT TAP-VERIFIED**: `simctl` has no tap command, so the two-level pop (`openMapId = nil` then
  `dismiss()`) is reasoned rather than photographed. If SwiftUI honours only one of the two the
  player lands on the map list, which is a degradation and not a hang.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion:
  - **AC1**, screenshotted on 46mm (`-mapDetailFoesDemo`): the pool draws **grouped**, with the
    `Child` heading between Nyaromon/Tokomon and Agumon/Patamon — grouping, not merely ordering.
    Group order is `Stage.allCases` and not `ladderIndex`, because Armor-Hybrid has no rung to sort
    on and `allCases` is already authored in ladder order with the side branch last. Within a group
    the authored order stands: that is what US-116 wrote and what US-122 will band.
  - **AC2 / AC3 / AC4 / AC5 are all on ONE 46mm screenshot** (`-mapDetailSlotsDemo`), which is what
    that flag exists for: `Agu Digitama` with its real sprite and name and **no hint rows**; a `?`
    marked `Ready to find` (sparkles, yellow) over a green-checked "Walk 2,000 steps in a day"; and
    a second `?` with an open circle beside "Fight one battle". Three states, one shot.
  - AC3 is not merely the same WORDING as the Dex's hints — the view draws them with
    **`ConditionHintRow`, the Dex's own row type**, made non-private for this. A second
    implementation could drift a word or a threshold, and the player would be reading two different
    promises about one `ConditionReveal` output.
  - AC4's "no hint rows" is enforced **on the value**: a revealed slot's `conditions` is empty, so
    there is nothing for the view to draw even if it tried. A test asserts the withheld slot beside
    it still has its own, so the emptiness is the reveal and not a slot that lost them on the way in.
  - AC5 is `!revealed && ConditionReveal.allMet` — an egg already owned is one that HAS dropped, so
    it is never "ready" however met its conditions are. Pinned against an unowned slot that IS ready
    on the same context, so the false is the ownership and not the context.
  - **AC6**: `MapDetail.make` returns **nil** for a locked row — not a stripped detail. There is
    nothing to push, the row's button is disabled as well, and a test shows the detail appearing the
    moment the lock opens on the same save, so the nil is the lock and not the fixture.
- Reveal source is the **Dex** (`GameStore.dexIds`), which is written the moment an egg is handed
  over or hatched and survives death and rebirth — exactly the span AC4's "owns or has owned" names.
  US-127's held-Digitama set will refine it; the seam is `MapDetail.make(discovered:)`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **A screenshot caught a defect no test could have.** The withheld row drew `?` twice — the art
    tile and the title — which reads as a rendering fault rather than as one withheld egg. Both were
    "correct" by every assertion in the suite. The title is now drawn only for a revealed slot.
  - **A demo flag does not have to write to the save.** All three of this story's
    (`-mapDetailDemo`, `-mapDetailSlotsDemo`, `-mapDetailFoesDemo`) seed through LITERALS — a
    `ConditionContext` and a discovery `Set` unioned at read time — so unlike US-119's there is
    nothing to undo and no `-…ResetDemo` inverse to remember. `DexModel.revealDemoContext` is the
    older example of the same trick. Prefer it: the container cannot be poisoned by something that
    never reaches disk.
  - When two screenshot flags stage the same screen at different scroll positions, the seeding must
    answer to **both** or the scrolled shot photographs an unseeded screen. `isMapDetailDemo` is one
    predicate all three flags go through, for exactly that reason.
  - To photograph that a list is GROUPED rather than merely ordered, scroll to the **first** row of
    the last group with `anchor: .bottom` — the heading lands on screen with the tail of the group
    before it. Scrolling to the last row shows three rows that could have come from anywhere.
  - The starting Digitama is **random among the graph's six**, and only three of them live in the
    starting map — so "a fresh install reveals a slot" is a coin flip, not a fact. Any screenshot
    that needs a revealed entry has to seed it.
  - `xcodebuild`'s DerivedData path for this project is not stable across runs; `find … -name
    DigiVPet.app -path "*Debug-watchsimulator*"` returns several, and the one to install is the
    NEWEST by mtime. Installing the wrong one silently photographs the previous story.
- REMAINS: US-122 onward (8/56 passing). Phase B is finished with US-122, which consumes the same
  `opponentPool` this screen now draws.
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-122: Opponents come from the map and scale with progress
- `Sources/MapOpponents.swift`: `MapOpponentBand` — the pure band arithmetic, with no generator in
  it at all — plus `BattleMatchmaker.choose(in:roster:playerId:map:recorded:using:)`. The strength
  roll moved out of the old `choose` into `BattleMatchmaker.rolled`, so the map path and the
  roster path cannot drift apart.
- Files: Sources/MapOpponents.swift (new), Sources/Battle.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift,
  Tests/MapOpponentTests.swift (new). **No existing test file was touched** — AC8's "existing
  battle tests pass unchanged" holds literally, not just in effect.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1496 tests, with 0 failures` (1466 + 30 new). All 30 new tests
  also observed passing on their own, and the 8 pre-existing `BattleMatchmakerTests` with them.

- **THE FIRST BUILD FOUND A REAL COLLISION, and it is the thing to carry forward:**
  **a map's `opponentPool` is authored and validated against the ROSTER, but `BattleMatchmaker`
  resolves against the `EvolutionGraph` — and those are not the same set.** The roster has 1025
  entries; `evolutions.json` authors 88 nodes. Resolving a pool through the graph dropped nearly
  every opponent every map names, the pool came back empty, and the code fell through to the
  roster-wide pick — US-122 doing nothing at all while its own fixture tests passed.
  - Caught ONLY because the shipped-catalog sweep asserts the drawn id is *in the map's pool*
    rather than merely "an opponent came back". `11_city_night` (ten Ultimates) drew `ogremon`.
  - Fix: `MapOpponentBand.nodes` resolves graph-node-first, and promotes a `RosterEntry` to an
    `EvolutionNode` otherwise. An opponent needs a name, a stage and a sheet; it does not need
    outgoing edges. The graph's node still wins where both exist, because it carries the `line`.
  - A promoted node carries an EMPTY `line`, which is honest: a roster-only Digimon is in no Dex
    tree. `MoveCatalog` and `ElementCatalog` both miss `lineDefaults` on it and fall through to
    their stage / keyword tiers, which is what "no line known" should produce.
  - Two element lookups in `MainScreenModel` moved from `types.type(for:in: graph)` to
    `types.type(forId:line:)` off the node already in hand — identical for an on-graph opponent,
    strictly better for an off-graph one (which the graph form would answer `.unauthored`).

- THE BAND RULE, as implemented and as measured:
  - `index(recorded:total:)` is AC2's literal quartile, pinned from BOTH sides at all three
    boundaries so an accidental `<=` fails the suite. `total <= 0` reads as the lowest band rather
    than dividing by zero.
  - The tier clamp is a rung table — t1 `2...3` (Baby II–Child) up to t5 `6...6` (Ultimate alone) —
    and it does real work: `13_factory_town` carries one Adult among its Perfects and Ultimates,
    which is dropped rather than fought at the start of a tier 4 map.
  - Within the clamped pool the four bands INTERPOLATE over the rungs the pool actually spans, so
    index 0 *is* the pool's lowest band and index 3 *is* its highest whatever it holds. A 4-rung
    pool gives a stage per band; the 2-rung shape every shipped map has splits at halfway.
  - AC4's nearest-populated fallback is tested three ways: nearer below, nearer above, and a tie —
    which breaks DOWNWARD, and that tie-break is exactly what keeps AC3's "never above it" true in
    the case where the top band itself is empty.
- AC6 IS ASSERTED AGAINST THE OLD CALL, not against a remembered list: with `map` nil the new
  signature returns the same node and the same rolled power at 50 seeds, and leaves the generator
  in the same place — so the battle that draws from it afterwards resolves identically too. That
  second half matters because `MainScreenModel` carries ONE generator through matchmaking and the
  fight.
- SHIPPED DATA verified twice over, by two implementations:
  - the test sweeps all 16 maps at 6 ratios x 5 seeds — always from the map's own pool, never above
    its tier, the band never falls as progress rises, `01_grassland` starts on Baby II and
    `12_cyberpunk` on Ultimate;
  - and a throwaway Python reimplementation of the rule read straight off `maps.json` +
    `roster.json` produces the same table map-for-map: every map steps up at halfway, tier 5 is one
    band throughout, `13_factory_town` q0 is Perfect and not its stray Adult.
- Also carried the map into the DEBUG `demoBattleSeed` search. It exists to replay exactly what
  `battle()` is about to draw, and since this story that depends on where the player is adventuring.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **`Roster` (1025) and `EvolutionGraph` (88) are DIFFERENT sets, and which one a feature resolves
    against is a design decision, not a detail.** Data authored against the roster — map pools,
    Digitama slots — cannot be looked up through the graph. Until Phase E wires the 780 orphans,
    anything that says "a Digimon" and means "any of them" must go through the roster.
  - A "did something come back?" assertion cannot catch a silent fallback. Assert what came back is
    from the set you asked about. That one line is the whole reason this story is not a false pass.
  - `EvolutionNode` is constructible from a `RosterEntry` with an empty `line`; both catalogs that
    read a line degrade gracefully through it. That is the bridge for any later story that needs a
    roster-only Digimon where a node is expected.
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-123: PlayerProfile holds what outlives a Digimon, and the existing save migrates
- `Sources/PlayerProfile.swift`: `@Model PlayerProfile` — `lifetimeEnergy`, `selectedMapId`, the
  per-map `recorded`/`finishedAt` dictionaries, and `ownedDigitamaIds` — with `MapStepCreditor`
  moved onto it. `GameStore` gains `loadOrCreateProfile(roster:)` and loses
  `loadOrCreateMapProgress`. `MapProgress` survives as a DRAIN-ONLY legacy `@Model`, still in the
  schema, read by the migration and by nothing else.
- Files: Sources/PlayerProfile.swift (new), Sources/MapProgress.swift, Sources/GameStore.swift,
  Sources/GameState.swift, Sources/EnergyLedger.swift, Sources/BattlePower.swift,
  Sources/Death.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Sources/MapListView.swift, Sources/MapStripView.swift, Sources/MapDetailView.swift,
  Sources/MapCatalog.swift, Tests/PlayerProfileTests.swift (new), Tests/Fixtures/pre-us123.store
  (new, binary), and 16 existing test files updated for the moved property.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1510 tests, with 0 failures` (1496 + 14 new), and all 14 also
  observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`.

- **THE MIGRATION IS TESTED AGAINST A FILE THE PREVIOUS BUILD WROTE, and that is the whole story.**
  AC6 says a test that constructs the NEW shape does not satisfy it — so before a line of code was
  changed, a throwaway `ZZPreUS123FixtureWriter` test was run ON THE US-122 COMMIT, writing a fully
  populated store into the Simulator's tmp. That file is now `Tests/Fixtures/pre-us123.store`
  (96KB), and it is genuinely the old shape: `sqlite3 … "select name from sqlite_master"` shows
  `ZGAMESTATE` and `ZMAPPROGRESS` and no `ZPLAYERPROFILE`. Five tests open a COPY of it (SwiftData
  migrates in place, so the bundle's copy must never be the one opened).
  - AC5 observed in full: `greymon` comes back Adult with stageEnergy 11/22/33/44, both dates, 2
    care mistakes, hunger 3, strength 17, `.sick` with its `sickSince`, a 5–6 battle record, 4
    poops and the light off — and 55/66/77/88 on a profile that did not exist when the file was
    written.
  - The fifth runs the SAME file through `MainScreenModel.start()` — the app's own path, the real
    graph and roster — and gets `.playing`, `greymon`, the same totals through `model.lifetimeEnergy`
    and the migrated `02_river` selection driving US-115's background.
- **AC3 HAS ONE DELIBERATE EXCEPTION AND IT IS WORTH A REVIEWER'S ATTENTION.** The Swift property is
  gone from `GameState`'s API — `private`, exposed only as the read-only `legacyLifetimeEnergy` the
  migration drains — but THE COLUMN STAYS. Deleting it deletes a live player's earnings with no
  second chance to read them. Renaming is no safer: opening the fixture in `sqlite3` shows SwiftData
  FLATTENS an `EnergyTotals` into one column per field named BY POSITION — `ZSTRENGTH1`,
  `ZSTRENGTH2`, `ZSTRENGTH` — not by property name, so a rename is a schema change that has to be
  exactly right for the one value nothing is allowed to lose. Four unread columns is the cheaper
  side of that trade.
- Every read in the game goes through the profile: `EnergyCreditor.credit` gained a `profile:`
  parameter and tops it up beside `stageEnergy`; `GameState.battlePower` and `memorial(displayName:)`
  now TAKE the total rather than reading it; `MainScreenModel.lifetimeEnergy` is the single place
  the "no profile yet" answer (`.zero`) is decided.
- Map progress MIGRATES rather than being dropped. `loadOrCreateProfile` adopts `MapProgress`'
  three fields and DELETES the record — asserted, including that no row is left behind. Two records
  answering "where am I adventuring" is one too many, and the one nothing writes is the one that
  loses.
- `ownedDigitamaIds` is seeded from the DEX, filtered through the roster's stages: the Dex has
  recorded every egg the moment it was handed over since US-016, so "ever owned" is a fact the old
  save already knows rather than a guess. The fixture's Dex holds `greymon` and `agu_digitama`;
  only the egg comes across. `resetGame` and `rebirth` record the egg they hand over.
- `resetGame` now wipes the profile's total EXPLICITLY (it used to fall out of deleting the state)
  and `rebirth` reads-then-restores it, so both pre-story behaviours hold with the value on its new
  home. A test pins that a rebirth keeps 111/222/333/444 AND the 900 steps already walked.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **To test a migration, write the fixture BEFORE you write the code.** One throwaway test on the
    current commit, run once, and the store harvested out of
    `~/Library/Developer/CoreSimulator/Devices/<UDID>/data/Containers/Data/Application/<uuid>/tmp/`
    (print the path from the test; it appears in the `xcodebuild` log). It costs one test run and it
    is the only artefact that can prove a migration at all. A `git worktree` build would work too,
    but is not needed if you do it first.
  - **`Tests/Fixtures/*` is bundled into the test target automatically** — xcodegen puts unknown
    file types in the resources phase, so no `project.yml` change was needed. Read it with
    `Bundle(for: Self.self).url(forResource:withExtension:)` and COPY IT OUT before opening: SwiftData
    migrates in place, so the second test to run would otherwise find it already migrated.
  - Only the `.store` needs committing. Its `-wal` came out 0 bytes (checkpointed on close) and the
    `-shm` is rebuildable; the tests pass with the two sidecars deleted from the repo.
  - **SwiftData flattens a composite attribute into one column per field, named by POSITION.**
    `EnergyTotals` becomes `ZSTRENGTH/ZVITALITY/…`, `ZSTRENGTH1/…`, `ZSTRENGTH2/…` in declaration
    order. Consequence: removing or reordering one composite is not a local change. `sqlite3
    <store> "pragma table_info(ZGAMESTATE)"` is how to look before leaping.
  - There was already a precedent for schema-migration tests in this repo and it is worth copying:
    `EnergyCreditingTests.testAStoreWrittenBeforeTheLedgerExistedStillOpens` opens a container on an
    explicit OLD `Schema([...])`, and `DominantEnergyTests.PreRecencySchema` declares a whole `@Model`
    of the previous shape inside a private enum. Both work; neither can express a property the new
    build has made private, which is why this story needed a file instead.
  - When a widely-read property moves off a `@Model`, the test churn is in the SETUP, not the
    assertions: 16 files set `state.lifetimeEnergy` to stage a scenario. Three of them
    (`FeedingTests`, `TrainingTests`, `TrainingMinigameTests`) asserted "spending does not rewrite
    the lifetime total" — a claim that is now structural, because those actions are handed the
    `GameState` alone. They were kept, on a `PlayerProfile` the action cannot reach, as the test
    that fails the day someone passes the profile in too.
- REMAINS: US-124 onward (10/56 passing). Phase C continues with US-124's multi-state store, which
  `PlayerProfile` was the precondition for.
