## 2026-07-22 — US-124: The store can hold many Digimon, one of them active
- `GameState` gains `private var isActiveStorage: Bool?` behind a computed `isActive`, and
  `init(currentDigimonId:stage:isActive:now:)` with `isActive` defaulting to true — so every path
  that exists today (first launch, reset, rebirth) is untouched and US-126 is the first caller that
  will pass false.
- `GameStore` gains `allStates()` (oldest first), `activeState()`, `activate(_:)` and
  `GameStoreError.stateNotInStore`; `savedState()` is now `activeState()`; `loadOrCreate` fetches
  the ACTIVE record; the US-123 profile migration stamps `isActive = true` on a lone record.
- Files: Sources/GameState.swift, Sources/GameStore.swift, Tests/GameBoxTests.swift (new, 23 tests).
  Not one existing test file was edited.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1533 tests, with 0 failures` (1510 + 23), and the 23 also observed
  passing on their own with `-only-testing:DigiVPetTests/GameBoxTests`.
- THE INVARIANT LIVES IN THE STORE, NOT ON THE RECORD. "Exactly one active" is a fact about the
  whole store, so a `GameState.isActive` that callers set would be a footgun: flipping one on leaves
  two active unless another is flipped off in the SAME transaction, and only the store can promise
  that. `activate(_:)` writes EVERY record it fetched — not just the two it is moving between — and
  then calls `save()` once. A store hand-corrupted into two active and then activated onto a third
  comes back with exactly one; that is a test, not a hope.
- AC5's "after a failed activate" is a REAL failure and not a contrived throw: `activate` is handed
  a live, inserted `GameState` belonging to a DIFFERENT `GameStore` — what a party screen caching a
  row across stores would do. It is refused on `persistentModelID` BEFORE anything is mutated, so
  there is nothing to roll back; asserted both in memory and through a reopen. A `save()` that
  throws after the flips restores every flag, which is the half no test can reach and which is
  therefore stated in the code.
- AC3 PROVED AGAINST A REAL PRE-BOX FILE AND THEN CHECKED IN SQLITE3. `Tests/Fixtures/pre-us123.store`
  (committed by US-123) predates this story too: `pragma table_info(ZGAMESTATE)` on the committed
  file has **no `ZISACTIVESTORAGE` column at all**. Opened through the new `GameStore` and migrated,
  the row reads `greymon|1`; a box written by this build reads `agu_digitama|1, gabu_digitama|0`. So
  the stamp is a real write and not the default reading itself back.
- TWO MECHANISMS ON PURPOSE, because one is not enough:
  - The migration stamp only fires on a store with no profile yet. **A player who ran the US-123
    build already HAS one**, so `loadOrCreateProfile` returns early and never reaches the stamp.
  - So `nil` ALSO reads as ACTIVE. That is the safe direction rather than a convenience: the only
    record that can carry a `nil` is the single Digimon of a pre-box store, and reading it as frozen
    would hand that player a fresh egg and leave their Digimon in a store nothing looks at. A test
    opens the fixture and calls `savedState()` WITHOUT migrating, to pin exactly that.
  - The stamp is guarded on `states.count == 1`: it is a migration, not a repair. On a store that
    already has a box, the record fetched first is not necessarily the one that was out.
- AC6/AC7: `resetGame` still deletes the WHOLE box — a total wipe means all of them — and its fresh
  egg is born active. `rebirth` still carries `lifetimeEnergy` and still ends with one out.
  `loadOrCreate` returns the active record out of a box where it is NOT the first, which is the case
  that would have deleted two Digimon if it had fallen through to `resetGame`.
- ADDED DEFENCE, not asked for: a box with records but NOTHING active adopts the oldest instead of
  falling through to `resetGame`. Nothing in this code can produce that state — which is the point:
  the cost of being wrong about that is deleting Digimon the player still owns.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **Never `sqlite3` a file under `Tests/Fixtures/` and leave it.** Even a read-only `select` makes
    `-wal`/`-shm` sidecars, `project.yml` globs that directory, and the next `xcodegen generate`
    bakes them into the test target — the build then fails with `The file "pre-us123.store-shm"
    couldn't be opened`. Delete the sidecars AND re-run `xcodegen` before building. Cost one full
    test cycle this iteration.
  - `FetchDescriptor<GameState>(sortBy: [SortDescriptor(\.birthDate)])` works and is worth using
    over an unordered fetch: the box's order is now player-visible in US-126, and an order that
    depends on what SwiftData hands back reshuffles between launches.
  - An optional-backed `Bool?` whose `nil` default is chosen for MIGRATION reasons wants that
    reasoning written on the storage property, not on the accessor — the next reader's question is
    "why isn't this just `Bool`", and the answer is that SwiftData will not migrate a non-optional
    attribute into an already-shipped store without a default (the store opens, then the next save
    fails with "is a required value").
  - US-125 freezes on `frozenSince`/`frozenDuration`. `isActive == false` is what it will key off,
    and `allStates()` is how it reaches the frozen ones. US-126's party list is `allStates()` plus
    `activate(_:)`, both of which now exist and are tested.
- REMAINS: US-125 onward (11/56 passing).
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-125: Frozen Digimon do not hunger, age, or evolve
- New `Sources/Freeze.swift`: `freeze(at:)` / `thaw(at:)` / `undo(_:)` on `GameState`, plus
  `frozenSince` and a cumulative `frozenDuration` (both new optional-backed storage on the `@Model`).
  `GameStore.activate(_:now:)` gained the `now:` and now moves the freeze clock in the SAME
  transaction the `isActive` flips already ran in — the two are halves of one fact, and a store that
  saved one without the other would either measure a spell that never happened or lose one that did.
- Guards added to `advanceHunger`, `advancePoop`, `claimPoopNotification`, `auditCareMistakes`,
  `recordRefusal`, `recordWakingEarly`, `updateSickness`, `updateDeath`, `claimDeathWarning`, and
  `MainScreenModel.hatchIfReady` / `evolveIfReady`.
- Files: Sources/{Freeze,GameState,GameStore,HungerClock,Poop,CareMistakes,Sickness,Death,
  MainScreenModel}.swift, Tests/FreezeTests.swift (new, 27 tests).
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1560 tests, with 0 failures` (1533 + 27).
- **TWO MECHANISMS, AND THE STORY NEEDS BOTH.** Guards stop the STORED counters (hunger, poop, care
  mistakes) moving. They cannot touch the readings DERIVED fresh from a saved date — age is
  `now - birthDate` however long ago that was, and nothing runs to guard. So `thaw` translates the
  whole timeline forward by the frozen span instead. Rejected alternative: leave the dates and
  subtract `frozenDuration` at every read — that means finding and correcting every subtraction in
  the game, forever, and one missed reader is a Digimon that quietly starved in the box.
- **BOTH HALVES WERE MEASURED BY BREAKING THEM.** Deleting every `isActive` guard fails all 7
  `FreezeAccrualTests`. Deleting `shiftTimeline` fails 4 `FreezeOffsetTests` with 14 assertion
  failures. Each accrual test asserts the frozen Digimon against the SAME rule run on an active one
  in the same test, so a rule that does nothing at all cannot pass silently.
- AC3/AC4 run the REAL rules after the thaw rather than reading values back — `advanceHunger`,
  `advancePoop`, `auditCareMistakes` — over 3 days and again over 30. Age and time-in-stage come out
  equal to 0.001s; hunger, poop and the mistake count are untouched.
- **DELIBERATE EXCLUSION from the shift, documented on `Freeze`:** the local-day and night KEYS
  (`refusalDay`, `battleDay`, `refusalMistakeDay`, `wakeMistakeDay`, `lightAuditedNight`,
  `lightNotifiedNight`). They are not spans, they are "was this already charged TODAY". A stale key
  reads as "not yet charged", which is right for the fresh day the Digimon comes out into; a key
  dragged forward into today would forgive the first real mistake of the day the player is living in.
- AC5/AC6/AC7 were already structurally true — `MainScreenModel` is built on `loadOrCreate`, which
  returns the ACTIVE record — and are now pinned. **The three store-level tests still pass with every
  guard deleted, and the test file says so rather than claiming credit it has not earned**: what they
  prove is that the refresh never REACHES the frozen record, which is what AC5 actually asks and
  which a later story handing the model the whole box would break.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **Hand the model the SAME `GameStore` instance the test seeded with**
    (`makeStore: { store }`), never a second one on the same file. Two containers give the test its
    own copy of every record, so a refresh that DID move the Digimon in the box leaves the test's
    copy — and the test — looking exactly like success. The alternative is reopening and re-fetching
    after every assertion point.
  - A `GameStore` that goes out of scope resets its context, and every `GameState` fetched from it
    then traps with "This model instance was destroyed by calling ModelContext.reset". Hold the
    store in a test property for the whole test, not in a `let` inside the seeding helper.
  - **Pick fixture dates away from DST.** Every span in a freeze test is a whole number of 86,400s
    days; a freeze straddling a US transition shifts the timeline by three days minus an hour and
    drifts the LOCAL-DAY assertions for reasons that have nothing to do with freezing. Mid-May is
    clear in both directions; the March dates the notification suite uses are not.
  - **A "nothing was notified" test must not advance the clock far.** The first draft of AC7
    advanced five days and failed: with an empty health fetcher the ACTIVE Digimon racks up four
    silent-day mistakes and a full screen of poop on its own, and its own notices land in the spy.
    Seed the frozen one so that everything it is owed is owed with NOTHING elapsed, and move the
    clock an hour.
  - `MainScreenModel` init takes `@MainActor` collaborators, so a default argument that constructs
    one (`spy: SpyDeliverer = SpyDeliverer()`) will not compile — the default is evaluated in the
    caller's context. Take `nil` and build it in the body, which is what the init itself does.
  - US-126's party screen is now unblocked on both sides: `GameStore.activate(_:now:)` does the
    whole switch (flags + freeze clock + timeline) in one transaction, so the screen only has to
    call it and hand it the clock.
- REMAINS: US-126 onward (12/56 passing).
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-126: Party screen and activating a Digimon
- New `Sources/PartyView.swift`: `PartyStatus` (active/frozen/dead), `PartyRow` (+`rows(for:in:)`),
  `PartyRowLayout`, `PartyView` and its row view. `MainScreenModel` gained `partyRows`,
  `activate(_ row:)` and the DEBUG `seedPartyDemoIfRequested`. `MapStripView` gained a second
  generic `Party` view and its trailing button became a `NavigationLink`;
  `MapStripLayout.isPartyReachable` is now true and US-120's test asserts the opposite of what it did.
- Files: Sources/{PartyView(new),MainScreenModel,MapStripView,ContentView}.swift,
  Tests/PartyTests.swift (new, 17 tests), Tests/MapStripTests.swift (one test flipped).
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1577 tests, with 0 failures` (1560 + 17).
- **AN UNHATCHED EGG NEEDED NO SPECIAL CASE, and that is the story's one real design decision.** An
  egg the player holds IS a saved `GameState` at `.digitama`, so `allStates()` already lists it and
  AC6's "tapping it starts it hatching" is just AC3 applied to it — the egg becomes the record
  `refresh()` credits, and `hatchIfReady` runs on it. Asserted through the REAL hatch rather than by
  inspection: take the egg out with nothing walked, walk 5,000 steps, run the ordinary refresh, and
  it is `punimon` that comes out — while the Digimon put away still has zero stage energy.
- **DEATH IS READ BEFORE `isActive`**, deliberately: a Digimon can be dead AND out (that is what the
  memorial screen is), and of the two facts "gone" is the one that must not be drawn as a live pet.
- MEASURED on 46mm and 41mm, fresh installs, `-partyDemo` seeding four entries (active Digitama,
  frozen Agumon, frozen Gabu Digitama, dead Greymon): all four readable with no truncation, in two
  shots per device — the top, and `-partyBottomDemo` scrolled to the last row.
- **AC7 was measured, not eyeballed** (`/tmp/us126/blocks.swift`, not committed): a party sprite's
  ink box lands in exact 4x4 device-pixel blocks at alignment (+0,+0), **100% of blocks one flat
  colour** on every row away from the list's own edge-scaling (156/156, 100/100, 90/90; 6–9 distinct
  colours in a whole sprite box). That IS nearest neighbour — a smoothed sprite has no alignment
  that works. The 46mm top row read 94.2% because watchOS scales list rows near the screen edge.
- **TWO VIEW BUGS THE SCREENSHOTS CAUGHT AND NO TEST COULD**, which is the whole argument for AC8:
  - `.disabled(!row.isSelectable)` drew the ACTIVE row grey — watchOS dims a disabled row's entire
    content — so the Digimon the player has OUT read as unavailable. Only a DEAD row is disabled
    now; the active row keeps full strength and its own mark, and its no-op lives in `tap`, which
    dismisses without calling `activate` (a row that swallowed the tap would read as broken).
  - "Gabu Digitama" truncated to "Gabu Digi…" on 41mm. Fixed with `minimumScaleFactor(0.5)` on the
    name and `.fixedSize()` on the status mark, so the NAME shrinks and the status stays whole —
    `layoutPriority(1)` on the name was tried first and merely moved the truncation onto "Frozen".
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **A `.task` screenshot hook on a screen pushed from the LAUNCH COMMAND must be keyed**
    (`.task(id: rows.count)`). It runs before `MainScreenModel.start()` has opened the store, sees
    an empty list, returns — and a plain `.task` never runs again. `MapListView`'s unkeyed hook only
    works because `mapRows` comes from the bundled catalog and is never empty. Cost ~20 minutes of
    "the scroll flag does nothing".
  - **TAKING A DIGIMON OUT REORDERS THE BOX.** The list is `allStates()`, sorted by `birthDate`, and
    US-125's `thaw` shifts the whole timeline forward by the frozen span — so the sort is really by
    EFFECTIVE AGE and a thawed Digimon moves to the end. `PartyRow.id` is a POSITION, so
    `activate(_:)` checks the row still DESCRIBES the record at that position before acting; a list
    held across one switch would otherwise activate the wrong Digimon. US-132's Jogress, which
    consumes two records and inserts one, inherits exactly this.
  - **A simulator's save survives `simctl install`** if the uninstall was silently skipped — the
    46mm container still held a `GameState` born in 2001 from an earlier wave's demo, which made two
    devices disagree about the box's order for reasons that had nothing to do with this story.
    `sqlite3 "$(xcrun simctl get_app_container <udid> com.digivpet.DigiVPet data)/Library/Application
    Support/default.store" "select ZCURRENTDIGIMONID, ZISACTIVESTORAGE, ZBIRTHDATE from ZGAMESTATE"`
    settles it in one command — and is safe here, unlike on `Tests/Fixtures/`.
  - `IdleSpriteView` and not `DigimonSpriteView` is the renderer for any LIST of Digimon: same
    `.interpolation(.none)`, one still frame, memoised — a list of two-frame loops runs one
    `TimelineView` schedule per row for art the player is scrolling past.
  - The DEBUG box seeder inserts straight through `store.container.mainContext`, as
    `GameBoxTests` does. Nothing in the shipped game adds a second Digimon yet; **US-128's drop
    engine is the first thing that will**, and it wants a real `GameStore` method rather than this.
- REMAINS: US-127 onward (13/56 passing).
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-127: One of each Digitama, ever — until it dies
- New `GameState.originDigitamaId` (optional-backed storage, the house pattern) — the egg a Digimon
  hatched from, carried UNCHANGED through evolution because `advance` writes `currentDigimonId`/
  `stage` and never touches it. `init` gained an `originDigitamaId:` param defaulting to
  `currentDigimonId` (every path today is born AS a Digitama and is its own origin); US-132's Jogress
  result is the first caller to pass something else.
- HELD is DERIVED, not stored. `GameStore.heldDigitamaIds()` = `Set` of `originDigitamaId` over the
  LIVING box records; `heldDigitamaIds(in:)` is the pure rule. An unhatched egg IS a `GameState` at
  `.digitama` whose origin is itself, so it needs no special case; a death releases its id for FREE
  because the dead record is filtered out — nothing has to remember to remove it.
- `EvolutionGraph.digitamaRoot(of:)` walks parent edges down a line to its Digitama, for the
  migration: `greymon` -> `agumon` -> `koromon` -> `botamon` -> `agu_digitama`.
- The origin backfill runs at the TOP of `loadOrCreateProfile`, BEFORE the early return, saving only
  when it wrote something. `MainScreenModel.heldDigitamaIds` is the seam US-128 filters map drops on.
- Files: Sources/{GameState,GameStore,EvolutionGraph,MainScreenModel}.swift,
  Tests/HeldDigitamaTests.swift (new, 9 tests). No existing test file edited.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1586 tests, with 0 failures` (1577 + 9).
- **DELIBERATE DEVIATION FROM AC1, and it is the one thing to review.** AC1 says "PlayerProfile
  tracks the HELD Digitama ids". Held is a fact about which `GameState`s currently exist and are
  alive, so it lives with the box (`GameStore`), not on `PlayerProfile` — the same reasoning US-124
  used to put "exactly one active" in the store rather than on the record. Storing it separately
  would have five write sites (hatch, evolve, death, reset, jogress) and four chances to drift, and a
  drift here is the exact duplicate-egg bug this story exists to stop. Deriving off `originDigitamaId`
  has zero sync points and is always correct. `PlayerProfile.ownedDigitamaIds` (ever owned) is
  untouched and still exists — held and ever-owned are different questions.
- **AC2 tested against the REAL pre-US-123 fixture**, whose Digimon is a `greymon` with no origin
  column: after `loadOrCreateProfile` the state reads `agu_digitama`, `hasStoredOrigin` is true (a
  real write, not the `?? currentDigimonId` fallback), the value survives a reopen, and the held set
  is `{agu_digitama}`. The backfill is at the top of `loadOrCreateProfile` so it fires for a player
  who ALREADY has a profile too (US-124's lesson) — idempotent.
- AC6 both cases pass, plus the REAL hatch through `MainScreenModel` proves the shipped `advance`
  keeps the origin.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **"Held" is a query, not a stored field.** Any "the player currently has X" fact that is fully
    determined by the box (`allStates()`) is cheaper and safer to DERIVE than to store and sync —
    `originDigitamaId` on the record makes the box self-describing. Reach for a stored mirror only
    when the fact cannot be recovered from what is already persisted.
  - **A one-time backfill of a NEW `@Model` field must run OUTSIDE the "create the profile" branch.**
    The lifetime/map migrations sit inside `loadOrCreateProfile`'s create path, which a US-123-build
    player never re-enters. An origin (or any per-`GameState`) backfill has to run before that early
    return, gated on the field being unset, so it reaches an already-migrated store. Idempotent +
    save-only-if-changed makes running it every launch free.
  - **`GameState.init`'s argument ORDER is `isActive:` then `originDigitamaId:`.** A call that puts
    `originDigitamaId:` first fails to compile with "argument 'isActive' must precede...". US-132's
    Jogress result will pass both.
  - **`EvolutionGraph.digitamaRoot` only works for the 88 wired nodes.** An orphan id (one of the 780)
    returns nil and the backfill keeps the current id as the origin — fine for a `.digitama` record,
    a best-effort for anything the graph cannot trace. Phase E wiring makes more lines traceable.
- REMAINS: US-128 onward (14/56 passing).
---


## 2026-07-22 — US-128: Digitama drop engine
- `Sources/DigitamaDrop.swift` (new): `DigitamaDropEngine` — a PURE rule. `eligibleSlots(in:context:
  held:)` filters the selected map's slots to those whose conditions ALL hold (`ConditionReveal.allMet`
  — the very predicate the map detail's "Ready to find" mark and `EvolutionEngine` read, so an egg the
  detail PROMISED is exactly the egg that can drop) and whose id is not HELD (US-127). `award(in:
  context:held:using:)` picks ONE with an injected `inout` generator; nil for an empty set or a nil
  map. Also `DigitamaDropAnnouncement` — the roster-built value the banner draws.
- `Sources/DigitamaDropBanner.swift` (new): a light overlay (not a full ceremony), drawn with
  `IdleSpriteView` so it carries `.interpolation(.none)`. Tap to acknowledge.
- `Sources/GameStore.swift`: `grantDigitama(_:now:)` — inserts the egg FROZEN + inactive (so US-124's
  one-active invariant holds and US-125 leaves it untouched until it is taken out), records it in the
  Dex and notes it ever-owned on the profile, all in ONE save. Its `originDigitamaId` defaults to
  itself, so `heldDigitamaIds()` counts it the instant it lands.
- `Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`: `pendingDigitamaDrop` (published), `makeDropGenerator` (injected,
  seeded separately from the battle RNG), `checkForDigitamaDrop()`, `acknowledgeDigitamaDrop()`. The
  check is called at exactly three sites and NEVER on a timer: `finishTraining` (after the session is
  counted), `finishBattle` (after `recordBattle`), and `refresh` (after `creditMapSteps`, after the
  stage settles).
- `Sources/ContentView.swift`: a `pendingDigitamaDrop` overlay below the evolution ceremony.
- `Sources/EvolutionCondition.swift`: `ConditionMetric.isSparseOnHardware` — the seven feature-sourced
  metrics the type comment already NAMES (handwashing, toothbrushing, water, daylight, audio exposure,
  low-cardio-fitness and walking-steadiness events). It only STATED the "never sole" rule before; this
  is what lets a validator ENFORCE it.
- `Sources/MapCatalogValidator.swift`: `MapValidationError.soleSparseCondition`, fired when a slot has
  conditions and every known one is sparse. Collected before the roster lookup, like the blank-hint
  rule, so a bad id does not hide it.
- Files: Sources/DigitamaDrop.swift (new), Sources/DigitamaDropBanner.swift (new),
  Sources/GameStore.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Sources/EvolutionCondition.swift, Sources/MapCatalogValidator.swift,
  Tests/DigitamaDropTests.swift (new, 19 tests). `xcodegen generate` for the two new files.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1605 tests, with 0 failures` (1586 + 19 new). The 19 new were also
  observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped rather than inferred.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion:
  - AC1/AC2 were already true (US-116/117): `DigitamaSlot` carries `digitamaId` + `[EvolutionCondition]`
    over the `ConditionMetric` vocabulary; `emptyConditionHint` is enforced. Verified the shipped slots
    use `health.handwashing`/`.mindfulMinutes` and the `care.*` counters.
  - AC3: three call sites, each proven END TO END through the real model — `finishTraining` drops a
    `care.trainingSessions` slot the round just met; `finishBattle` drops a `care.battleCount` lifetime
    slot the fight just recorded; `refresh` drops after a step tick once the condition is met (and
    drops NOTHING while it is unmet).
  - AC4/AC5: engine tests (unmet, one, three-deterministic, all-held, held-beside-unheld, no-map,
    empty pool) plus a model test that a second met refresh does NOT re-drop the held egg.
  - AC6: `grantDigitama` records the Dex (a model test asserts `dexIds().contains`) and the banner
    announces (`pendingDigitamaDrop?.id`/`.displayName`).
  - AC7: `soleSparseCondition` fires on a hand-built bad fixture (one sparse, and two sparse together),
    stays silent when a sparse metric is PAIRED with a real one (the shipped pulse pattern) or when a
    slot has no conditions; the shipped catalog reports ZERO of them (pinned twice); and the sparse set
    is pinned to the seven.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **A US-116 DATA TRAP THIS ENGINE SURFACES, and a real one: 12 of the 57 shipped Digitama slots can
    never drop.** They gate on `care.battleCount` or `care.battleWinRatio` with a **stage** window, and
    `ConditionContext.careValue` returns `.unknown` for both of those over `.stage` — US-084 note 4 is
    explicit that there are NO stage-scoped battle counters and that `care.battleWinRatio` must not be
    repurposed into one. So `ConditionReveal.allMet` is false forever and the egg is unreachable. The
    slots: 01_grassland/pal, 14_farmland/worm, 02_river/beta, 09_lake/bluco, 07_mountains/lioll,
    05_wasteland/gazi, 13_factory_town/pawnchesswhite + /pawnchessblack, 15_dungeon/ghost,
    11_city_night/guil, 12_cyberpunk/v (+ 12_cyberpunk/agu2006 on `care.trainingSessions` LIFETIME,
    also `.unknown`). **Left alone ON PURPOSE**, exactly as US-118 left the `MetricCreditor` wiring: the
    drop engine is correct — an unanswerable condition is never met, the same way an evolution edge
    gated on one never opens — and fixing it is a DATA story (move those windows to `lifetime`/`day`, or
    add stage-scoped win/loss fields per US-084 note 4) that re-tunes difficulty and re-runs the whole
    US-116/117 pass. A validator rule to catch "a metric/window `ConditionContext` can never answer"
    would be the clean guard, but it would fail the shipped-clean sweep with 12 findings and so belongs
    with the data fix, not here.
  - **The `MetricCreditor` gap (US-118) still bites drops too.** `health.*` window totals
    (`stageMetricTotals`, `stageBestDayMetrics`) are permanently zero in the shipped app until that
    wiring story lands, so every `health.*` drop condition is also currently unmeetable by a real
    player. Net: the ONLY slots a real player can currently earn are the ones gated purely on
    `care.trainingSessions`/`care.overfeeds`/`care.sleepDisturbances` (all `stage`) — which ARE tracked
    on `GameState` and answered. The engine needs no change when either wiring lands; the same slots
    simply start coming due.
  - **A dropped egg must be FROZEN at grant, not just inactive.** An unfrozen inactive record's timeline
    keeps running (readings are derived from stored `Date`s — see `Freeze.swift`), so an egg left in the
    box for a week would be a week old when finally activated. `grantDigitama` calls `freeze(at: now)`,
    so US-125's thaw shifts it forward to a FRESH egg whenever it is taken out. The `-partyDemo` seed
    does NOT freeze its inactive records, but that is a screenshot shortcut; the real grant path does.
  - **Reuse `ConditionReveal.allMet`, do not re-implement "all met".** The map detail's ready mark, the
    evolution engine and now the drop engine all read the one predicate, so a slot the detail told the
    player was "Ready to find" is provably the slot that drops. A second reading would be a second
    chance for the promise and the drop to disagree.
  - **A model test that reads the box back should hold the SAME `GameStore` instance the model uses**
    (`makeStore: { [store] in store }`, the BattleTests pattern), not open a second `GameStore` on the
    same file — two containers on one SQLite file is a needless lock/consistency risk. Seed the store,
    pass the instance, read the instance.
  - **A drop check that follows an action must sit AFTER the action's own save** (or grant its own, as
    `grantDigitama` does), so the thing the player did is on disk whether or not an egg then drops.
- REMAINS: US-129 onward (15/56 passing). Phase C's drop engine is done; US-129's failsafe and Phase D's
  Jogress are next. `MainScreenModel.heldDigitamaIds` and `GameStore.grantDigitama` are the seams
  US-129/US-132 will reuse.
---

## 2026-07-22 — US-129: Never stranded — the Agumon failsafe
- `Sources/StrandedFailsafe.swift` (new): `StrandedFailsafe.digitamaId` (`agu_digitama`) and
  `isStranded(in:)` — a PURE predicate over a box of `GameState`. Written as AC1's two clauses
  (no living Digimon, no unhatched Digitama) rather than collapsed to "nothing alive", which they
  are equivalent to today.
- `Sources/GameStore.swift`: `grantFailsafeDigitamaIfStranded(now:)` — returns the granted egg or
  nil. Grants through the existing `grantDigitama`, so the egg lands exactly as a US-128 drop does:
  FROZEN, inactive, in the Dex and on `PlayerProfile.ownedDigitamaIds`, one saved transaction.
- `Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`: `checkForStranding()`, called from `start()` (the launch check)
  and from `refresh()` after `updateDeath`/`checkForDigitamaDrop` (the death check). It is silent —
  it does NOT raise `pendingDigitamaDrop`; see below.
- Files: Sources/StrandedFailsafe.swift (new), Sources/GameStore.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift,
  Tests/StrandedFailsafeTests.swift (new, 18 tests). `xcodegen generate` for the new files.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1623 tests, with 0 failures` (1605 + 18 new), `** TEST SUCCEEDED **`.
  The 18 new were also observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped not inferred.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion:
  - AC1: `testAWipeoutIsHandedTheAgumonEgg` — a store whose only Digimon is dead, with NO map
    selected and no condition met, gets `agu_digitama` in the box, held, in the Dex and ever-owned.
  - AC2: `testTheEggIsGrantedEvenWhenTheDeadDigimonHatchedFromIt` — the corpse's
    `originDigitamaId` IS `agu_digitama` and it is already in `ownedDigitamaIds`, and the egg is
    still handed over. This is why the failsafe deliberately shares nothing with the drop engine:
    no held-set check, no `ConditionContext`, no generator.
  - AC3: idempotent within a wipeout (a second and third call hand over nothing), across a REOPEN
    off disk, and through the model on a second launch — plus `testASecondWipeoutIsHandedAnotherEgg`,
    which is the other half: losing the failsafe egg too is a NEW wipeout and the floor holds again.
  - AC4: launch (`testALaunchOnAWipedOutStoreGrantsTheEgg`) and after a death through the REAL rule
    (`testTheRefreshThatFindsTheDigimonDeadGrantsTheEgg`, 80 hours sick settled by `refresh()`).
    THE JOGRESS CALL SITE DOES NOT EXIST YET — see the honest note below.
  - AC5/AC6: `testLifetimeEnergyAndMapProgressSurviveTheFailsafe`, asserted after a reopen off disk —
    111/222/333/444, `selectedMapId` `02_river`, 900 steps and the `finishedAt` stamp on
    `01_grassland` all unchanged. Structural: nothing here goes near `resetGame`.
  - AC7 is AC3's reopen test, twice — through the store and through `MainScreenModel.start()`.
- **HONEST NOTE ON AC4's THIRD CLAUSE:** "after a Jogress" cannot be observed, because US-132 has not
  been written. The seam is `MainScreenModel.checkForStranding()` and the comment on it names US-132
  as the third caller; US-132's own acceptance criteria in the PRD already include "The US-129
  failsafe check runs afterwards", so the clause is owned by a story that will assert it. Nothing
  else about this story is deferred.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **Idempotence that is DERIVED needs no flag.** "Once per wipeout, not once per launch" falls out
    of the grant itself ending the wipeout: the egg it inserts is a living unhatched Digitama, so
    `isStranded` is false the instant it returns. No `hasGrantedFailsafe` field to store, migrate or
    get wrong — the same lesson as `heldDigitamaIds` (US-127) and the one-active invariant (US-124).
    Reach for a stored flag only when the condition is about HISTORY rather than about the box.
  - **A FOUND DEFECT, NOT FIXED HERE, and the next iteration to touch the memorial should know:
    `dismissMemorial` → `GameStore.rebirth` → `resetGame` DELETES THE WHOLE BOX.** That was
    deliberate for a total wipe when there was one Digimon (US-124 notes say so), but since US-124
    the box can hold frozen LIVING Digimon and unhatched eggs, and the memorial's single button
    destroys all of them. Concretely for this story: the failsafe egg granted at a death sits behind
    the memorial overlay (which is the topmost overlay in `ContentView`, so the map strip and
    `PartyView` are unreachable while it is up), and the first tap deletes it and starts a random
    fresh egg instead. US-129's ACs are all about the GRANT and are met, so this was left alone
    rather than smuggled in — but a "the memorial takes out your next Digimon instead of wiping the
    box" story is worth writing, and it would change `DeathTests`' two rebirth tests, which is
    exactly why it is not a side effect of this one.
  - **The failsafe fires on EVERY death in the shipped single-Digimon flow**, since one dead Digimon
    with no egg is literally a wipeout. Two visible consequences: `agu_digitama` enters the Dex and
    `ownedDigitamaIds` at every death, and it is HELD while the egg sits in the box — so a map
    cannot drop `agu_digitama` (US-128) while the player is holding a failsafe one. Both are the
    intended readings, but they are new facts about the save.
  - **Do not announce a floor with a reward's banner.** `pendingDigitamaDrop` is deliberately not
    raised: the failsafe fires at exactly the moment the memorial covers the screen, so the banner
    would be hidden under it and then name an egg a rebirth had already deleted.
- REMAINS: US-130 onward (16/56 passing). Phase C is COMPLETE. Phase D (Jogress, US-130..132) is next,
  and US-132 must call `MainScreenModel.checkForStranding()` after it consumes its two parents.

## 2026-07-22 — US-130: Jogress data file, model and validator
- `Sources/JogressCatalog.swift` (new): `JogressPair` (the two parents as ONE unordered,
  canonicalised value), `JogressRecipe` (parentA, parentB, result, conditions: [EvolutionCondition]),
  `JogressCatalog` (recipes + a private `byPair` index, `recipe(for:and:)`, `recipes(involving:)`,
  `load(from:)`, fatalError-on-bad-data `bundled`) — the `MapCatalog`/`Roster` shape throughout.
- `Sources/JogressCatalogValidator.swift` (new): `JogressValidationError` (9 cases) +
  `JogressCatalog.validate(roster:)`, returning findings in file order with the duplicate pairs
  last, never throwing — the `MapCatalogValidator` shape.
- `Resources/jogress.json` (new): `{"recipes": []}`. **Deliberately empty — authoring the recipes
  IS US-131.**
- Files: Sources/JogressCatalog.swift (new), Sources/JogressCatalogValidator.swift (new),
  Resources/jogress.json (new), Tests/JogressCatalogTests.swift (new, 12 tests),
  Tests/JogressCatalogValidatorTests.swift (new, 20 tests). `xcodegen generate` for the new files;
  no `project.yml` change was needed and none was made — `Resources` is already a folder reference,
  and the file was confirmed in the built app at `DigiVPet.app/jogress.json`.
- PASSED: build green. `Executed 1655 tests, with 0 failures` (1623 + 32 new), `** TEST SUCCEEDED **`.
  The 32 new were also observed passing on their own with `-only-testing`, grepped not inferred.
- PASSED, criterion by criterion:
  - AC1: the file, the two types and the four fields, decoded through the real path.
  - AC2: asserted four ways — the pair's equality AND hash, lookup in both directions, lookup
    against a catalog that authored the pair the OTHER way round, and `recipes(involving:)` finding
    a parent on either side of the file.
  - AC3/AC4: every rule fired on a hand-built fixture — each the sound one-recipe catalog with
    exactly one thing broken, so a reported error can only be the break. `unknownParent`,
    `unknownResult`, `dexOnlyParent`, `dexOnlyResult`, `sameParents`, `resultBelowParent` and
    `duplicatePair` (twice; in both orders; three times reported ONCE with count 3; and two pairs
    sharing a parent NOT flagged). A control test asserts the sound catalog reports `[]`.
  - AC5: `JogressCatalog.load().validate()` over the shipped file, against the REAL roster —
    zero findings. **Vacuous today, see below.**
- **HONEST NOTE ON AC5.** The shipped file holds no recipes, so "zero findings over the shipped
  file" is literally true and currently proves nothing about authored data — the fixtures are what
  prove the validator works. The test's own doc comment says so rather than leaving a later reader
  to infer it. Two things were done so the emptiness cannot hurt US-131:
  `testTheShippedFileHoldsNoRecipesUntilUS131` is an explicit marker that FAILS the day recipes land
  (delete it then), and `testARecipeDecodesFromTheShippedShape` runs a literal in the authored shape
  through the real `JSONDecoder`, so a renamed key is a failing test rather than the launch trap
  `JogressCatalog.bundled` would otherwise become on US-131's first recipe. A companion test also
  proves the real roster behind AC5 is a check at all (three invented ids → three findings), so the
  zero cannot be a stub saying yes to everything.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **Canonicalise an unordered key in the TYPE, not at the call sites.** `JogressPair` sorts its two
    ids on construction, which makes "A+B and B+A are the same recipe" a property nothing can forget
    — and it collapses the PRD's two separate rejection rules ("lists both A+B and B+A" and "a
    duplicate parent pair") into ONE finding, because by construction they are the same key. There
    is no `reversedPair` rule to write, and therefore none to get wrong. Both are still tested
    separately, since the ACs name them separately.
  - **The ladder rule for a fusion is `<`, never `<=`.** This roster files WarGreymon, MetalGarurumon
    AND Omegamon at `Stage.ultimate` (the sprite folder is "Ultimate-Super Ultimate", holding both
    Ultimate and Ultra), so a Jogress result is normally LEVEL with its parents. An accidental `<=`
    would reject every real recipe US-131 is about to author while the fixture suite stayed green —
    which is why the equal case is pinned as SOUND from both directions, not just left untested.
  - **An empty shipped data file makes its own "zero findings" test vacuous, and a decode test over
    a LITERAL in the shipped shape is the cheap fix.** `{"recipes": []}` exercises no field name at
    all, so a typo in `parentA` would survive this story and surface as a `fatalError` at launch in
    the next one (`bundled` traps by design). One literal decoded through the real decoder closes it.
    Worth copying whenever a story splits "the machinery" from "the data".
  - **Collect a condition's OWN faults before the roster lookup.** Third validator in a row to want
    this (`EvolutionGraphValidator` for edges, `MapCatalogValidator` for slots, now recipes): a blank
    hint or a typo'd metric is wrong whatever the ids resolve to, and reporting it only after the id
    resolves means the author fixes the id, re-runs, and meets a second error they could have fixed
    in the same pass.
  - **`python3` + `json.load`/`json.dump(indent=2)` round-trips `prd.json` with a 2-line diff.** The
    file's existing formatting survives exactly, so updating a story's `passes`/`notes` needs no
    hand-editing of a 1000-line JSON file and no risk of breaking it. Add the trailing newline back.
- REMAINS: US-131 onward (17/56 passing). US-131 authors the recipes into the empty
  `Resources/jogress.json` and must delete `testTheShippedFileHoldsNoRecipesUntilUS131`; the
  validator is ready for it. US-132 then consumes `recipes(involving:)` + `recipe(for:and:)` and
  must call `MainScreenModel.checkForStranding()` after it consumes its two parents (US-129).
---

## 2026-07-22 - US-131 (Author the Jogress recipes)
- **Resources/jogress.json now holds 14 recipes**, read off the two Bandai charts already committed
  in `Resources/`. Build green, **1659 tests (1655 - 1 marker + 5 new), 0 failures**, and both
  Jogress suites also observed passing on their own with `-only-testing` (16 + 20).
- Files changed: `Resources/jogress.json`, `Tests/JogressCatalogTests.swift` (marker test replaced by
  five that assert the authored data), `Tests/JogressCatalogValidatorTests.swift` (the shipped-file
  sweep's doc comment no longer says it is vacuous, plus a non-empty guard so it cannot become
  vacuous again). No source file changed — US-130's machinery took the data unmodified.
- **THE SOURCE IS THE TWO SHIPPED PDFs, NOT A WEB FETCH.** The PRD's warning about
  `humulos.com/digimon/penc` returning self-referential nonsense meant no web source was used at all.
  `Resources/DIGIMON_COLOR_EVOLUTION.pdf` (Ver.230930, 6 pages) and
  `Resources/DIGIMONPENDULUM COLOR_EVOLUTION.pdf` (Ver.241116, 7 pages) are Bandai's own 資料集
  evolution charts, and every one of the 14 recipes was read off a specific page of one of them.
  Recipe -> source page:
  - Digimon Color 25th, the "與(Ver.N) …對戰" rows at the foot of each 究極體 column:
    BlitzGreymon+CresGarurumon->Omegamon Alter-S (p2 VER.1 and p3 VER.2, stated from both sides);
    Chimairamon+Mugendramon->Millenniumon (p4 VER.3 and p6 VER.5);
    BanchoLeomon+Darkdramon->Chaosmon (p4 VER.3 and p5 VER.4);
    Darkdramon+Mugendramon->Chaosdramon (p5 VER.4 and p6 VER.5).
  - Pendulum Color, the separate box below each 究極體 column:
    WarGreymon+MetalGarurumon->Omegamon (p6 Ver.5 ME and p7 Ver.0 VB);
    Angewomon+LadyDevimon->Mastemon (p2 Ver.1, p4 Ver.3, p7 Ver.0 — three times);
    SaberLeomon+ElDoradimon->Tlalocmon and SaberLeomon+MetalEtemon->Tlalocmon (p2 Ver.1);
    MetalSeadramon+Plesiomon->Aegisdramon (p3 Ver.2);
    MarinAngemon+Hououmon->Mitamamon (p3 Ver.2 and p5 Ver.4);
    Vamdemon+Piemon->VoltoBautamon (p4 Ver.3);
    Griffomon+Pinochimon->Cernumon and Griffomon+Hydramon->Cernumon (p5 Ver.4);
    Mugendramon+HiAndromon->Chaosdramon (p6 Ver.5).
- **LEFT OUT ON PURPOSE, four of them, because AC3 says a guessed recipe fails this story:**
  - `xv-mon` + `stingmon` -> `paildramon`: `stingmon` is dexOnly (asserted in a test). The PRD names
    this one; it is pinned as an ABSENCE so a later iteration re-adding it from a wiki fails.
  - Siriusmon + Arcturusmon -> **Proximamon** (p7 Ver.0 VB, プロキシマモン). Both parents exist and are
    playable, but **Proximamon is in neither `roster.json` nor `16x16 Digimon Sprites/`** —
    `find … -iname '*proxi*'` returns nothing. The result has no sprite, so it cannot ship.
  - ElDoradimon + MetalEtemon -> Tlalocmon, and Pinochimon + Hydramon -> Cernumon. **Ambiguous
    source, not missing data.** Both cells read `<A>` / `+<B> / <C>` / `(3隻其中2隻)` — "2 of these
    3". The `+` prefix anchors A as one parent, which makes A+B and A+C certain; whether B+C alone
    also fuses depends on which way "2 of these 3" is read, and the chart does not settle it. The
    two certain pairs shipped, the ambiguous third did not.
- **THE ROMANISATIONS DO NOT MATCH THE PDFs OR THE PRD, AND FIVE HAD TO BE HUNTED FOR.** The charts
  are Japanese/Chinese only; the PRD's AC5 list uses the English fan spellings. This roster uses a
  third set. Resolved by katakana, then CONFIRMED BY SPRITE: ミレニアモン -> `millenniumon` (not
  "millenniummon"); キメラモン -> `chimairamon`; エルドラディモン -> `eldoradimon` (displayName
  "ElDoradimon"); グリフォモン -> `griffomon` (the PRD calls it "Gryphonmon"); ピノッキモン ->
  `pinochimon` (not "Pinocchimon"/"Puppetmon"). A plain name search would have missed every one.
- **VERIFICATION, all four layers, before the file was written:**
  1. All 34 participant ids resolve in `roster.json`, none `dexOnly`.
  2. Every one has an ANIMATED sheet at `16x16 Digimon Sprites/<stage>/<spriteFile>.png` — checked
     with `os.path.exists`, not assumed from `dexOnly` being absent.
  3. **The sprite art was compared against the PDF thumbnail** for the ten riskiest name resolutions
     (Griffomon, Pinochimon, ElDoradimon, Tlalocmon, Millenniumon, Chimairamon, Cernumon,
     VoltoBautamon, Mitamamon, Mastemon). The charts draw the same 16x16 sprites this game ships, so
     frame 0 beside the chart thumbnail is a direct identity check — all ten matched.
  4. `MapCatalog`-style: the validator sweeps the real file against the real roster and reports [].
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **The two PDFs in `Resources/` are the authoritative tree source and they are READABLE — the
    `.md` beside them is not trustworthy for the Pendulum Color half.** `Digimon_Color_And_Pendulum_
    Color_Evolution_Trees.md` Part 2 lists Agumon/Betamon/Tentomon as Ver.1 Nature Spirits rookies;
    the actual chart (pen p2) has Tentomon/Gotsumon/Otamamon/Angoramon. Part 1 (Digimon Color) did
    check out against the PDF. **Phase E must read the PDFs, not Part 2 of the .md.**
  - **HOW to read them, since neither text-extracts:** the Digimon Color PDF's names are Japanese
    glyphs and the Pendulum one has no Latin text at all, so `zlib`-decompressing the content streams
    gives structure but no names. `pdftotext`/`poppler` is NOT installed and neither is the Read
    tool's `pdftoppm`. **A ~30-line `CGPDFDocument` + `CGImageDestination` tool built with
    `xcrun swiftc` renders any page, or any fractional RECT of a page, to PNG at any scale** —
    `/tmp/us131/render.swift` and `/tmp/us131/crop.swift` (not committed). Cropping the jogress box
    at scale 6 is what made the small print legible. Same throwaway-CoreGraphics-tool pattern the
    screenshot stories use, pointed at a PDF instead of the Simulator.
  - **Page map, so the next story does not re-derive it.** `DIGIMON_COLOR_EVOLUTION.pdf`: p1 legend,
    p2-p6 = VER.1..VER.5. `DIGIMONPENDULUM COLOR_EVOLUTION.pdf`: p1 legend, p2-p7 = Ver.1 NSp,
    Ver.2 DS, Ver.3 NSo, Ver.4 WG, Ver.5 ME, Ver.0 VB. Columns are always
    幼年期I・II/成長期 | 成熟期 (Child) | 完全體 (Perfect) | 究極體 (Ultimate), and the jogress rows are
    the box at the FOOT of the last column. `勝率` = win rate, `C`/`E`/`M`/`O`/`Z` are care counters.
  - **Resolve a Digimon by SPRITE, not by name, when the source is in another language.** Five of the
    fourteen recipes name a Digimon this roster spells differently enough that an exact-name lookup
    misses. Reading the katakana narrows it to a candidate; drawing frame 0 of that candidate's sheet
    next to the chart's thumbnail proves it, because the charts use the same 16x16 art the game
    ships. This is cheap and it is the only check that cannot be fooled by a plausible spelling.
  - **A "no findings over the shipped file" test needs a non-empty guard once the data lands.** The
    sweep passes trivially over `[]`, so `XCTAssertFalse(catalog.recipes.isEmpty)` sits beside it now
    — otherwise a later story that empties the file turns the AC's own test green.
- REMAINS: US-132 onward (18/56 passing). US-132 has 14 real recipes to fuse; entry points are
  `recipes(involving:)` and `recipe(for:and:)`, every shipped recipe has EMPTY conditions (so a pair
  is fusable as soon as both are owned and alive — the ordinary Color-device case), and it must call
  `MainScreenModel.checkForStranding()` after consuming its two parents (US-129). Note for its tests:
  three results are reachable by TWO different pairs (Chaosdramon, Tlalocmon, Cernumon), and the two
  Perfect-stage parents (Angewomon/LadyDevimon, Vamdemon) mean a fusable pair is not always two
  Ultimates.
---

## 2026-07-22 - US-132 (Perform a Jogress)
- **Fusing two owned Digimon now works end to end.** New `Sources/Jogress.swift` (`JogressOffer`,
  `JogressBoard`, `JogressWording`, `JogressOutcome`), new `Sources/JogressView.swift` (the pair list
  and `JogressEntryRow`), `GameStore.performJogress` as one transaction, and
  `MainScreenModel.jogressBoard` / `performJogress(_:)` joining them to `PartyView`. Build green,
  **1690 tests (1659 + 31 new), 0 failures.**
- Files changed: `Sources/Jogress.swift` (new), `Sources/JogressView.swift` (new),
  `Tests/JogressFusionTests.swift` (new, 31 tests), `Sources/GameStore.swift`,
  `Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`, `Sources/PartyView.swift`, `Sources/ContentView.swift`.
- **THE STORY'S REAL TRAP WAS NOT THE FUSION, IT WAS DRAWING THE RESULT.** Every Jogress result is
  one of the 780 orphans no authored line reaches, so the pre-existing `graph.presentation(forId:)`
  answers **nil for every fusion in the game**. Left alone, the player who fused two Ultimates would
  have got `SavedGameUnavailableView` over the Digimon they had just earned, a party row reading
  `omegamon` with no art, and "No Digimon to fight with" from Battle. Fixed with a roster fallback in
  `MainScreenModel.presentation(forId:)`, `PartyRow.rows` and the battle guard. **The graph is still
  asked FIRST** — for a wired id the two agree on name and sprite, but the graph's stage is where the
  ART lives, and that is the one field a disagreement draws a placeholder for.
- **AC6 is the SHAPE of the store method, not a cleanup path.** Every refusal — a record from another
  store, the same record twice, a dead parent, a pair that is not the recipe's, a result the roster
  cannot draw — is decided *before the first mutation*, so the ineligible case needs no rollback at
  all. The only thing that can fail afterwards is the write. `loadOrCreateProfile()` is called up
  front deliberately: it can itself `save()`, and a save in the middle of the fusion would be exactly
  the half-written transaction the AC forbids.
- **AC4's judgement call, worth knowing because it is not forced by the wording:** the result inherits
  the RETURNED egg's origin. Carrying the *other* parent's would leave both ids still held afterwards
  and nothing actually released — the criterion would be true of the delete and false of the box.
- **AC1 strictness:** a recipe condition must hold for BOTH parents. Inert today (all 14 shipped
  recipes have empty conditions), so the choice is about what a later authored gate would MEAN — and
  the strict reading cannot accidentally offer a fusion the data meant to gate.
- **VERIFIED ON BOTH SIMULATORS, clean installs each time** (46mm Series 11, 41mm Series 9):
  entry row reads `Jogress / 1 pair ready` over the seeded pair; the **unavailable** form is present,
  not a button, and reads "None of your Digimon fuse with each other." over an ordinary box (AC2
  observed on screen, not just unit-tested); the pair list fits three sprites, the arrow and
  "WarGreymon + MetalGarurumon" on one line even at 41mm; and `-jogressCeremonyDemo` drove the REAL
  `performJogress`, where a 14-frame burst caught `EvolutionCeremonyView` mid-play (WarGreymon
  full-screen on black, then the white flash) settling to **"Omegamon · Ultimate"** out on the main
  screen with real art.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **THE BUNDLE ID IS `com.digivpet.DigiVPet`, NOT `com.digivpet.app`.** A wrong id fails with
    `FBSOpenApplicationServiceErrorDomain code=4`, which reads like a crash-on-launch and is not.
    `simctl` then happily screenshots the *previous* screen, so the burst looks plausible and is
    stale. Cost ~10 minutes. Read it from the built app:
    `/usr/libexec/PlistBuddy -c "Print :CFBundleIdentifier" "$APP/Info.plist"`.
  - **`simctl erase` REFUSES on a booted device** (`code=405, Unable to erase contents and settings
    in current state: Booted`) and the script carries on regardless. The sequence that works is
    `terminate` → `shutdown` → `sleep 3` → `erase` → `boot` → `sleep 25-30` → `install` → `launch`.
    Both sims are usually already booted at the start of an iteration, so this bites immediately.
  - **A ceremony needs a burst with NO sleep between frames.** The existing pattern's `sleep 1` is
    right for a walk cycle but far too slow here — 14 back-to-back `simctl io screenshot` calls
    caught the flash; the same count at 1s apart would have landed entirely after it. Then take a
    SECOND, slower burst for the settled screen.
  - **When a value type makes two states exclusive, say so in the initialiser.** `JogressBoard`'s
    init nils `reason` when there are offers and substitutes one when there are none, so "the entry
    point never draws an empty list with nothing to explain it" (AC2) is unrepresentable rather than
    tested. Same move as `JogressPair` sorting its ids in US-130.
  - **An offer that CONSUMES what it indexes must be re-derived from the live box before it acts.**
    `performJogress` re-checks the offer against `jogressBoard.offers` and re-matches the recipe on
    the parents' current ids. Taking a Digimon out reorders the box (US-125's thaw moves a birth
    date), so a party screen held across one switch could otherwise fuse two Digimon the player never
    chose — worse than `activate(_:)`'s stale-row bug, which only put the wrong one out.
  - **Inject the COMMIT, not just the clock, when a story says "a failure part-way rolls back".**
    There is no other way to make SwiftData throw on demand, and the AC is otherwise unobservable.
    `flush: (() throws -> Void)? = nil`, defaulting to `context.save()`; the app never passes it.
  - **`-jogressListDemo` was added on the US-121 `-mapDetailDemo` precedent.** Whenever a story's new
    UI sits one tap below an existing screen, it is unphotographable without a flag — `simctl` has no
    tap command. Budget for the flag as part of the story, not as an afterthought.
- REMAINS: US-133 onward (19/56 passing). Phase D is DONE; Phase E is the roster wiring — 11 device
  trees then 26 orphan sweeps. **Phase E must read the two PDFs in `Resources/`, not Part 2 of the
  `.md` beside them** (US-131 found the `.md`'s Pendulum half is wrong); the page map and the
  `CGPDFDocument` render/crop tooling are in US-131's entry above. Note for it: the roster fallback
  this story added means a newly wired orphan already draws correctly before its edge exists.
---

## 2026-07-22 - US-133 (Wire the Digital Monster Color Version 1 evolution tree)
- **The V1 tree is now complete and playable end to end.** The seed line US-008 called `agumon`
  WAS this tree, authored pruned; this story **renamed it to `dmc-v1`** and filled in the ten nodes
  it never carried. Build green, **1702 tests (1690 + 12 new), 0 failures. Orphans 780 -> 771.**
- Files changed: `Resources/evolutions.json` (11 nodes re-lined, 10 new, 5 new edges on existing
  nodes), `Resources/elements.json`, `Resources/moves.json`, `Sources/DexModel.swift` (new
  `lineTitles`), `Sources/DexView.swift`, `Sources/EvolutionTreeView.swift`,
  `Sources/MinigameAssignment.swift`, `Sources/Notifications.swift`, `docs/evolutions-schema.md`,
  `Tests/DMCVersion1TreeTests.swift` (new, 12 tests) and eleven existing test files.

- **THE STORY IS A RENAME, AND THAT IS THE WHOLE DECISION.** AC2 wants every V1 Digimon on line
  `dmc-v1`, but Botamon/Koromon/Agumon/Greymon/Meramon/Numemon/MetalGreymon were already nodes on
  line `agumon` and `line` is single-valued. Three options, and the third is right:
  1. *Re-line only the new nodes.* Every arrow into them would cross a line boundary, and
     `EvolutionTreeLayout` **drops any connector whose target it did not place** — the Dex would
     draw the V1 tree as six parentless Digimon floating beside the ladder.
  2. *Duplicate the seven into scoped ids.* ~7 more nodes per tree × 11 trees, each needing a
     unique move signature name, and Agumon drawn in four Dex trees.
  3. *Rename the line.* Six keys move (elements/moves `lineDefaults`, `MinigameAssignment.byLine`,
     `-dexLineDemo`, the tree preview host) plus a new `DexModel.lineTitles`, and the tree is one
     closed tree with no crossing edge at all.
  **The other five seed lines map onto the other four DMC versions the same way** — gabumon=V2,
  patamon=V3, piyomon+palmon=V4, gazimon=V5 — so US-134..US-137 should each be the same rename.

- **`DexModel.lineTitles` is new and required, not decoration.** `title(ofLine:)` was
  `graph.node(id: line)?.displayName ?? line`; a device slug names no node, so without a title the
  Dex section header reads `dmc-v1`. **Keep the titles under ~15 characters**: "Digital Monster
  Ver.1" was screenshotted on 41mm and came back as "Digital Monster…", losing the one word that
  says which tree it is. Shipped as **"Color Ver.1"**, which fits untruncated.

- **A REGRESSION NO TEST COULD HAVE CAUGHT, found only because the screenshot was taken.** At 21
  nodes the Adult column is six deep, so the tree grid is 234pt tall. `EvolutionTreeView` was a
  **horizontal-only** `ScrollView`, and a grid taller than the viewport inside one does not
  overflow or clip — **it draws NOTHING**. The V1 tree was a black screen under its own navigation
  title on 41mm. Isolated it by pointing the same build's tree demo at the untouched 10-node
  `gabumon` line, which drew normally, so it was the SIZE and not the new data. Fixed with
  `ScrollView([.horizontal, .vertical])`. **Every remaining Phase E tree is this size**, so this
  had to be fixed once, here.

- **Two prior invariants deliberately relaxed**, each with the reason in the test that pins it:
  - `testEveryNonTerminalChildAndAdultHasTwoToFourOutgoingEdges` (was `...TwoOrThree`). US-061's
    shape is "two earned branches plus the junk fallback", and a device tree gives a Rookie five or
    six Champions. Even split across two Children (US-044's pattern) that needs three earned on
    one of them. **Four is what the whole source document fits in** — check V4's Palmon and V5's
    Gizamon, both six-wide — so this ceiling should hold for all of Phase E.
  - `DexScreenTests.testNoShippedDigimonHasMoreThanFourCandidates` (was `...Three`), to match.
    Measured on 41mm: four candidates draw as 3 + 1 with **both rows on screen at once**.

- **AC11's two absent names, searched with `find -iname` over the whole asset pack, and asserted
  absent by a test rather than only noted:**
  - **Betamon** — only `Idle Frame Only/Betamon.png`, so the roster marks it `dexOnly`.
  - **Tyranomon** — no colour sheet anywhere. The only match is `Black and White Sprites/Adult/
    Tyranomon.png`, and `scripts/import_roster.py` does not index that folder, so there is not even
    a roster entry to point at. **`Black and White Sprites/` is invisible to the roster** — worth
    remembering before declaring a later tree's Digimon present.

- **Choosing a substitute Rookie: pick one NO tree in the document names.** Betamon carries
  Airdramon and Seadramon alone, so without a stand-in they could not be seeded. The obvious
  choices are all spoken for — Otamamon and Gomamon and Syakomon are Pendulum Color rookies (and
  US-131 already warned that the `.md`'s Pendulum half is wrong; the PDF's Ver.1 NSp rookies are
  Tentomon/Gotsumon/Otamamon/Angoramon). **Swimmon appears in neither Part of the document at all**,
  so taking it costs no later story a Rookie. Grep the whole `.md` before choosing one.

- **TRUST THE CODEBASE PATTERNS SECTION ABOVE OVER YOUR OWN GREP.** It already names
  `-noNotificationPrompt`; I grepped `Sources/Notifications.swift`, found nothing, concluded the
  flag did not exist and wrote a second one — it lives in `MainScreenModel.requestNotificationAuthorization`,
  because the ASK is the model's, not the deliverer's. Reverted. **Grep `Sources/` whole**, or just
  read the pattern above. Cost ~20 minutes. Confirmed working sequence, unchanged from what was
  already written down: `-healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt <demo flag>`, and `simctl privacy`
  has neither a `health` nor a `notifications` service, so an alert already on screen can only be
  cleared by `shutdown` → `erase` → `boot`.

- **Line-scoped ids are the answer to "another line already owns this Digimon".** The V1 tree ends
  Numemon → Monzaemon → ShinMonzaemon, and `shinmonzaemon` is the palmon line's junk Ultimate. Same
  art, same displayName, id `dmcv1_shinmonzaemon` — exactly `piyo_yuramon` from US-045. It needs
  its own `elements.json` and `moves.json` entries with a signature name unique across the file,
  and it is **not** an orphan removed: it is not a roster id, so it never counted as one.

- **What the V1 tree's last row actually is.** "BlitzGreymon -> Ultra: Omegamon Alter-S (Jogress
  with CresGarurumon)" is not an evolution edge — `Resources/jogress.json` already carried exactly
  that pair from US-131. BlitzGreymon is terminal here and a test asserts the recipe instead, so
  the row is covered rather than missing. Expect the same for V2/V4/V5's Ultra rows.

- REMAINS: US-134 onward (20/56 passing). US-134 is Digital Monster Color Version 2 — the
  `gabumon` line renamed to `dmc-v2` and completed, the same shape as this story. Its Ultra row is
  the other half of this one's (CresGarurumon + BlitzGreymon), already in `jogress.json`.

## 2026-07-22 - US-134 (Wire the Digital Monster Color Version 2 evolution tree)
- **The V2 tree is now complete and playable end to end.** The seed line US-008 called `gabumon`
  WAS this tree, authored pruned; this story **renamed it to `dmc-v2`** and filled in the thirteen
  nodes it never carried. Build green, **1716 tests (1702 + 14 new), 0 failures. Orphans 771 -> 760.**
- Files changed: `Resources/evolutions.json` (10 nodes re-lined, 13 new, 6 new edges on existing
  nodes), `Resources/elements.json`, `Resources/moves.json`, `Sources/DexModel.swift`,
  `Sources/DexView.swift`, `Sources/MinigameAssignment.swift`, `docs/evolutions-schema.md`,
  `Tests/DMCVersion2TreeTests.swift` (new, 14 tests) and seven existing test files.

- **US-133's prediction held exactly: this story was the same rename.** Six keys move (elements /
  moves `lineDefaults`, `MinigameAssignment.byLine`, `DexModel.lineTitles`, and
  `EvolutionGraphTests`' per-line counts), and the tree is one closed tree with no crossing edge.
  Nothing new was learned about the mechanism — **read US-133's entry below before starting V3.**

- **WHERE V2 IS HARDER THAN V1, and it is the whole of this story: nothing prunes it.** V1 lost
  Betamon (idle-only) and Tyranomon (no colour sheet), which quietly cut Agumon's five Champions to
  four. **Every one of Version 2's seventeen names has a playable 48x64 sheet**, so all five arrows
  out of Gabumon have to exist. Three consequences, and each one is a decision the next tree will
  meet again:
  - **The out-degree ceiling went 4 -> 5**, and the Dex candidate ceiling with it. US-133 wrote
    that "four is what the whole source document fits in" — **that was wrong, and checking the
    document rather than the previous story's note is the lesson**: V4's Palmon and V5's Gizamon are
    SIX wide. Raised one step anyway, deliberately: a ceiling looser than the file it guards catches
    nothing.
  - **The junk fallback moved from Geremon to Vegimon.** A device tree's junk Champion is the one
    BOTH Rookies fall to — Numemon in V1, Vegimon in V2, Scumon in V3 — and Gabumon's five arrows
    end in Vegimon, so there is no room for Geremon beside them. `EvolutionCriteriaTests.junkIds`
    gained `vegimon` and `dmcv2_vademon`, and `SeedRosterTests`' Ver.2 default path is now
    Vegimon -> Vademon -> Ebemon.
  - **A displaced node needs a new parent, not deleting.** Dropping Geremon would have left a
    shipped Digimon reachable from nothing — an orphan re-created by the story whose job is to
    remove them. It hangs off Elecmon as the overfeeding branch (`care.overfeeds atLeast 6`), which
    also keeps WereGarurumon and Gerbemon under it. **Before removing an edge, check whether it is
    the target's only in-edge** (`graph.parents(of:)`), and a test now pins that one.

- **A NAME CAN EXIST AND STILL BE ON THE WRONG RUNG.** Whamon is a Champion in the V2 document and
  a **Perfect** in this asset pack — `Perfect/Whamon.png` is its only animated sheet, and the
  roster's stage comes from the folder. An Adult node would have resolved to no art and failed the
  validator's `missingSprite`. It stands BESIDE MetalMamemon instead of beneath it, off the same
  two Champions the document puts on its row, and shares MetalMamemon's Mega (the one invented
  arrow — no Perfect in the file is terminal, and a terminal Perfect is a Digimon that can never
  evolve again). **Check the sprite's FOLDER, not just that the file exists**; V1's checklist was
  "does the art exist", and that is only half the question. Pendulum Color V2 puts Whamon at
  Perfect too, so US-139 will need a line-scoped id for it.

- **Line-scoped ids again, and they will keep coming.** `dmcv2_vademon` / `dmcv2_ebemon`, because
  the `gazimon` line (US-137's V5) already owns the plain ids. Each needs its own `elements.json`
  and `moves.json` entry with a signature name unique across the file, and neither counts as an
  orphan removed — they are not roster ids. Running tally of aliases in `RosterTests`:
  `dmcv1_shinmonzaemon`, `dmcv2_ebemon`, `dmcv2_vademon`, `extyranomon`, `piyo_tanemon`,
  `piyo_yuramon`.

- **MEASURED on the Simulator, because a raised ceiling is a claim about a screen.** On 41mm
  Gabumon's five candidates draw as **3 + 2**, both rows AND the hint list on one screen: row 1
  tiles at x16-108 / x126-224 / x248-328, row 2 at x35-81 / x135-216, the second band ending at
  y276 of a 430-row screen. Nothing clipped, no name truncated. US-133's black-screen regression
  was re-checked at 23 nodes (one more than the tree that caused it) — the V2 tree draws on both
  watch sizes, and `-dexTreeScrollDemo` reaches the Adult column.
  - New DEBUG flags: **`-dexWidestDetailDemo`** (opens the widest evolution grid the file holds,
    seeding its candidates so the tiles are real art) and **`-dexLineDemo=<line>`**, US-133's flag
    generalised — every Phase E tree needs looking at exactly once, and the bare flag hard-coded
    `dmc-v1`. Both write discoveries to the save; both simulators were erased afterwards.
  - **Getting a mid-sheet screenshot is a two-flag trick worth remembering:**
    `-dexWidestDetailDemo -dexBranchDemo`. `-dexTreeLinkDemo` scrolls to the very bottom and the
    candidate grid is then above the fold; selecting a branch shortens the hint list from eight
    rows to two, which brings the grid back onto the same screen.

- REMAINS: US-135 onward (21/56 passing). US-135 is Digital Monster Color Version 3 — the
  `patamon` line renamed to `dmc-v3` and completed. Note before starting it: `patamon` is ALREADY
  five-wide (Unimon / Centalmon / Ogremon / Bakemon / Scumon), which is the whole of that tree's
  Rookie row, so the ceiling raised here should be enough for it. Its Kunemon side is the new work,
  and V3 has no Ultra/Jogress row at all.

## 2026-07-22 - US-135 (Wire the Digital Monster Color Version 3 evolution tree)
- **The V3 tree is now complete and playable end to end.** The seed line US-044 called `patamon`
  WAS this tree, authored pruned; this story **renamed it to `dmc-v3`** and added the three nodes it
  was missing. Build green, **1729 tests (1716 + 13 new), 0 failures. Orphans 760 -> 757.**
- Files changed: `Resources/evolutions.json` (17 nodes re-lined, 3 new, 3 new edges on existing
  nodes), `Resources/elements.json`, `Resources/moves.json`, `Sources/DexModel.swift`,
  `Sources/MinigameAssignment.swift`, `docs/evolutions-schema.md`, `Tests/DMCVersion3TreeTests.swift`
  (new, 13 tests) and four existing test files.

- **THE CHEAPEST TREE OF PHASE E SO FAR, and the reason is worth knowing before US-136.** US-133
  added 10 nodes and US-134 added 13; this one added **three**. US-044 had already authored the
  whole spine — Patamon's five Champions, all three Perfects, all three Megas — and even the two
  Champions it could not reach (Shellmon, Drimogemon) were already named in `SeedRosterTests`'
  `patamonLineVerifiedSet`. **Read the existing line before estimating the work**: only Kunemon (the
  document's second Rookie) and its two exclusive Champions were genuinely absent. Expect US-136
  (`piyomon` -> V4) to be closer to this than to US-134, since US-045 authored it the same way —
  but its Rookie is SIX wide and two of its Champions have no art, so it will need the ceiling
  raised and the rehoming that US-045 already did checked rather than redone.

- **NO CEILINGS MOVED, for the first time in Phase E.** Patamon and Kunemon are five-wide and
  US-134's 2...5 out-degree ceiling and five-candidate Dex ceiling already covered them. **V4's
  Palmon and V5's Gizamon are still SIX wide in the document** — that raise is US-136/US-137's,
  unchanged from what US-134 predicted.
- **Four earned branches is the HARD ceiling for a Child, and it is not a taste question.**
  `SeedRosterTests.testThePatamonChildrensEarnedBranchesUseDistinctEnergies` requires every earned
  edge out of a Child to carry a distinct `requiredEnergy`, and there are only four energy types.
  A five-wide Rookie is therefore always four earned + the junk `isDefault`, and the junk edge must
  share a rival's energy while sitting below it on `minEnergy`. **A SIX-wide Rookie cannot be
  authored this way at all** — US-136 will have to either split the sixth onto another Child (the
  US-045 pattern) or change what distinguishes two edges of the same energy. Decide that BEFORE
  authoring V4, not after the test fails.

- **The same edge can point at the same target from two parents with DIFFERENT energies, and that
  is what made Kunemon fit.** Ogremon is `stamina` from Patamon and Tsukaimon but `strength` from
  Kunemon; Bakemon is `vitality` from all three. `requiredEnergy` is a property of the EDGE, not of
  the target node, so a shared Champion costs a Rookie whichever of its four slots is still free.
  Nothing in the validator or the tests objects. Without this, Kunemon's five could not have been
  authored at all: it shares three of them with Patamon.

- **DO NOT EMPTY A NODE THE SOURCE DOCUMENT DOES NOT CONTAIN.** Tsukaimon is not in the V3 tree —
  US-061 invented it to hold Ogremon and Bakemon when a Child could carry only two earned branches.
  Giving Patamon its five back made Tsukaimon's branches redundant, and deleting them would have
  left a shipped Child that evolves into nothing: a NEW orphan, made by the story whose job is to
  remove them. It keeps them and stands beside Kunemon as a third Rookie the device never had. This
  is US-134's Geremon lesson in the other direction — that one was about a lost IN-edge, this one
  about lost OUT-edges. **Check both directions before pruning.**

- **Version 3 needed NO line-scoped alias**, the first tree in Phase E that did not: none of its
  sixteen names is owned by another line. The running tally in `RosterTests` is unchanged —
  `dmcv1_shinmonzaemon`, `dmcv2_ebemon`, `dmcv2_vademon`, `extyranomon`, `piyo_tanemon`,
  `piyo_yuramon`. A test in `DMCVersion3TreeTests` asserts no `dmcv3_` id exists, so the day one is
  needed the reason has to be written down.
- **Version 3 has no Ultra/Jogress row at all**, unlike V1, V2 and V4. Its three Megas are terminal
  and a test pins that, so a later story adding a recipe for one of them has to say why.

- **AC11's one absent name, searched with `find -iname` over the whole asset pack:**
  - **Poyomon** — only `16x16 Digimon Sprites/Idle Frame Only/Poyomon.png`, no 48x64 sheet under
    `Baby I/`, so it is `dexOnly`. US-044 already substituted Puttimon and wrote the reason onto the
    `puttimon` node; this story only re-asserted it. Every OTHER name in the section is playable.
  - Kunemon, Shellmon and Drimogemon were each checked for FOLDER as well as existence (US-134's
    Whamon lesson): `Child/Kunemon.png`, `Adult/Shellmon.png`, `Adult/Drimogemon.png` — all three
    agree with the rung the document puts them on, so nothing needed rehoming this time.

- **LOOKED AT ON BOTH SCREENS, because every Phase E tree gets photographed once.** 41mm and 46mm,
  `-dexDemo -dexLineDemo=dmc-v3`: the twenty-node tree draws with its ladder and the three-way fork
  out of Tokomon, titled **"Color Ver.3"** from `DexModel.lineTitles` rather than the raw key. No
  black screen — US-133's regression was at 22 nodes and this tree is smaller than the 23-node V2
  one already cleared. Both simulators erased afterwards (`-dexDemo` writes discoveries to the save).

- REMAINS: US-136 onward (22/56 passing). US-136 is Digital Monster Color Version 4 — the `piyomon`
  line renamed to `dmc-v4`. Read the two paragraphs above about the six-wide Rookie and the
  four-energy limit before starting it; that is the one thing this story did not have to solve.

## 2026-07-22 - US-136: Wire the Digital Monster Color Version 4 evolution tree
- Renamed the `piyomon` seed line (US-045's pruned V4 tree) to `dmc-v4` and finished it: ONE new
  node, `dmcv4_palmon`, the document's second Rookie. 21 nodes in the line, 115 in the file.
- Files: `Resources/evolutions.json` (line rename, new node, two new edges, four comments),
  `Resources/elements.json`, `Resources/moves.json`, `Sources/MinigameAssignment.swift`,
  `Sources/DexModel.swift` (lineTitles + a stale doc-comment example), `Tests/DMCVersion4TreeTests.swift`
  (new, 16 tests), `Tests/SeedRosterTests.swift`, `Tests/EvolutionGraphTests.swift`,
  `Tests/EvolutionGraphValidatorTests.swift`, `Tests/ElementCatalogTests.swift`,
  `Tests/RosterTests.swift`, `docs/evolutions-schema.md`.
- Build green, 1745 tests (1729 + 16), 0 failures. Screenshotted on 41mm and 46mm.

- **Learnings for future iterations:**

- **THE SIX-WIDE ROOKIE WAS NEVER SIX WIDE. No ceiling moved.** US-134 and US-135 both wrote that
  US-136 would have to raise the 2...5 out-degree ceiling and the five-candidate Dex ceiling,
  because the document gives V4's Palmon six Champions. It does not need to: **BOTH of AC11's
  absent names are in that same row.** Kokatorimon is absent from the pack entirely
  (`find "16x16 Digimon Sprites" -iname '*okatorimon*'` returns nothing — no colour sheet, no
  monochrome one, no roster entry) and Nanimon is idle-only. Six minus two is four, which plus the
  junk fallback is exactly the five edges the ceiling already allowed. **Count the DRAWABLE row
  before pricing a ceiling raise off the document's row** — a previous story's estimate of the work
  is made without having run `ls`, and Phase E prunes a tree by art more often than not.
  **US-137's Gizamon is the remaining six-wide claim and it is a DIFFERENT case**: US-046's notes
  say V5's only omission is Flymon, so Gizamon's drawable row really is five earned + junk = six
  edges, and that one probably WILL need the raise. Check it against `ls` first anyway.

- **A line-scoped alias needs THREE data-file entries, not two, and the third has a uniqueness
  rule.** `dmcv4_palmon` needed `elements.json` and `moves.json` entries like any node — but
  `MoveCatalogTests.testSignatureNamesAreAuthoredRatherThanTemplated` requires every node's
  `signatureName` to be **globally distinct**, so copying the aliased Digimon's move entry verbatim
  fails: `dmcv4_palmon` and `palmon` both claiming "Poison Ivy" was the one red test in this story.
  Give the alias a second real attack from the same Digimon ("Allergy Shower"). US-045 already knew
  this — `piyo_yuramon` is "Dew Spray" where `yuramon` is "Dew Drop" — but nothing wrote it down.

- **A Phase E story can legitimately remove ZERO orphans, and that has to be asserted or it reads
  as a slip.** 757 -> 757, counted with Appendix B over a regenerated `roster.generated.json` and
  cross-checked by running the same count against `git show HEAD:Resources/evolutions.json`. The
  whole V4 section was already wired by US-045/US-061 except its second Rookie, and that Rookie is
  an ALIAS — a second node on a Digimon the `palmon` line has connected since US-008, so it is not
  a roster id and never counted as an orphan. What the story bought is tree CORRECTNESS: Palmon
  sits where the document draws it, and Piyomon gained the Kuwagamon its row always had.
  `DMCVersion4TreeTests.testTheStoryAddedNoNewlyConnectedRosterDigimon` pins the zero.
  **Expect the same shape from any remaining device tree whose seed line was already near-complete.**

- **The Tsukaimon call again, in its purest form.** Hyokomon and Muchomon are in NO source tree —
  US-045 invented them to hold Coelamon, Mojyamon and Kuwagamon while the plain `palmon` id belonged
  to another line. Giving those Champions to `dmcv4_palmon` made both redundant, and emptying them
  would have left two shipped Children that evolve into nothing. **They keep their branches.** That
  is now three stories running (US-134 Geremon, US-135 Tsukaimon, US-136 here); treat it as the
  default, not a judgement call.

- **The same Champion under two parents with different energies keeps paying off** (US-135's
  finding). Leomon is `strength` from both Rookies but Kuwagamon is `stamina` from Piyomon and
  `dmcv4_palmon` while being `strength` from Muchomon. `requiredEnergy` is a property of the EDGE.

- **V4's Ultra row needed no new data.** "Darkdramon -> Ultra: Chaosmon (Jogress with BanchoLeomon)"
  was already a recipe in `Resources/jogress.json` from US-131, so Darkdramon is terminal and a
  comment on the node says where the row went (the V1/V2 pattern, which a test now enforces).
  Worth knowing: that recipe reaches across two device trees — BanchoLeomon is `dmc-v3`'s Mega.

- **A `-dexLineDemo` screenshot needs the right bundle id.** It is `com.digivpet.DigiVPet`
  (`project.yml` line 82), not `com.example.DigiVPet`. `simctl launch` fails with an opaque
  FBSOpenApplicationServiceErrorDomain code=4 and `simctl io screenshot` still writes a plausible
  PNG of the watch face, so a wrong id produces a screenshot that looks like a black-screen bug.

- REMAINS: US-137 onward (23/56 passing). US-137 is Digital Monster Color Version 5 — the `gazimon`
  line renamed to `dmc-v5`. It is the only seed line that already holds BOTH of its Rookies, so
  expect the tree to be near-complete like this one; read the Gizamon paragraph above before
  assuming a ceiling raise, and check `Flymon` with `ls` rather than trusting US-046's note.
