## 2026-07-23 - US-189: Agility decides dodges, and the dodger turns away
- Each incoming swing now rolls a hit chance from both Agility stats before it can deal damage
  (US-189). A lost roll is a DODGE: no HP lost, the defender turns aside.
- Files changed:
  - Sources/Battle.swift — BattleTurn gained `dodged: Bool = false` (defaulted, so every existing
    BattleTurn(...) keeps its meaning); new `BattleAgility` bundle (player/opponent Agility +
    HitRateCoefficients); `BattleEngine.hitChance(attackerAgility:defenderAgility:coefficients:)` —
    base + weight*(atk-def), clamped floor...ceiling; `resolve` gained `agility: BattleAgility? = nil`
    and, when non-nil, rolls `Double.random(in:0..<1)` against hitChance FIRST each turn — a miss
    records a dodge turn (damage 0, HP unchanged) and passes the turn, a hit rolls damage as before.
  - Sources/BattleView.swift — `animation(for:during:landed:)` returns .idle (walk) on a dodge, never
    hurt; new static `faces(_:during:landed:)` flips the DEFENDER to `!faces(side)` at the impact
    instant of a dodge only; instance `faces(for:)` reads beat/hasLanded; arena uses it for both
    sprites' `flipped:`.
  - Sources/MainScreenModel.swift — finishBattleRound builds BattleAgility from each side's base
    Agility (ConsumptionConfig.stats(for: stage)?.baseAgility) and passes it to resolve; nil (no
    dodges) only if a stage has no stats.
  - Tests/BattleTests.swift — BattleAgilityDodgeTests (9 tests): AC3 formula (equal->base, monotonic
    decreasing in defender / increasing in attacker, clamped in [floor,ceiling]), forced-miss dodge
    with no HP lost, forced-hit no-dodge, back-compat no-agility never dodges, and the face-turn +
    keep-walking. Uses a private ConstantGenerator.
- VERIFIED: build green; full suite 2565 tests, 0 failures (Series 11 46mm, +9 over US-188's 2556).
  AC4 screenshot via a TEMP `-battleDodgeProbe` (resolve + all-miss generator, then removed): arena
  showed Greymon (opponent) facing the SAME way as the attacking Agumon — i.e. flipped from its
  normal leftward face-off heading, so turned away.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **A ConstantGenerator(value: 0) HANGS Int.random(in:using:).** `Int.random`'s rejection sampling
    keeps drawing the same rejected 0 forever (99% CPU, no timeout). This cost a 24-minute hung test
    run. Use word `1` instead: it reads as ~0 for `Double.random(in:0..<1)` (so still forces a hit)
    AND terminates `Int.random` on the first draw. `.max` is safe (the float random takes one draw,
    no loop) and forces a MISS (~0.9999 >= any hit chance since ceiling<1).
  - **The dodge roll is the FIRST draw of a turn, damage the second — and ONLY when `agility` is
    non-nil.** Passing nil draws neither, so every seeded battle test predating US-189 rolls the exact
    same numbers. This is the same defaulted-optional back-compat seam US-188 used for HP. Any future
    battle change that adds a per-turn draw MUST keep the nil-agility / default path drawless or it
    shifts every pinned seed.
  - **HitRateCoefficients + the whole stageStats table were ALREADY shipped (US-170/US-186) and
    tested by ConsumptionConfigTests.** US-189 read them; it authored no config. US-190 (element
    damage: ElementDamageMultipliers is likewise already in the struct + consumption.json), US-191/192
    (training bonuses + trainingCap on StageStats) should also READ, not re-author.
  - **A leftover system alert (notification permission) from a PREVIOUS killed demo app persists on a
    sim device and covers the next launch's screenshot.** `-noNotificationPrompt` suppresses the app's
    OWN ask (DEBUG only) but not a stale alert already on screen. Fix: screenshot on a CLEAN device
    that never showed it, not the one a prior iteration left dirty.
---

## 2026-07-23 - US-190: Element matchup scales real damage
- Every landed swing is now scaled by the attacker-vs-defender element matchup (US-190). The dodge
  and HP model from US-188/189 are untouched; this only changes what a landed hit dents.
- Files changed:
  - Sources/Battle.swift — new `BattleElements` bundle (player element + opponent element +
    ElementDamageMultipliers) with `scaled(_:attacker:defender:)` = max(minimum, round(damage *
    matchupMultiplier)), the multiplier read from `DigimonElement.effectiveness(against:)` mapped to
    config advantage/neutral/disadvantage. `resolve` gained `elements: BattleElements? = nil`
    (defaulted, back-compat) and, when non-nil, scales the ROLLED landed damage AFTER the draw — no
    extra randomness, so every pre-US-190 seed is byte-stable.
  - Sources/MainScreenModel.swift — finishBattleRound builds BattleElements from
    `matchup.playerType.element` / `matchup.opponentType.element` (already resolved by
    BattleModifiers.matchup) + `config.elementDamage`, and passes it to resolve. Always supplied (no
    optional): an unauthored type resolves to `.neutral`, which nets the neutral multiplier.
  - Tests/BattleTests.swift — new BattleElementDamageTests (3): (1) `scaled` orders advantage>=neutral
    >=disadvantage and floors at minimum over base 1..12, strict at base 4; (2) a full-length fight
    (equal power, huge HP -> runs to maximumTurns so all three matchups roll IDENTICAL base hits off
    one seed) has the player deal strictly more total dashes advantaged than neutral than disadvantaged
    over seeds 0..19, every landed hit >= minimum; (3) a neutral matchup (mult 1.0) resolves
    bit-for-bit like the no-elements engine over seeds 0..39.
- VERIFIED: build green; full suite 2568 tests, 0 failures (Series 11 46mm, +3 over US-189's 2565).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **THE ELEMENT DAMAGE MULTIPLIER IS A SECOND, STRONGER ELEMENT AXIS — DISTINCT FROM
    BattleModifiers.** BattleModifiers.elementAdvantage (1.25/0.8) scales POWER pre-battle (who wins);
    ConsumptionConfig.elementDamage (1.5/1.0/0.5, minimum 1) scales the REAL per-swing dent. Both fire
    on the same matchup, both were already in place (struct + consumption.json from US-170); US-190
    only wired the damage one into resolve. Do not collapse them.
  - **BattleElements uses `DigimonElement.effectiveness(against:)`, NOT BattleModifiers net
    arithmetic.** That means a MUTUAL pairing (light vs dark) lands BOTH attackers on `.advantage`
    (each hits harder), where BattleModifiers nets the power factor to 1.0. This is deliberate and
    matches the AC's "advantage/neutral/disadvantage from ElementCatalog". If US-192+ ever needs the
    netted behaviour for damage, that is a separate decision.
  - **SCALE THE ROLL AFTER THE DRAW, NEVER BEFORE, to keep seeds stable.** The third defaulted-optional
    back-compat seam in a row (US-188 HP, US-189 agility, US-190 elements): every one adds capability
    only when its optional is non-nil AND draws no randomness on the nil path. A neutral BattleElements
    is byte-identical to nil (pinned by testANeutralMatchupResolvesIdenticallyToNoElements) — mult 1.0
    and floor never bites a >=1 roll.
  - **TESTING A PER-SWING MULTIPLIER: EQUAL POWER + HUGE HP RUNS THE FIGHT TO maximumTurns, so all
    matchups share the exact base-roll sequence off one seed** and the ONLY difference is the
    multiplier. Sum the attacker-side turns; do not compare single turns (round(r*1.5) vs r vs
    round(r*0.5) can tie at r=1). US-191 (train caps -> effective stats) and US-192 will read the same
    stage stat table; the battle plumbing (HP/agility/elements) is now all in resolve's defaulted args.
---

## 2026-07-23 - US-191: Stats train up to a per-Digimon cap
- Training now raises HP/Attack/Agility toward a per-stage cap; the bonuses are stored per-Digimon
  and the player's EFFECTIVE (base+bonus) HP and Agility are what battle fights on.
- Files changed:
  - Sources/GameState.swift — three optional-backed storage fields (trainedHPBonusStorage /
    trainedAttackBonusStorage / trainedAgilityBonusStorage), init'd to 0, same migration seam as the
    charge stores. Computed trainedHPBonus/trainedAttackBonus/trainedAgilityBonus (?? 0);
    trainedBonus(for: BattleStat) reader; trainStat(_:cap:by:=1) raises one stat toward cap=
    StageStats.trainingCap — floors amount/cap at 0, never reduces (guard current<ceiling -> return 0
    at/over cap), returns the non-negative gain; effectiveStat(_:base:) = base + bonus.
  - Sources/MainScreenModel.swift — finishBattleRound builds playerMaxHP and player Agility through
    state.effectiveStat(.hp/.agility, base:), so a trained Digimon fights on more HP dashes and slips
    more swings. Opponent side unchanged (a wild node is no GameState). No new draw -> every pinned
    battle seed is byte-stable.
  - Tests/TrainedStatsTests.swift — 8 pure tests: fresh=0, per-Digimon independence, repeated training
    never passes base+cap, at-cap gains 0, one-per-call below cap, Perfect cap>Child cap (off bundled
    config) and a Perfect out-trains a Child, effective=base+bonus, negatives/negative-cap never reduce.
- VERIFIED: build green; full suite 2576 tests, 0 failures (Series 11 46mm, +8 over US-190's 2568).
  Ran TrainedStatsTests + BattleTests + TrainActionTests together first to confirm no seed shifted.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **BattleStat (the HP/Attack/Agility enum) lives in StatBarsView.swift but is a plain domain enum
    — GameState (Foundation/SwiftData only) references it fine, same module, no SwiftUI import needed.**
    Reuse it for anything stat-keyed rather than authoring a parallel enum.
  - **US-190's learning holds: the battle plumbing (HP/agility/elements) is all in resolve's defaulted
    args, and the player-side stat now flows through state.effectiveStat(...). Adding a bonus to the
    base BEFORE resolve adds no randomness, so seeds stay stable — same discipline as US-188/189/190.**
  - **baseAttack is STILL not read by any battle rung** (only battlePower drives the power compare, HP
    drives US-188 dashes, Agility drives US-189 dodges). US-191 stores a trained Attack bonus but it
    is inert in combat until a story wires baseAttack in. Don't assume Attack scales damage yet.
  - **trainStat is model-level and reached live only through battle's effectiveStat read** — there is
    no Train-button stat-picker UI. The current Train button still buys the separate strengthStat
    (US-025/075/177), which steers evolution branches and is untouched. If a UI story wants the player
    to pick which of HP/Attack/Agility to raise, it calls trainStat with the stage's trainingCap.
  - **trainingCap is ONE value per stage in StageStats (applies to all three stats), already shipped
    in consumption.json (US-170).** US-191 authored no config — it only read the table, exactly as
    US-189/190 read hitRate/elementDamage. The cap grows with stage (Child 4 -> Perfect 8 -> Ult 10).
---

## 2026-07-23 - US-192 (Losing a battle heals or costs a care mistake, and can kill)
- Reversed US-031's "losing never causes a care mistake" in `GameState.recordBattle`
  (Sources/Battle.swift). A WIN is unchanged (record only). A LOSS now forks on current health:
  - sick  -> HEALED: the exact cure `Sickness.updateSickness` applies (healthStatus=.healthy,
    careMistakeCount=0) PLUS the death-clock reset `Death.updateDeath` does on becoming healthy
    (sickSince=nil, deathWarningSentAt=nil). No care mistake. This is the "or healed" fork.
  - healthy -> care mistake: `careMistakeCount += 1`, which rides the existing neglect ladder
    (>=3 -> sick via updateSickness on refresh -> dead after 72h via updateDeath).
- Updated the doc comment on `MainScreenModel.finishBattle` (was "losing never kills / never a
  care mistake (US-031)").
- Tests: rewrote the 5 that pinned the OLD rule and added coverage for the new one:
  - BattleTests: split the old "neither death nor care mistake" pair into
    testLosingWhileHealthyChargesACareMistake, testLosingWhileSickHealsInsteadOfCharging,
    testEnoughLosingAccruesCareMistakesThatLeadToDeath (3 losses -> updateSickness -> sick ->
    +72h updateDeath -> dead); renamed the fought-battle test to
    testLosingAFoughtBattleWhileHealthyChargesACareMistake (asserts +1, survives a refresh).
  - LightNeglectTests.testLosingBattlesChargeCareMistakesWithoutTrippingTheLightAudit (25 losses
    -> 25 mistakes, lightAuditedNight still nil).
  - BattleCostTests.testLosingChargesOneCareMistakePerLossAndNoExtraEnergy (careMistakeCount ==
    before + battleLosses; no refresh between bouts so all losses land while healthy).
- Full suite: 2577 tests, 0 failures. Build green (watchOS Series 11 46mm).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - The death path is care mistakes -> sickness (Sickness.careMistakesUntilSick=3) -> death
    (Death.secondsSickUntilDeath=72h). Care mistakes do NOT shorten the 72h clock once sick; they
    only get you TO sick. So any "battles cause death" wiring must charge the mistake while HEALTHY.
  - Do NOT add a random draw inside `BattleEngine.resolve` for loss consequences: dozens of tests
    pin literal outcomes off `SeededGenerator` seeds, so any extra draw shifts the whole sequence.
    Keep loss-consequence logic in `recordBattle` off deterministic GameState instead.
  - Curing (updateSickness) resets careMistakeCount=0 but NOT the per-spell markers
    (starvationMistakesCharged/poopMistakesCharged); the heal branch mirrors that exactly, so a
    still-starving Digimon is not instantly re-charged for the same spell.
  - Several tests fight real battles via model.battle()/finishBattle() without asserting care
    state (WanderingTests, PreBattleRoundTests grade loop, BackgroundRefreshTests battle-count) —
    they were unaffected because no refresh runs between bouts, so the Digimon stays healthy and
    the accrued mistakes never tip it into sickness within the test.
---

## 2026-07-23 - US-167 (Orphan sweep: Ultimate-Super Ultimate N-R)
- Wired all 20 remaining N-R Ultimate orphans as evolution nodes in Resources/evolutions.json, each
  with one Perfect in-edge on its parent's line: Nezhamon (Sanzomon), Omegamon (Chimairamon),
  Omegamon X (MetalGreymon X), Omegamon Zwart (WereGarurumon Black), Omegamon Alter-S (MetalGreymon
  Virus), Ogudomon (Mephismon), Ogudomon X (Mephismon X), Ophanimon Core (Angewomon), Ophanimon
  Falldown X (Angewomon X), Ordinemon (Lucemon Falldown), Plesiomon X (MegaSeadramon X),
  PrinceMamemon X (Mamemon X), Quantumon (Andromon), RagnaLordmon (Grademon), Ragnamon (Nanomon),
  Rapidmon X (Rapidmon), Rasenmon Fury (Hisyaryumon), Rosemon Burst (Lilamon), Rosemon X (Lilimon X),
  RustTyrannomon (MetalTyranomon).
- Each new node: line = parent's line, a >200-char Wikimon-citing comment, an explicit elements.json
  type row and a moves.json row (symbol+tint unique within the line, signature name globally unique).
- Each in-edge: inserted BEFORE the parent's isDefault climb (fallback stays last), requiredEnergy
  distinct from the parent's other edges, minEnergy 150, maxCareMistakes 2, exactly two conditions
  (one health metric + one care counter), every hint free of digits.
- Orphan count for stage 'Ultimate-Super Ultimate': BEFORE 39, AFTER 19 (Appendix B script). Overall
  playable orphans 55 -> 35. EvolutionGraphValidator: zero findings over the whole file.
- Added Tests/UltimateSweepNToRTests.swift. Build green; all 2597 tests pass.

**Learnings for future iterations (US-168 / US-169 will hit all of this):**
- An Ultimate sweep is an IN-EDGE-ONLY sweep: every new node is terminal (Ultimate is rung 6, the
  top; the validator's stage-transition check forbids any out-edge). Twenty orphans = twenty nodes.
- The graph is built ONLY from Resources/evolutions.json nodes. The N-R orphans were NOT in that file
  — they existed only as sprite-derived entries in roster.generated.json. So wiring = ADD the node to
  evolutions.json (with `line`, or EvolutionGraph.bundled traps) AND add a Perfect in-edge.
- HARD CONVENTIONS enforced by the per-story test suites (violate any and ~470 tests go red):
  * every edge is INTRA-LINE (orphan.line == parent.line); no edge crosses a line.
  * the isDefault climb must be LAST in each node's evolutions — insert new edges before it.
  * no node offers two edges with the same requiredEnergy (EvolutionEngine matches on dominant type).
  * every evolutions.json node needs an explicit elements.json `types[id]` AND moves.json `moves[id]`
    row — the line/stage fallbacks are unreachable and ElementCatalog/MoveCatalog tests demand the id.
  * moves: (projectileSymbol, tint) unique per line, signatureName globally unique, symbols must be
    real SF Symbols (MoveCatalogTests renders them), signatureName must not contain the displayName.
  * hints must contain NO digit characters (spell numbers as words) — a sweep test checks this.
- SNAPSHOT tests across ~20 files hardcode the CURRENT global totals and must all be bumped: every
  `graph.nodes.count` (was 878, now 898), `graph.nodes(at: .ultimate).count` (199 -> 219), each
  `sizes["<line>"]` you touch, EvolutionGraphTests' whole byLine dict, the ultimate orphan buckets
  (39 -> 19; CToD's jogress-adjusted 37 -> 17), and EvolutionTreeTests' dmc-v1 rowCount/connectors.
- Forking a Perfect that a Perfect/Adult sweep already gave a climb means updating that story's
  `branchedBySweeps`/`wiredBy...` count dict or expected-climb list (they map parent -> edge count).
- DO NOT fork a Perfect that sits on one of US-002's three walked named lines (Agumon/dmc-v1 via
  MetalGreymon, Palmon via Lilimon, Gabumon via WereGarurumon): SeedRosterTests.earnedPath walks the
  single earned edge at each rung, so an added branch redirects the named line. Hang the node on a
  sibling Perfect instead (Omegamon -> Chimairamon, Rosemon Burst -> Lilamon here; the AToB story did
  the same with BanchoLilimon -> Lilamon).
- Jogress-result Ultimates (Omegamon family, Ogudomon, Ordinemon) are counted as orphans by Appendix
  B and DO take an evolution in-edge in the sweep (as IToM did for Mastemon/Mitamamon). Device-tree
  tests that asserted `graph.node(id: "omegamon") == nil` had to change — the line still leaves it a
  Jogress recipe (its own WarGreymon draws no edge), but the node now exists on dmc-v1.
- penc-sw (Saiyu Warriors) has no Digitama, so a node placed there is stranded-from-egg and must be
  added to EvolutionCriteriaTests.strandedUltimate; its comment MUST contain "Saiyu Warriors"
  (BabyII/ChildAToF/DigitamaBabyI membership tests check that).
- Fast dev loop: a Python replica of EvolutionGraphValidator + the Appendix B count catches most data
  errors in <1s before the ~1-minute watchOS build/test.

## 2026-07-23 - US-193 (Fix the Dex crash: reuse the one GameStore, never open a second)
- Added `MainScreenModel.sharedStore() throws -> GameStore` (returns the model's one open store, or throws `SideScreenStoreError.notOpen`) and wired ContentView's three DexView build sites to `DexModel(makeStore: model.sharedStore)` (toolbar link + both DEBUG demo navigationDestinations).
- DexModel's `makeStore` default `{ try GameStore() }` is retained but documented as preview/test-only — the live app must pass the shared store. Both DexModel.load and DexModel.loadHealthReadings now run on the single app-wide ModelContext, so no second GameStore opens on the live file (DigiVPetApp GameSession single-store invariant holds).
- Files: Sources/MainScreenModel.swift (new error enum + sharedStore()), Sources/ContentView.swift (3 sites), Sources/DexModel.swift (doc), Tests/DexScreenTests.swift (regression test).
- Verified: build green; full suite 2598 tests pass (incl. new testTheDexSharesTheGameStoreSoAStateStaysValidAfterWork). Simulator run with `-dexDemo -healthAnswered` pushed the Dex and stayed alive with no new crash report. Pre-fix crash report DigiVPet-2026-07-23-174142.ips confirmed the exact bug: DexModel.loadHealthReadings -> ConditionContext.init(state:) -> GameState.stageMetricTotals.getter -> _assertionFailure (use-after-reset on an invalidated GameState).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - The Dex crash lived in TWO DexModel store opens, not one: `load()` (line 261) AND `loadHealthReadings()` (line 309). The visible crash was in the async loadHealthReadings path reading a persisted GameState property. Any side screen that needs the saved game must take the store via `MainScreenModel.sharedStore`, never `try GameStore()`.
  - `.ips` crash reports in `~/Library/Logs/DiagnosticReports/DigiVPet-*.ips` are gold for pinpointing SwiftData use-after-reset traps — the triggered thread's `frames` name the exact source lines.
  - Simulator smoke test recipe for the Dex: install the Debug-watchsimulator .app, `xcrun simctl launch <sim> com.digivpet.DigiVPet -dexDemo -healthAnswered`, then check `launchctl list | grep digivpet` for survival + `find ~/Library/Logs/DiagnosticReports -name 'DigiVPet*.ips' -mmin -5` for fresh crashes. A system notification prompt overlays the app but does not block SwiftUI rendering behind it.

## 2026-07-24 - US-194 (Shorter room, and the action row sits 12 from the bottom)
- Changed `MainScreenLayout.actionRowBottomInset` from 4 to 12 (Sources/ContentView.swift). This one
  constant satisfies BOTH acceptance criteria: the action row now sits exactly 12pt off the physical
  bottom (AC2), and because the inset is padded INSIDE `.ignoresSafeArea(.container, edges: .bottom)`
  and the sprite `GeometryReader` is the only row claiming `maxHeight: .infinity`, all 8 added points
  come straight out of the play area (AC1 — the deliberate room reduction). Documented before/after in
  the constant's comment and in the padding-application comment.
- RE-MEASURED both slots on the Simulator with `-wanderDemo` (Agumon walks; measured yellow-body
  pixel bbox, calibrated against progress.txt's "2*scale screenshot-px per sprite-px"):
  * 46mm (Series 11, 416x496 @2x): sprite body ~90px tall = 15 sprite-rows x 6px = scale 3. Was
    scale 4. Slot 64.0 -> 56.0pt.
  * 41mm (Series 9, 352x430 @2x): sprite body ~44-48px = 11-12 rows x 4px = scale 2. Was scale 3.
    Slot 49.5 -> 41.5pt.
  Both dropped exactly one deliberate scale step and now sit MID-BAND (41mm 9.5pt down-slack to 32,
  46mm 8pt to 48) rather than on a scale edge, so the old razor-thin font ceiling is now looser.
- Files: Sources/ContentView.swift (inset constant + two comments: MainScreenLayout, MainScreenTypography,
  and the padding-application block), Tests/MainScreenLayoutTests.swift (renamed
  testTheActionRowKeepsExactlyTwelvePointsBelowIt -> asserts ==12; re-measured slot evidence in
  testTheMainScreenFontsStaySmallEnoughToKeepTheSpriteScale to 41.5->2 and 56.0->3).
- Verified: build green (46mm); full suite 2598 tests pass; layout confirmed in
  /tmp/us194/wander46_*.png and wander41_*.png — action row 12pt off bottom, all rows fit, sprite
  walks inside its slot (scrim/map still track SpriteSlotBoundsKey unchanged, so they cover only that
  slot, AC3).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - `actionRowBottomInset` and the sprite-slot height are ONE degree of freedom, not two: every point
    of that inset is subtracted from the flexible sprite `GeometryReader`. You cannot both grow the
    inset and keep the sprite scale — US-194's whole point was to spend the room. A future story that
    wants the buttons closer to the edge again would GIVE the sprite that height back.
  - The `-wanderDemo` flag is the right seed for measuring the sprite slot: it puts a walking Agumon
    (asymmetric, scalable art) on the main screen where every other demo suspends motion and the
    default egg is near-symmetric. Take a burst of ~4-6 and measure the yellow body bbox; the
    calibration is 2*scale screenshot-px per 16px sprite-px (@2x), so body-height/(2*scale) ~= the
    Agumon content rows (~11-15).
  - Screenshot recipe that worked this iteration: `simctl erase` the device FIRST (a stale
    notification-authorization alert from a prior session survives terminate+uninstall and fully
    covers the screen, even though `-noNotificationPrompt` suppresses the real ask), then boot,
    install the SAME Debug-watchsimulator .app, launch with `-healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt
    -wanderDemo`. 46mm sim BA425DD4-8856-4933-8198-0E4B89960E48, 41mm FB045EDB-DEB9-40AA-B8FB-819E9E742517.
  - When you change the main-screen layout, `MainScreenLayoutTests`'s slot-evidence numbers (49.5/64.0
    historically) are EVIDENCE not arithmetic — re-measure and update them, or they silently describe
    a screen that no longer exists.

## 2026-07-24 - US-195: Dash bars read as one solid bar split by 2pt lines
- Reworked Sources/DashBar.swift so segments TOUCH instead of being spaced pills.
  - HStack spacing is now 0; the full width is split evenly (dashWidth = width/count), no layout gap.
  - Dashes are square-cornered Rectangles (was per-dash RoundedRectangle) so a run of solids butts
    into one continuous bar; the whole row is clipped to a RoundedRectangle(cornerRadius: h/3) so
    only the two OUTER ends are rounded.
  - The 2pt divider is carved out of each SOLID fill's trailing edge with a Rectangle().frame(width:2)
    .blendMode(.destinationOut) under a .compositingGroup(); destinationOut erases to whatever is
    behind the bar, so the divider reads against any container colour (watchOS canvas is black).
  - Divider is applied ONLY to solid dashes (guarded `dash == .solid`): two touching outline boxes
    already show a 2pt boundary where their inset strokeBorders meet, so punching them too just knocked
    the right wall off every empty tick (first attempt looked like open "C" boxes — fixed).
  - `spacing` property kept (default 2) but repurposed as the divider width, not HStack spacing.
- No test changes: DashBarTests only pin DashBarLayout.dashes arithmetic, untouched.
- Files changed: Sources/DashBar.swift, prd.json, progress.txt.
- Verified: build green (Series 11 46mm), full suite 2598 tests pass. Screenshot recipe (see below)
  at /tmp/us195_final.png + zoom /tmp/zz2_big.png confirm STEP/KCAL/Zz/EXER and the four currency
  bars all render as one solid bar split by thin lines, empty portion as closed touching ticks.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - SCREENSHOT RECIPE that worked: on a freshly `xcrun simctl erase`d Series 11 46mm
    (BA425DD4-8856-4933-8198-0E4B89960E48), launch with `-noNotificationPrompt -healthAnswered
    -sleepBarDemo`. `-noNotificationPrompt` alone is NOT enough on a device with a stale pending
    notification alert — you must ERASE first (the alert survives reinstall). `-healthAnswered`
    bypasses the HealthKit onboarding gate (the "Feed Your Digimon / Steps → Strength" intro screen),
    `-sleepBarDemo` seeds a Child Agumon with 6 banked sleep hours so the main screen (with all dash
    bars) renders. GUI clicking via AppleScript/System Events does NOT work here — the Mac screen is
    not capturable (`screencapture` fails) and System Events sees 0 Simulator windows, so the ONLY way
    to reach a screen is a launch-arg demo, never a tap. Crop/zoom with `sips -c H W --cropOffset TOP LEFT`.
  - destinationOut + compositingGroup is the clean way to draw a "divider that shows the background"
    in a segmented bar without hardcoding a background colour.

## 2026-07-24 - US-196: Energy bars leave the screen; map-step and Zz dash bars stay
- Replaced the three STEP/KCAL/EXER energy bars on the main screen with two stacked DashBar lines.
  - New Sources/MainReadingBars.swift: `MainReadingBars` draws line 1 = map steps (green, figure.walk
    leading label) and line 2 = Zz sleep (secondary). `MainStepBar.filled(recorded:total:dashes:)` is
    free-standing testable arithmetic — a map is tens of thousands of steps across, so the reading is
    the fraction walked drawn over a FIXED 16 dashes (matched to `sleepHoursDisplayCap` so the two
    lines are the same length), floored so it never reads a step early, clamped so an overshoot
    (finished maps are not capped at totalSteps) can't draw a phantom dash. `MainReadingBarLayout`
    holds the sizes (label width 21 matches EnergyBarLayout.nameWidth, barHeight 5 matches the
    currency bars).
  - Sources/ContentView.swift: the `if let progress = model.energyProgress { EnergyBarsView(...) }`
    block became `if let strip = model.mapStrip, model.state != nil { MainReadingBars(...) }`. Gated on
    state like the currency row so no lone bar draws pre-hatch; map numbers come from the same
    MapStrip the strip reads, so a credited step moves both.
  - Sources/MapStripView.swift: MapStrip gained `recordedSteps`/`totalSteps` Ints (the numbers
    progressText spelled). The strip view dropped `Image(systemName: strip.symbol)` (the figure.walk
    travelling icon) AND the `Text(strip.progressText)` step count — the strip is now just the map
    name (colour still carries prompt vs travelling) + party button. Removed the now-redundant
    `.accessibilityValue(strip.progressText)`.
- EnergyBarsView.swift is UNCHANGED and its `EnergyBarsView` view struct is now unused by the app, but
  the file stays: `EnergyProgress`, `EnergyGoal`, `EnergyBarLayout`, the `EvolutionNode.energyProgress`
  extension and `model.energyProgress` are all still live model+test API (EnergyBarsTests, the detail
  view's sleep bar). Deleting only the view struct would orphan its private EnergyBarRow/SleepDashBarRow.
- Files: Sources/MainReadingBars.swift (new), Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/MapStripView.swift,
  Tests/MainReadingBarsTests.swift (new, 8 tests), prd.json, progress.txt.
- Verified: build green (Series 11 46mm); full suite 2605 pass (was 2598). Screenshots at
  /tmp/us196/{main,desert,cyber}.png + zoom /tmp/us196/{bars,d,c}_big.png show exactly two dash-bar
  lines above the action area (map walk bar, then Zz), the strip reading just "Grassland"/"Desert"/
  "Cyberpunk" with no walk icon and no count, and no STEP/KCAL/EXER bars anywhere.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - The map-step bar reads FULL in every -mapDemo screenshot (grassland 3000, desert 16000, cyberpunk
    50000 all fill 16/16), because with -healthAnswered the sim credits a large synthetic STEP total to
    the currently-selected map via US-118's MapStepCreditor. It is NOT an always-full bug: the Zz bar,
    the same DashBar component with a different value, renders 6/16 in the same shot, and the arithmetic
    (empty/half/full/overshoot) plus an end-to-end MapStrip.make→bar no-swap check are pinned in
    MainReadingBarsTests. If a future story needs a PARTIAL map-bar screenshot, no shipped map is large
    enough to out-scale the sim's step credit — you'd need a demo flag that seeds recorded < total.
  - A `DashBar`'s own accessibilityLabel is only "N of M"; wrap it (as MainReadingBars' ReadingRow does
    with accessibilityElement(.ignore) + label/value) whenever the bar needs a spoken meaning.
  - `MainReadingBarLayout.dashes` is deliberately == `MainScreenModel.sleepHoursDisplayCap` (16) and a
    test pins the equality — the two reading lines must stay the same length to read as a pair.

  default 0/0 so pre-existing test call sites compile unchanged). Overlaid a `DashRing` on the Train

  row — only the orange **meat** bar remains (meat has no single per-tap button to ring). Passed the
  three charge pairs into `ActionControls`.

  Updated the two tests that pinned 2: `ConsumptionConfigTests.testNamedConstantsMatchThePRD` and
  `CleaningChargeTests.testTheBarReadsTheProfileCountAndTheConfigCap`.

  battle + a little poop so both spending buttons are enabled) so the rings are screenshottable.

  /tmp/us199/rings.png shows red Train ring, blue Clean ring, purple Battle ring, and the single
  remaining orange meat bar above the grid.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - `simctl erase` FAILS silently-ish on a BOOTED device — the stale notification permission alert
    then survives every relaunch and `-noNotificationPrompt` cannot help (the alert is a system modal
    the app never requested this run, it just persisted). Recipe: `simctl shutdown` -> `erase` ->
    `boot` -> `install` -> `launch ... -noNotificationPrompt`. Then wait ~10s: the app shows a
    ProgressView spinner for several seconds before the main screen, so the first screenshot after
    launch can catch the loading state.
  - To draw a value bar AROUND a button without disturbing the grid: use `.overlay { DashRing(...) }`.
    An overlay never changes the button's layout size or the HStack spacing; size the ring inside its
    own `.frame` (slightly larger than the face) and it extends symmetrically past the content.
  - `ActionControls` now carries the three spend charges. Its charge params are DEFAULTED 0/0 on
    purpose so the older `ActionControlsTests` constructors (which don't pass them) still compile and
    simply draw no ring — add-with-defaults beats touching every call site.

## 2026-07-24 - US-200: A Digimon's age shown as '1Y' beside the battle record
- New persisted `hatchedDate: Date?` on `GameState` (`Sources/GameState.swift`): the instant the
  Digitama hatched into Baby I, distinct from `birthDate` (stamped when the EGG is created — an egg
  spends real time accruing energy before it cracks). OPTIONAL for the standard SwiftData
  migration reason; `nil` reads as 0Y (an egg not yet hatched, a save from before this, or a
  Jogress result born past the egg stage).
- `GameState.ageYears(now:)`: whole elapsed 24-hour periods since `hatchedDate` (matching `Death`'s
  lifespan reckoning), clamped to 0 for nil/backward clock. One "year" per real day.
- `MainScreenModel.hatchIfReady` stamps `state.hatchedDate = now()` right after `advance(...)` — in
  the ONE hatch-specific path, NOT in the shared `advance`, so an evolution never resets age.
- `Freeze.shiftTimeline` shifts `hatchedDate` with the rest of the timeline, so a frozen Digimon
  does not age.
- `MainScreenModel.ageYears` computed off the injected clock; `StatsStrip` (`Sources/ContentView.swift`)
  gained a defaulted `ageYears` param and draws `\(ageYears)Y` right after the `0W 0L` record with a
  matching `accessibilityValue` ("... N years old"). `-wanderDemo` now stamps hatchedDate to 3 days
  ago so the strip screenshots a real `3Y`.
- Tests: `GameStateTests` age suite (0Y fresh + unhatched, increments once per whole day, clamps on a
  backward clock, `hatchedDate` round-trips through disk) and `EggHatchingTests`
  testHatchingStampsTheHatchDateAndAgeCountsFromIt (real hatch stamps the date; a mutable clock wound
  one day forward makes `model.ageYears` read 1) + an unhatched-egg control.
- Verified: build green (Series 11 46mm); full suite 2610 tests, 0 failures. Screenshot
  /tmp/us200/age5.png shows `STR 0  PWR 25  0W 0L  3Y`.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - **DerivedData ambiguity wasted a screenshot loop.** This checkout has THREE
    `~/Library/Developer/Xcode/DerivedData/DigiVPet-*` directories, and `find ... DigiVPet.app | head -1`
    (and even `ls -dt`) can pick a STALE bundle from a different one, so `simctl install` installs old
    code and the change looks missing on screen while the source is correct. Fix: build AND install
    from an explicit `-derivedDataPath` (e.g. `-derivedDataPath /tmp/dd`) so the installed `.app` is
    provably the one just built. Do this for every screenshot verification.
  - The watch simulator also gates the main screen behind a HealthKit authorization intro screen
    ("Feed Your Digimon ... Never leaves this watch"). Launch with `-healthAnswered` (a
    `StubHealthAuthorizer.Outcome` in `Sources/HealthAuthorization.swift`; siblings `-healthDenied`,
    `-healthUnavailable`) to walk straight onto the main screen. Combine with `-wanderDemo`
    `-noNotificationPrompt`.
  - Adding a time-derived `GameState` field is a THREE-line contract: the optional property, a line
    in `Freeze.shiftTimeline` (or a frozen Digimon keeps aging/hungering), and a stamp at the one
    lifecycle moment that owns it. `advance` is shared by hatch AND evolve — stamp hatch-only fields
    in `hatchIfReady`, not `advance`.
  - `xcodebuild`'s incremental builder here intermittently serves a STALE module to the test target
    ("Value of type 'GameState' has no member ...") even though the app target compiled the new
    member. A `xcodebuild clean` before the test run fixes it.

- A wild encounter now interrupts the main screen when the player has walked 500 steps into their

  (`Sources/WildEncounterView.swift`) with FLEE/BATTLE buttons, shown as an overlay in
  `ContentView` mutually exclusive with the battle overlay.
- `PlayerProfile` (`Sources/PlayerProfile.swift`): per-map `encounterMarkerStorage` (recorded-step
  total at the last encounter) and `metStorage` (residents met), both inline-`[:]` defaulted so old
  saves migrate for free. New `reduceRecorded(steps:forMap:)` (floors at 0 — the one place map
  progress goes DOWN), `encounterMarker`/`setEncounterMarker`, `metDigimon`/`hasMet`/`recordMet`.
- `MainScreenModel`: `@Published pendingWildEncounter`; `checkForWildEncounter()` (runs at the tail
  of every `refresh()`, gated on nothing-else-on-screen + alive + map selected + a met opponent from
  the map pool via `BattleMatchmaker.choose`); `fleeWildEncounter()` (500 penalty, marker moves to
  the new total, refuse+recoil pose, saves); `acceptWildEncounter()` (fights, win=recordMet + no
  penalty, loss=500 penalty, hands the bout to `pendingBattle` to replay, saves).
- Refactor: pulled the whole matchup/HP/agility/element/meat fight out of `finishBattleRound` into a
  shared `resolveBattle(player:opponent:result:using:)` so the pre-battle round (US-093) and the wild
  encounter fight the identical fight from a carried seed — no second copy that could drift.
- New `-wildEncounterDemo` launch flag (Agumon on the first map, 600 steps recorded, shipped check
  run) for the screenshot.
- Verified: build green (Series 11 46mm); 9 WildEncounterTests pass; full suite 2619 tests, 0
  failures. Screenshot /tmp/us201/wild.png shows "A wild Tsunomon!" with Flee/Battle.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - The app bundle id is `com.digivpet.DigiVPet` (NOT com.example.*) — `simctl launch` needs the real
    one; read it with `PlistBuddy -c "Print :CFBundleIdentifier" <app>/Info.plist` if unsure.
  - US-202 ("map residents are '?' until met") is already half-built here: `PlayerProfile.hasMet` /
    `recordMet` / `metDigimon(forMap:)` exist and a wild WIN already records a meeting. US-202 mostly
    needs the "met on the encounter occurring" + 500-step-meeting paths and the `MapDetailView` art
    gate + a render test.
  - To share the fight between two entry points, resolve into a replayable `BattleBout` and set
    `pendingBattle`; the encounter carries the same `SeededGenerator` it drew the opponent from
    (mirrors `PendingBattleRound`), so one seed pins one whole bout across pick-then-fight.

  records met the instant the encounter surfaces) and FIGHTING it (`acceptWildEncounter` records met

    reinstall clears the container for a clean demo. Prefer demo hooks that DON'T write to the save
    (a context/met literal unioned at read time, like `mapDetailDemoMet`/`mapDetailDemoDiscoveries`),
    exactly so they leave no residue for the next screenshot.

  "Boss: Patamon!" with a single Battle button (no flee).
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - "Finished" (PlayerProfile.finishedAt/isFinished/markFinished) now means BOSS BEATEN, not step
    total. UI unlock/checkmark tests set finishedAt directly and are unaffected; only US-118's
    step-finish tests changed.
  - A map's "residents to meet" and its "boss" come from MapOpponentBand.residents/.boss — the same
    non-dexOnly, exclude-player universe wild encounters draw from, so every gate condition is
    actually reachable.
  - Sim screenshot recipe for a game screen: launch with `-noNotificationPrompt -healthAnswered`
    (StubHealthAuthorizer .answered skips the health gate straight to .ready) plus the demo flag.
    Without -healthAnswered you hit the un-scriptable HealthKit system sheet; without
    -noNotificationPrompt you hit the un-scriptable notification prompt. Each demo seed runs in
    start(), i.e. after the health gate.
  - A boss/wild loss sets pendingBattle (the loss replays); checkForBossEncounter is guarded against
    a pending battle, so a test must finishBattle() before re-checking the trigger.

## 2026-07-24 - US-204 (Step/metric accounting is never doubled, and it is documented)
- Documentation + verification story. Double-checked the accounting: no gap found. Steps,
  calories, exercise and sleep are already credited by today's DELTA against a stored, persisted
  baseline (never the raw daily total), so re-opening within a day credits zero and a day rollover
  re-baselines without back-crediting yesterday.
- Files changed:
  - docs/metric-accounting.md (new) — the today's-delta rule; the two ledgers (EnergyLedger for the
    four energy currencies with EnergyRates caps, MetricLedger for raw ConditionMetric totals with
    no cap); why two ledgers reading one metric is NOT double counting (a step is 1 Strength-energy
    AND 1 map-step, different units); MetricLedger.claim as the single de-dup site; the one-read /
    one-claim wiring in MainScreenModel.refresh() (map/train/clean/sleep spend the deltas
    MetricCreditor returns, never claim twice); the widget-reads-the-snapshot rule
    (ComplicationSnapshot.swift:101); a per-metric table for steps/calories/exercise/sleep; and the
    full list of tests that pin each AC.
  - README.md — Layout-table pointer to the new doc.
- Verified: xcodegen + build green (Series 11 46mm). Accounting test classes all pass:
  MetricCreditingTests, MetricTotalsPersistenceTests, MetricLedgerWiringTests, EnergyCreditingTests,
  EnergyLedgerPersistenceTests.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - TEST CLASS NAMES DO NOT MATCH FILE NAMES. `-only-testing:DigiVPetTests/<Class>` filters by
    CLASS, so filtering by the file's basename silently runs a subset (or nothing). Map:
    Tests/MetricTotalsTests.swift -> classes MetricCreditingTests + MetricTotalsPersistenceTests;
    Tests/MetricWiringTests.swift -> MetricConditionReachTests + MetricLedgerWiringTests;
    Tests/EnergyCreditingTests.swift -> EnergyRatesTests + EnergyCreditingTests +
    EnergyLedgerPersistenceTests + HealthEnergySourceTests. Grep `final class .*: XCTestCase` to get
    the real names before using -only-testing.
  - The double-credit guarantee lives in TWO persisted @Model ledgers, each with its own per-day
    baseline: EnergyLedger (currency, capped by EnergyRates.dailyCapPerEnergyType) and MetricLedger
    (raw metric totals, uncapped). MetricLedger.claim(_:dayTotal:now:) is the single place the metric
    de-dup rule lives — map/train/clean/sleep all SPEND the deltas MetricCreditor.credit returns
    rather than claiming a second baseline. Adding any new consumer of a metric must spend a returned
    delta, never call claim itself.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-205 (Best-effort background step check raising a wild-battle notification)
- Split foreground vs background in the one shared refresh path: `MainScreenModel.refresh(background:)`
  now takes a flag (default false). At the tail, a foregrounding still runs `checkForWildEncounter()`
  (the on-screen BATTLE/FLEE dialog, US-201); a background wake runs the new
  `notifyWildEncounterIfDue()`, which raises a `.wildBattle` local notification when steps are >=500
  past `PlayerProfile.encounterMarker` for the selected map. Mutually exclusive by design.
- Background wakes pass `background: true` from `BackgroundRefreshCoordinator.performRefresh()`
  (BGAppRefreshTask) and `healthDataChanged()` (HealthKit observer — the timelier path, fires when
  steps actually land).
- Dedup: new persisted `PlayerProfile.wildBattleNotifiedMarker` (per map), stamped with the
  current encounterMarker ONLY on actual delivery and saved, so one crossing = one nudge even across
  process death. A crossing held back by sleep or a switched-off toggle is left unstamped, so a later
  wake still delivers it. Guarded on nothing else pending (encounter/boss/battle/round/training/
  evolution/memorial), a live map, and a non-dead Digimon — a boss due at the same time wins, same as
  the dialog. New `NotificationKind.wildBattle` (default on; `firesWhileAsleep` false).
- Tap-to-open: surfacing the dialog on the next foregrounding calls `notifications.cancel(.wildBattle)`
  to withdraw the now-stale nudge (like cleaning withdraws the mess notice). No deep-link plumbing —
  tapping a local notification launches the app, whose foreground refresh re-derives the encounter.
- Files: Sources/Notifications.swift (new kind + gates/strings), Sources/PlayerProfile.swift (marker
  storage/accessors/init/clearForDemo), Sources/MainScreenModel.swift (refresh flag,
  notifyWildEncounterIfDue, cancel on surface), Sources/BackgroundRefresh.swift (background:true on
  both wake paths), docs/background-wild-battle.md (new), README.md (Layout pointer),
  Tests/WildBattleNotificationTests.swift (new, 9 tests + SpyNotificationDeliverer fixture).
- Verified: xcodegen + build green (Series 11 46mm). WildBattleNotificationTests 9/9 pass; FULL suite
  2642 tests, 0 failures. The `NotificationSettingsView` toggle row appears for free off
  `allCases`, so the user gets a Wild Battles toggle with no view change.
- SIMULATOR LIMITATION (manual note, AC5): the end-to-end "watch notices 500 real steps on its own
  and buzzes" path is device-only. HealthKit is empty in the Simulator so the observer path has
  nothing to observe, and `scheduleBackgroundRefresh` is not honoured on a real schedule there (you
  can force one BGAppRefreshTask via Xcode Debug > Simulate Background Fetch, but not the cadence or
  budgeting, which are hardware behaviour). All logic decidable without the OS scheduler is covered by
  the tests, which seed the map counter and call refresh(background:) directly.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - `refresh()` is the SINGLE path a foregrounding and a background wake share (see
    BackgroundRefreshCoordinator). To make background behave differently from foreground, thread a flag
    THROUGH refresh() rather than adding a second code path — the whole point of the shared path is
    that the rules never fork. `refresh(background:)` is the pattern.
  - Notification dedup that must survive process death needs a PERSISTED marker on a @Model
    (PlayerProfile/GameState) + a save(); an in-memory flag only dedups within one launch. Stamp the
    marker on DELIVERY (use NotificationDispatcher.send's Bool return), not on decision, so a
    sleep/toggle-suppressed notice is retried rather than silently spent — the mirror of
    claimPoopNotification but gated on real delivery.
  - Adding a NotificationKind is nearly free: NotificationSettingsView and SettingsView drive off
    `NotificationKind.allCases`, so the toggle appears automatically. But `firesWhileAsleep` and the
    switch statements in Notifications.swift are exhaustive — the compiler forces you to handle the
    new case in each, which is the safety net. Default `firesWhileAsleep` to false unless the notice
    ONLY makes sense at night.

  Chaosdramon and Chaosmon: they begin with C (out of S-Z range) AND their device trees pin them to
  NO node (Jogress results), so they stay orphaned by design and the top rung is otherwise spent.
  Overall playable orphans 35 -> 18 (16 Armor-Hybrid remain for US-169). Validator: zero findings.
- Added Tests/UltimateSweepSToZTests.swift (xcodegen generate AFTER writing it; grep confirmed it
  bundled). Build green; all 2665 tests pass.

**Learnings for future iterations (US-169 is the LAST sweep - Armor-Hybrid):**
- THE S-Z (or any letter) RANGE INCLUDES ALREADY-WIRED ULTIMATES. `roster.entries.filter { .ultimate
  && S..Z }` returned 35, not 17 - eighteen were wired by device trees / earlier sweeps. The range
  test must partition into `Set(swept) union alreadyWired`, exactly like NToR's. My first draft
  asserted the range == my seventeen and failed at 35 != 17. Copy NToR's partition, not a bare equality.
- `roster.entries` (Roster.bundled = roster.json, one per SHEET) differs from roster.generated.json
  (Appendix B, mirrors evolutions.json aliases and all): the S-Z band is 35 sheets vs 42 generated
  ids. Count the RANGE test off roster.entries; count ORPHANS off roster.generated.json.
- THE KNOCK-ON FOR A 17-NODE ULTIMATE SWEEP WAS 78 FAILING TESTS ACROSS ~25 FILES, all mechanical:
  (1) `graph.nodes.count, 898` -> 915 (22 files); (2) `nodes(at: .ultimate).count, 219` -> 236 (7);
  (3) per-line `sizes["<line>"], N` in every `testTheSweepOpenedNoNewLines` for the 10 touched lines
  (wanyamon 31->33, penc-sw 23->26, penc-vb 61->62, penc-nsp 46->47, penc-me 74->75, penc-wg 50->53,
  dmc-v4 35->36, penc-nso 84->86, dmc-v3 56->58, commandramon 15->16); (4) EvolutionGraphTests' whole
  byLine dict (colon form, edit by hand); (5) each UltimateSweep*Tests' "bucketFell"/"handsTo" reads
  the CURRENT orphan bucket, now 2 (CToD's jogress-adjusted remainder now 0); (6) five Pendulum tree
  `testEveryNodeInTheLineIsReachableFromItsDigitama` inLine.count bumps + their orphan-removal counts;
  (7) the single-climb dicts (PerfectSweepSToZ branchedByUS163, PerfectSweepM branchedBySweeps,
  UltimateSweepAToB forkedLater, UltimateSweepEToH's hardcoded vamdemon==3->4); (8) climb-list
  assertions (AdultSweepSToT metalgreymon_x, AdultSweepUToZ canoweissmon x2, PerfectSweepAToC/NToR
  pandamon, PerfectSweepNToR wanyamon Mega set); (9) SeedRosterTests patamon set (dmc-v3: WarGreymon
  X, Yukinamon) + piyomon set (dmc-v4: UltimateBrachimon) - APPEND, never widen; (10) three penc-sw
  nodes into EvolutionCriteriaTests.strandedUltimate, comments MUST say "Saiyu Warriors".
- SCRIPTING GOTCHA that cost one build cycle: a python batch that edits several files and asserts
  per line will, on a mis-guessed line number, throw AFTER editing earlier files in that run but
  BEFORE writing the current file - so every file listed AFTER the failing one is silently skipped.
  Re-run leaves three inLine.count bumps unapplied. Apply per-file with its own write, or verify each
  file changed on disk before moving on.
- vamdemon already had a duplicate-energy-free set of 3; etemon (dmc-v3) ships with TWO vitality
  edges (bancholeomon + kingetemon), so DO NOT fork etemon - `testNoPerfectThisStoryForkedOffers...`
  would inherit its pre-existing collision. Check the parent's own energies before choosing it.

## 2026-07-24 - US-169 (Orphan sweep: Armor-Hybrid)
- Wired all 16 playable Armor-Hybrid orphans into the evolution graph as terminal apex forms.
- Each takes an EARNED in-edge (2 hinted criteria, requiredEnergy the parent had free) from a
  Digitama-REACHABLE Child on that Child's line, so no edge crosses a line and every form is
  genuinely obtainable, not stranded behind a parent with no egg.
  - adventure02: goldv-dramon, submarimon, rapidmon_armor (V-mon); daipenmon, manbomon, shadramon (Wormmon)
  - commandramon: bitmon, raihimon, rhinomon (Commandramon)
  - vital: beowolfmon, kaisergreymon, duskmon (Pulsemon); velgrmon, lynxmon (Kokabuterimon); kaiserleomon, sheepmon (Sunarizamon)
- Armor-Hybrid is off the ladder (Stage.armorHybrid.ladderIndex == nil) and the top of its own side
  branch, so — exactly like the terminal Ultimates US-163..US-168 — each is an in-edge and nothing
  above. No out-edges: a fallback out-edge would have to be an unconditional junk edge to nowhere.
- Appendix B orphan count, stage Armor-Hybrid: BEFORE 16, AFTER 0. Overall playable orphans 18 -> 2
  (only the two device-pinned Chaos Ultimates remain).
- Files: Resources/{evolutions,elements,moves}.json (+16 nodes / element / move entries, +16 earned
  parent edges), scripts/us169_wire_armor_hybrid.py (data authoring), Tests/ArmorHybridSweepTests.swift
  (new), plus pinned-test updates across ~30 test files (node count 915->931, line sizes
  adventure02 24 / commandramon 19 / vital 49, dead-end ledger 58->74, Armor-Hybrid orphan bucket
  16->0, ChildSweep branch counts, BabyII onward-rung, PerfectSweepM's Velgrmon-is-now-a-node claim).
- EvolutionGraphValidator: ZERO findings. Full suite: 2678 tests, 0 failures.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- `UltimateSweepSToZTests.testNoEdgeCrossesALine` is a GLOBAL invariant: every edge's target must
  share its source's `line`. A new node's line MUST equal its parent's line; out-edges can only point
  within the same line. This is why the Armor forms group by parent line, not by theme.
- `SeedRosterTests` global rules a sweep must satisfy: every node with edges has exactly one
  isDefault edge; a fallback (isDefault) edge must have EMPTY conditions ("a junk fallback may not be
  gated" — also pinned in DMCVersion5TreeTests); every non-Digitama edge names a requiredEnergy.
  So a conditioned isDefault edge is illegal — I dropped an intended Duskmon->Velgemon chain over it.
- The "dead-end ledger" (`graph.nodes.filter { evolutions.isEmpty && stage != .ultimate }.count`) is
  asserted as a literal in ~10 Perfect/Ultimate sweep tests AND as an explicit id LIST in
  `ChildSweepAToFTests.testTheOnlyDeadEndsBelowUltimate...`. Any new terminal non-Ultimate node lands
  on both; update the count everywhere and add the ids to the list.
- Line node counts are pinned in `EvolutionGraphTests.testBundledNodesAreTaggedWithTheirLine` and in
  per-sweep `sizes[...]` assertions. Adding to a line means updating both.
- Device-tree lines (dmc-v1..v5, penc-*) have full tree-shape tests (targets/counts per Rookie); the
  "extra" lines (adventure02, commandramon, vital, tamers, wanyamon, ...) do not, so they are the
  safest parents to extend — but their Children are still counted in the ChildSweep `branchedByALater
  Sweep` dicts and `EvolutionCriteria`'s Digitama-reachability (avoid stranded parents like ryudamon).
- Signature names in moves.json must be GLOBALLY unique; projectileSymbol+tint pairs unique PER LINE.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-206 (A map's Digitama conditions measure progress on that map, not globally)
- A map's egg now asks "what have you done HERE", not "what have you ever done". Before this, the
  map detail and the drop engine were both judged on a `ConditionContext(state:)` built from the
  Digimon's stage/lifetime totals, so a veteran arriving in a fresh map found its slots already
  satisfied and marked "Ready to find" before walking a step there.
- THE COUNTERS (`Sources/PlayerProfile.swift`): two new stored dictionaries — `mapMetricStorage`
  (map id -> MetricTotals.values) and `mapBattleWinStorage` (map id -> wins). API: `mapMetrics(forMap:)`,
  `stepsWalked(forMap:)`, `battlesFought(forMap:)`, `battlesWon(forMap:)`, `credit(_:forMap:)` (a
  whole MetricTotals delta set, or one ConditionMetric), `recordBattle(won:forMap:)`. Nothing writes
  a non-positive amount, so "absent means never credited" stays true and an unwalked map answers
  `health.steps` `.unknown` rather than a 0 that would satisfy an `atMost` gate.
  On PlayerProfile and NOT GameState (the AC says "via GameState" loosely): every other per-map fact
  already lives here, and GameState is deleted whole on death — map progress must outlive a Digimon.
- THE CREDITING (`Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`), always to the map SELECTED AT THE MOMENT, which
  is what makes leakage impossible rather than merely unlikely:
  - `creditMapMetrics(creditedMetrics)` in `refresh()`, off the SAME deltas `MetricCreditor` claimed
    (a second SPENDER of one claim, never a second claim — the US-204 rule).
  - `creditMapCare(.careTrainingSessions)` at `train()`'s `.started`, `.careOverfeeds` at `feed()`'s
    `.refused`, `.careSleepDisturbances` in `wakeIfAsleep()`.
  - `profile.recordBattle(won:forMap:)` in `finishBattle()` — the one site every battle (ordinary,
    wild, boss) resolves through. Fought and won move together, so the ratio can never exceed 1.
- THE READING (`Sources/MapScopedContext.swift`, new): `ConditionContext.mapScoped(_:profile:
  lightState:readings:)`. ALL THREE WINDOWS read the map's running total — a map is a place, not a
  span of anybody's life, so `health.steps day atLeast 2000` means "walk 2,000 steps in this map".
  `lightState` and `readings` stay global (a NOW reading and the standing measurements a running
  total cannot hold have no per-map version). Care counters flatten to a real 0; health metrics stay
  `.unknown` until credited.
- WIRED AT TWO SEAMS, deliberately the same value: `mapDetailContext(for:)` (was a computed global
  property, now a function of the map id) and `checkForDigitamaDrop`. So what the detail promises is
  exactly what can drop.
- Files: Sources/PlayerProfile.swift, Sources/MapScopedContext.swift (new), Sources/MainScreenModel.swift,
  Tests/MapScopedProgressTests.swift (new, 17 tests in 3 classes), Tests/DigitamaDropTests.swift
  (3 tests reseeded), docs/metric-accounting.md.
- Verified: xcodegen + build green; FULL suite 2695 tests, 0 failures. The AC6 regression
  (`testProgressIsEarnedPerMapAndSurvivesSwitchingAway`) walks alpha -> meet -> beta not met ->
  back to alpha still met, on the SAME condition in both maps so the result cannot be about which
  criterion was picked. Clock injected (`now: { Fixture.morning }`) throughout; nothing waits.
- NOT screenshotted: no AC asked for one, and the demo flag (`-mapDetailDemo`) short-circuits to a
  literal context so it would photograph the stand-in rather than the new path. The screen's own
  seam is asserted instead — `model.mapDetail(for:)` -> `detail.digitama[0].isReady`.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **THREE SETS OF TOTALS NOW EXIST AND THEY ARE NOT INTERCHANGEABLE.** `GameState.stage/lifetime
  MetricTotals` (the Digimon's life, what an EVOLUTION is judged on), `PlayerProfile.recorded(forMap:)`
  (progress toward a map's BOSS, which a flee/loss takes 500/1,000 off), and
  `PlayerProfile.mapMetrics(forMap:)` (what was earned while that map was selected, what a map's EGG
  is judged on, and which only ever goes up). Adding a new gate means choosing one on purpose.
- **THE "SECOND SPENDER, NEVER A SECOND CLAIM" RULE EXTENDS CLEANLY.** `MetricCreditor.credit`
  RETURNS its claimed deltas; any new per-metric consumer takes that return value as a parameter and
  never touches `MetricLedger.claim` itself. `creditMapMetrics` is the fourth consumer wired this way
  (after map steps, train charges, clean charges) and cost no new de-dup reasoning at all.
- **A "SCOPED" CONTEXT IS A CONSTRUCTOR, NOT A NEW WINDOW.** The temptation was to add a `.map` case
  to `ConditionWindow`; that would have touched the validator, `answerableWindows`, every hint string
  and all authored JSON. Building a different `ConditionContext` from different counters changed
  nothing about the vocabulary — same `ConditionReveal`, same `ConditionEvaluator`, same authored
  conditions — and is why the blast radius was 3 pre-existing tests.
- **TESTS THAT SEED A GLOBAL COUNTER TO DRIVE A MAP FEATURE ARE THE ONES THAT BREAK.** Exactly three
  did (`DigitamaDropModelTests`, all setting `model.state?.stageTrainingSessions = 1`); the fix is
  `model.profile?.credit(.careTrainingSessions, forMap: "<id>")`. Grep `stageTrainingSessions =` /
  `battleWins =` before assuming a fixture drives a map path.
- `HealthSampleFetching`'s method is `samples(of: QuantityMetric, in: DateInterval)` — the stub
  fetchers copied between test files are easy to mistype as `HealthMetric` and fail only at compile.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-207 (Win a battle to (maybe) find the egg, and the condition stays shown after you have it)
- Meeting a map slot's conditions no longer GIVES you the egg — it makes the egg **findable**, and
  each battle **won** in that map is one look for it, at a coin flip. Two changes, one rule.
- THE ROLL (`Sources/DigitamaDrop.swift`): `DigitamaDropEngine.winDropChance = 0.5` and
  `findsTheEgg(chance:using:)`, an `inout G: RandomNumberGenerator` draw kept SEPARATE from `award`
  because the two answer different questions — `award` says WHICH egg is on offer, this says whether
  the player gets a look at all.
- THE GATE (`Sources/MainScreenModel.swift`): `checkForDigitamaDrop()` is called from ONE place now,
  `finishBattle()`, wrapped in `if bout.report.playerWon`. The US-128 calls in `refresh()` (after the
  step accrual) and in `finishTraining()` are gone. Inside the check the roll is drawn FIRST and
  unconditionally — one win draws one Double whatever the map holds, so a seeded generator forces the
  same branch regardless of the fixture — and the `guard findsIt` sits AFTER `award` but before any
  write, which is what makes a miss consume nothing (AC4).
- THE SCREEN (`Sources/MapDetailView.swift`): `DigitamaSlotDetail.conditions` is now always the
  slot's own (US-121 emptied it once revealed; that is reversed), plus a new `isHeld` fed from
  `GameStore.heldDigitamaIds()` via `MapDetail.make(held:)` and `MainScreenModel.mapDetailHeld`.
  A held row draws `checkmark.seal.fill` + "Found" in green (the app's finished glyph, not the ready
  sparkle) and its hint rows are drawn satisfied — `ConditionHintRow` gained an `isSatisfied: Bool =
  false` that pins the level to `.met`, defaulted off so every Dex row is untouched.
- Files: Sources/DigitamaDrop.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/MapDetailView.swift,
  Sources/DexView.swift, Tests/DigitamaDropTests.swift, Tests/MapDetailTests.swift,
  Tests/MapScopedProgressTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2705 tests, 0 failures**. AC9 screenshotted on 46mm
  (`-mapDetailSlotsDemo`, /tmp/us207/slots2.png): the held Agu Digitama row shows its real sprite,
  a green "Found", and a green-checked "Train it once" under it — art plus condition line, exactly
  what the AC asks — beside a "?" marked "Ready to find" and a third "?" still working.
- Tests added: engine — `testTheWinRollIsSeededAndAnswersBothWays`,
  `testTheChanceIsOneInTwoAndTheExtremesAreAbsolute`, `testAboutHalfOfManyWinsFindTheEgg`; model —
  forced-hit drops, forced-miss does not, miss-then-win drops (one model, seed QUEUE), a loss never
  drops, a refresh no longer drops, a train no longer drops; view — a revealed slot KEEPS its hint
  rows, a held slot is `isHeld` and keeps them, found glyph != ready glyph.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A drop seed is drawn per CHECK, so a test that needs two different outcomes in one run needs a
  seed QUEUE, not a seed.** `makeDropGenerator: () -> SeededGenerator` is called fresh at every
  check, so `SeedQueue` (a small class the escaping closure advances, holding its last value once
  exhausted) is how "miss this win, hit the next" is said. Measured seeds for `Double.random(in:
  0..<1)`: seed 1 -> 0.318 (a hit at 50%), seed 2 -> 0.757 (a miss). Reuse them.
- **Roll BEFORE you branch on the fixture.** Drawing the chance first and unconditionally makes the
  generator's draw order independent of whether a slot happened to be eligible; if the roll had sat
  inside the eligible branch, the same seed would mean different things in two tests.
- **A model test that hangs off a battle RESULT must decide the fight by the power gap, not the
  seed.** The pattern is `BossEncounterTests`': stage/strength on the player against a fixed pool
  (`.ultimate`/30 vs a Baby-I = sure win; `.babyI`/0 vs an Ultimate = sure loss), then assert
  `bout.report.playerWon` so a seed regression fails loudly instead of silently testing the other
  branch. `MapScopedProgressTests`' `foe` was retuned from Adult to Baby-I for exactly this.
- **`model.battle()` needs THREE things stocked or it silently returns nil and
  `finishBattleRound` hands back nil:** `battleCharges > 0`, a payable energy (`BattleCost.energy` =
  5 from `stageEnergy[.strength]`/`.stamina`), and no other minigame pending. Dropping the
  `stageEnergy` line from a fixture cost a full test-run cycle here.
- **THREE records of "the player has this egg" now exist and they are not interchangeable:**
  `dexIds()` (has EVER owned — never shrinks, `MapDetail.make(discovered:)`), `heldDigitamaIds()`
  (in the box RIGHT NOW — empties on hatch, `MapDetail.make(held:)` and the drop engine's refusal),
  and the slot's own conditions being met. `isRevealed` and `isHeld` are the screen's names for the
  first two; a held egg is always revealed, a revealed one need not be held.
- **A screenshot caught the AC6 defect again** (the same lesson US-121 learned): the "Found" row's
  hint drew an UNMET open circle, because `ConditionHintRow` was reading the live context — which for
  a held egg may have been reset by a hatch since. Value-level tests all passed. Forcing the level
  with `isSatisfied` is the fix; prefer a defaulted parameter on the shared row over a second row type.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-208 (The Feed button wears a meat ring like the others)
- The last currency that read somewhere other than its own button now reads on it. `ActionControls`
  gained `meat`/`meatCap` (defaulted 0/0, like US-199's six charge params, so every older call site
  compiles unchanged and simply draws no ring), an `.overlay { DashRing(filled: meat, total: meatCap,
  tint: .orange) }` on Feed, and `.accessibilityValue(chargeValue(meat, meatCap))` — the SAME helper
  the three charges speak through, not a second phrasing.
- `Sources/ContentView.swift`: the standalone `DashBar(filled: model.meat, ...)` is GONE. US-199 had
  left meat alone on a row of one because a pool is not a per-tap charge; a pool still has a count and
  a cap, so the row itself is now empty and deleted. Two reading bars remain above the grid (map steps,
  sleep), and the vertical space the row took goes back to the sprite.
- `-chargesDemo` seeds `profile.meat = min(13, config.meatCap)` so the orange ring is screenshottable
  beside the red/purple/blue three.
- Files: Sources/ActionControls.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift,
  Tests/ActionControlsTests.swift, Tests/FeedingTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2709 tests, 0 failures** (+4). AC5 screenshotted on 46mm
  (/tmp/us208/rings.png, and feed_zoom.png cropped 6x): an orange 20-segment ring around `fork.knife`
  with 13 solid ticks marching clockwise from 12 o'clock and 7 faint ones, and no meat bar anywhere.
- Tests added: `testFeedSpeaksItsMeatThroughTheSharedChargeValue` (7 of 20, the 0/full boundaries, an
  overshoot clamped to "20 of 20", and a 0-cap economy staying silent), `testTheMeatRingIsTheSameRing
  TheChargesUse` (diameter/lineWidth/gapDegrees equal to a charge ring's, diameter = face + 4),
  `testARowBuiltWithoutMeatCarriesNoRing`, and in FeedingTests `testTheMeatRingOnFeedFallsAsItIsSpent
  AndRisesAsItIsRefilled` — a real `model.feed()` through the real store, asserted on the numbers the
  ring is BUILT from (4 -> 3 on a meal, 20 on a refill, 0 when the larder blocks with "No meat").

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A ring's segment count is its CAP, and `meatCap` is 20 — twice any charge cap.** At the shipped
  8° gap on a 34pt ring that is 20 ticks of ~10° each: legible as a fill on screen, but visibly finer
  than the 8- and 10-segment rings beside it. US-212 ("every ring is 10 segments") is the story that
  reconciles this; do not "fix" the density by retuning `Resources/consumption.json`, which would move
  the economy to serve the drawing.
- **`accessibilityValue` is where a decorative ring speaks.** `DashRing` is `accessibilityHidden`, so
  a new ring that does not also add `chargeValue(...)` to its button is silently mute to VoiceOver —
  there is no test that catches this by construction, only one that asserts the string.
- **The currency row above the action grid no longer exists.** A future reading that wants a bar there
  is adding a row back, not appending to one; the `if model.state != nil` block now opens straight
  onto `ActionControls`.
- `FeedOutcome` has no `.noMeat` case — an empty larder is `.blocked(reason: "No meat — go battle.")`,
  and the funds check sits AFTER the refusal check, so a full Digimon refuses for free.
- Screenshot recipe held again, with the DerivedData rule that matters: `-derivedDataPath /tmp/dd208`
  on the build, install THAT bundle, `simctl shutdown` -> `erase` -> `boot` -> `install` -> `launch
  com.digivpet.DigiVPet -healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt -chargesDemo`, then throw away the first
  few screenshots (the app shows a spinner for several seconds). `sips -c H W --cropOffset Y X` then
  `sips -Z 400` is enough to eyeball a 30pt ring's fill without leaving the shell.

## 2026-07-24 - US-209 (Clean and Battle go back to their previous glyphs)
- A pure revert of US-197's two glyph choices, and ONLY the glyphs. Clean draws `"sparkles"` again
  (US-197 had drawn `ActionGlyph.waste`, a three-ellipse coil of droppings) and Battle draws
  `"bolt.fill"` again (US-197 had made it `figure.martial.arts`). AC3 is explicit that the tints stay
  as they are, so Clean keeps the `.brown` US-197 gave it — a brown sparkle, not the pre-US-197 teal
  one — and Battle keeps `.purple`, which never changed. Rings, `isCleanDisabled`/`isBattleDisabled`
  and both accessibility labels are untouched.
- AC4 ("recorded in a code comment so the revert is auditable") is answered with a named constant
  rather than a bare comment: a new non-generic `enum ActionSymbol { clean, battle }` whose doc lines
  carry the full three-step history (pre-US-197 -> US-197 -> US-209). Non-generic for the same reason
  `ActionButtonFace.diameter` is: `ActionControls` is generic over three destination types, so
  `ActionControls.cleanSymbol` would not infer at a test call site.
- Deleting the coil left `ActionGlyph` with one case and `WasteGlyph` with no callers, so both are
  gone and `ActionButtonFace` holds a plain `let systemImage: String` again — the exact shape it had
  before US-197. `PoopShape` (the mess on the ground) is a different type and is unaffected.
- Files: Sources/ActionControls.swift, Tests/ActionControlsTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2710 tests, 0 failures** (+1). AC5 screenshotted on 46mm
  (/tmp/us209/s6.png, zoom.png cropped): a brown four-point sparkle inside its blue 8-segment ring
  and a magenta bolt inside its purple one, side by side in row 1.
- Test added: `testCleanAndBattleWearTheirPreUS197Glyphs`, asserting the two `ActionSymbol` constants
  the faces are built from (a view body is unreachable from a test here).

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **"Keep their existing tints" in a revert story means the tints AT THE TIME OF THE STORY, not the
  ones from the era being reverted to.** US-197 changed Clean's glyph AND its tint (teal -> brown);
  US-209's AC3 lists tints among the things to keep, so only half of that pair came back. Read a
  revert AC for what it EXCLUDES — going "all the way back" would have failed AC3 and also collided
  with Party, which is `.teal` in row 2.
- **A view-body-only change still deserves a test, via the constant the body is built from.** There
  is no way to assert `Image(systemName:)` inside a SwiftUI body in this suite, so the pattern is:
  hoist the literal to a named non-generic constant, assert that. Same trick `ActionButtonFace
  .diameter` uses for geometry. Cheap, and it makes an "I preferred the old one" story regression-safe.
- **When a story removes the last caller of a helper, delete the helper in the same commit.** US-197's
  `ActionGlyph`/`WasteGlyph` existed solely because SF Symbols has no poop glyph; leaving them would
  have left a documented-as-used View that nothing draws. `ActionButtonFace(glyph:)` had no call site
  outside this file — grep before assuming that of any other helper.
- Screenshot recipe unchanged from US-208 and still reliable: build with `-derivedDataPath /tmp/ddNNN`,
  install THAT bundle, `simctl shutdown` -> `erase` -> `boot` -> `install` -> `launch
  com.digivpet.DigiVPet -healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt -chargesDemo`, discard the first few
  shots (multi-second spinner), then `sips -c H W --cropOffset Y X` + `sips -Z 500` to eyeball a 30pt
  glyph. The action grid's row 1 sits at roughly y=350, x=210 in a 46mm screenshot.

## 2026-07-24 - US-210 (The map name and Party button move off the sprite area into the grid)
- The map strip is deleted. `ContentView`'s `if let strip = model.mapStrip { MapStripView(...) }` block
  is gone, and with it the map's name floating under the sprite and the small `person.2.fill` beside
  it. US-197 had already given the action grid its own Map and Party circles, so this row was a second
  door to a screen the grid already opens plus a label nothing is gated on; the line of height it cost
  goes back to the Digimon.
- `Sources/MapStripView.swift` -> `Sources/MapStrip.swift` (git mv; `project.yml` globs `Sources`, so
  only a re-`xcodegen generate` was needed). The VIEW layer is deleted — `MapStripView`,
  `MapStripLayout`, `MapStripMarks`, and `MapStrip.symbol` / `MapStrip.accessibilityLabel`, which only
  the view read — and `import SwiftUI` became `import Foundation`. The VALUE survives because
  `MainReadingBars` fills the map-step `DashBar` from `strip.recordedSteps`/`strip.totalSteps`.
- `mapName` stays on `MapStrip`, undrawn, documented for the reason `progressText` already was (US-196
  left that one behind the same way): it is the single place this feature decides which map a save with
  no selection is invited towards (US-120 AC6), and what `MapStripTests` pins that rule against. AC5's
  "no dead mapName plumbing" is read as the view plumbing — the parameter chain — and that is all gone.
- `MainReadingBars` no longer takes `mapName`. Its map bar was the second place the name appeared under
  the sprite (spoken, as "Adventuring in Grassland"), so AC1's "remove the `mapName:` reading from that
  area" takes it too; the bar now speaks `MainReadingBarLayout.mapLabel` = "Map progress", which names
  the READING. Which map you are on is read off the map list.
- Stale comments repointed in `PartyView` ("pushed from the map strip's trailing button" -> "from the
  action grid's Party button"), `MainScreenModel.mapStrip`, and two `MapStripLayout`-referencing
  "named rather than left as literals" asides in `ContentView`/`PartyView`.
- Files: Sources/MapStrip.swift (renamed), Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/MainReadingBars.swift,
  Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/PartyView.swift, Tests/MapStripTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2707 tests, 0 failures** (-5 view-layer tests, +2). AC6
  screenshotted on 46mm (/tmp/us210/s3.png): "Agumon · Child" runs straight into the two reading bars —
  no map name, no party glyph — and the teal two-people button appears only in grid row 2.
- Tests: deleted `testTheTravellingAndPromptStatesUseDifferentGlyphs`,
  `testTheTwoStatesReadDifferentlyToVoiceOver` and the whole `MapStripLayoutTests` class (3 tests) with
  the code they described. Added `MapStripRemovalTests.testTheMapStepBarNoLongerNamesTheMap` (the bar's
  spoken label contains NO shipped map's `displayName` — absence made assertable) and
  `testTheGridsMapAndPartyButtonsCarryTheStripsTwoDestinations`, which builds `ActionControls` with the
  exact `mapDestination`/`partyDestination` expressions `ContentView` uses, then calls
  `list.select("second")` and `party.activate(mate)` and asserts the model moved.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A destination closure is testable: call it and drive the view it returns.** `controls
  .mapDestination()` hands back a real `MapListView` whose `select` is the model's `selectMap`, and
  `controls.partyDestination().activate(row)` really takes a Digimon out. That is how "no navigation
  is lost" stops being a screenshot-only claim — build the destinations with the SAME expressions
  `ContentView` passes, or the test proves nothing about the app.
- **Deleting a view leaves its value behind, and that is not automatically dead code.** `MapStrip` is
  now a pure reading with no strip; `mapName`/`progressText` are undrawn but are where the feature's
  wording and its "which map when none is chosen" rule live. The rule this codebase follows: delete a
  helper when its last CALLER goes (US-209), keep a value property when it is still the single place a
  DECISION is made — and say which, in the doc comment, so the next sweep does not re-litigate it.
- **A removal story's test is the thing that must now be ABSENT, restated as something assertable.**
  "No map name under the sprite" is a screenshot; "the map bar's VoiceOver label contains no shipped
  map's displayName" is a test, and it catches the regression that a screenshot would not (a name that
  is spoken but not drawn).
- **`xcrun simctl io <device> screenshot` silently writes nothing if `DEVELOPER_DIR` is not exported
  in THAT shell invocation.** Each Bash call starts a fresh shell, so a screenshot loop in a second
  command needs its own `export` — the failure is a zero-file directory, not an error message.
