## 2026-07-24 - US-211 (The action grid becomes a staggered, scrollable, list-style grid)
- New `ActionGridLayout` (in `Sources/ActionControls.swift`, free-standing and non-generic like
  `DashBarLayout`): `columns = 5`, `spacing = 4`, `cellPitch = 34`, `width = 166`,
  `rowCounts(forButtons:)`, `staggerOffset(forRow:)` and `height(forRows:)`. All six are USED by the
  body — no ornamental constants — and all six are asserted directly.
- `ActionControls.body` is now a `ScrollView(.vertical)` over a `VStack(alignment: .leading)` of two
  extracted row properties (`careRow`, `placesRow`), `.frame(width: ActionGridLayout.width,
  alignment: .leading)` so a short row is placed inside the FULL row's box rather than re-centred on
  its own buttons, with `placesRow.offset(x: staggerOffset(forRow: 1))`. The caption stays outside
  the scroll view so a refusal never scrolls away.
- The button SEQUENCE is untouched; it is only chunked five to a row instead of four, so Map is the
  fifth circle of row 1 rather than the first of row 2 (AC4). Every ring, `.disabled`, action closure
  and accessibility label moved with its button verbatim (AC5).
- Diameter stays **30** and AC2's "document the diameter constant chosen" is answered on
  `ActionButtonFace.diameter` with the arithmetic that actually binds: five faces and four gaps come
  to `5*30 + 4*4 = 166pt`, 10pt inside the 176pt of the narrowest screen; the 4pt gap is exactly the
  `DashRing` overhang (`diameter + 4`, 2pt each side) so two neighbouring rings MEET instead of
  overlapping; 32 — US-038's cap — would come to exactly 176pt with no margin AND overlapping rings.
  34pt of ring every 34pt of row is list-row scale; the list-row FEEL comes from the stagger and the
  scrolling, not from a taller button.
- Scroll cap: `.frame(maxHeight: height(forRows: rowCounts.count))` = 64pt for two rows, which is
  exactly `30 + 4 + 30` — the pre-US-211 height. So the sprite's slot is unchanged and
  `MainScreenLayoutTests`' pinned `SpriteScale` bands still hold (they do; suite green).
- Files: Sources/ActionControls.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift (comment only),
  Tests/ActionControlsTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2712 tests, 0 failures** (+5). Screenshots on BOTH sizes
  (/tmp/us211/46mm.png, /tmp/us211/42mm.png): row 1 is Feed, Train, Clean, Battle, Map; row 2 is
  Party, Light, Dex sitting in the notches between them; nothing clipped at either edge on either
  watch. Measured off the 46mm shot at @2x: row-1 centres 73/141/209/277/345px (68px = 34pt pitch),
  row-2 centres 107/175/243px — 34px = 17pt = exactly half a cell.
- Tests: renamed `testARowOfFourFitsTheNarrowestScreen` -> `testAFullRowFitsTheNarrowestScreen`
  (it now guards a row of FIVE), plus `testTheStaggeredRowStaysInsideAFullRowsWidth`,
  `testTheButtonsChunkFiveToARow`, `testTheSecondRowsCirclesSitBetweenTheFirstRows`,
  `testTheGridsHeightIsItsRowsAndNothingMore`, `testTheGapIsWideEnoughForTwoNeighbouringRingsToMeet`.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **AC1's "Row 2 holds 4" needs US-213's Sleep button, and the PRD says so itself.** US-211's own
  Context paragraph reads "appending the new Sleep button (US-213)" — the 5-and-4 split is the END
  state of US-211 + US-213, not of US-211 alone. A Sleep button here would have had no destination
  (US-214 builds the view) and so could only have been a stub, which the rules forbid. What US-211
  can own honestly is the ARRANGEMENT, so it is proven by test rather than by screenshot:
  `rowCounts(forButtons: 9) == [5, 4]`. **US-213 appends one `NavigationLink` to `placesRow` and
  bumps `ActionControls.buttonCount` from 8 to 9 — nothing else.** The height cap, the stagger and
  the scroll all follow from those two edits.
- **A ScrollView in a fixed VStack must be capped with `.frame(maxHeight:)` or it eats the sprite.**
  A bare `ScrollView` is greedy vertically and would have fought the sprite's `GeometryReader` for the
  leftover height. Capped at its content's natural height it takes exactly that when there is room —
  behaving like the plain VStack it replaced, which is why no `SpriteScale` test moved — and scrolls
  only when the screen offers less. This is the pattern for any future scrollable row on this screen.
- **A short row needs `.frame(width:, alignment: .leading)` on the CONTAINER, not centring.** Inside a
  `VStack`, an `HStack` of three sizes to its own 98pt and gets centred, which puts the stagger
  nowhere in particular. Sizing the VStack to a FULL row's `ActionGridLayout.width` and leading-
  aligning is what makes "offset half a cell" mean the same thing at 3, 4 or 5 buttons.
- **The constraint on this grid's button size is the RING, not the face.** `DashRing.diameter` is
  `ActionButtonFace.diameter + 4`, so the row's gap must be >= 4pt or adjacent rings overlap. Any
  future story that wants bigger buttons has to move `DashRing`'s overhang or drop a column first —
  `testTheGapIsWideEnoughForTwoNeighbouringRingsToMeet` fails loudly if it does neither.
- **Stagger is assertable on CENTRES.** "Row 2 sits between row 1's" = centre(1, c) is the mean of
  centre(0, c) and centre(0, c+1). That catches a whole-cell offset and a zero offset, which a
  screenshot only catches if someone looks carefully.
- Screenshot recipe unchanged, and the two-device loop works in ONE Bash call as long as
  `DEVELOPER_DIR` is exported in that call: `shutdown` -> `erase` -> `boot` -> sleep 25 ->
  `install` -> `launch ... -healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt -chargesDemo` -> sleep 20 ->
  `io <id> screenshot`. The 42mm is `F4A12A1C-1C5E-4B83-8278-341634CDE4F5`.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-212 (Map steps become a ring around the Map button; every ring is 10 segments)
- New `DashRingLayout` in `Sources/DashBar.swift` (free-standing, non-generic, `DashBarLayout`'s
  spirit): `segments = 10`, `gapDegrees = 8` and `solidSegments(filled:total:segments:)`. `DashRing`
  no longer draws one arc per unit — it draws `DashRingLayout.segments` arcs and lights
  `solidSegments` of them, and its per-instance `gapDegrees` property is GONE so two rings cannot be
  given different divider spacing. `filled`/`total` stay the raw economy; the ring draws the fraction.
- **Rounding rule (AC4): floored.** A segment lights only once fully earned — `DashBarLayout`'s rule
  (a dash is a whole unit) and `MapListRow.recordedSteps`' (a step count is never rounded up). Two
  documented consequences now that one segment can stand for more than one unit: a value under a tenth
  of its cap shows an empty ring (1 meat of 20 is half a segment), and a ring is full only at
  `filled >= total`, never a meal or a step early.
- The Map button carries `DashRing(filled: mapRecorded, total: mapTotal, tint: .green)` and speaks
  `ActionControls.mapValue` — "1050 of 3000 steps", clamped like `chargeValue` and silent at 0 total.
  It says "steps" where `chargeValue` says nothing: these two numbers are not a charge count, and
  "1500 of 25000" alone would not say what is being counted.
- `MainReadingBars` lost its map line and its `mapRecorded`/`mapTotal` parameters; `MainStepBar` and
  `MainReadingBarLayout.dashes`/`.mapSymbol`/`.mapLabel` were deleted with it (last caller gone).
  Only the Zz line is left — US-213 rings that too and retires the view.
- `ContentView` binds `let strip = model.mapStrip` once inside the `state != nil` branch and passes
  `strip?.recordedSteps ?? 0` / `?? 0`; no map selected is 0 of 0, which draws no ring.
- `-chargesDemo` grew a fifth ring: `seedMapRingForChargesDemo` selects map 1 and sets it to 35%
  (1050/3000). It also moves that map's wild-encounter marker to the same total — see learnings.
  New DEBUG-only `PlayerProfile.setRecorded(_:forMap:)` because `record(steps:)` only ADDS, and a
  screenshot flag that writes to the save must be idempotent.
- Files: Sources/DashBar.swift, Sources/ActionControls.swift, Sources/MainReadingBars.swift,
  Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/PlayerProfile.swift,
  Tests/DashBarTests.swift, Tests/ActionControlsTests.swift, Tests/MainReadingBarsTests.swift,
  Tests/MapStripTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2717 tests, 0 failures** (+5). AC6 screenshotted on 46mm
  (/tmp/us212/b2.png, brow.png, bmap.png): the five rings show the same ten arcs and the same gaps,
  filled 6 (meat 13/20), 4 (train 4/10), 6 (clean 5/8), 7 (battle 7/10) and 3 (map 1050/3000) — every
  one of them the floored value, counted off the zoomed crop.
- Tests: new `DashRingLayoutTests` class in `Tests/DashBarTests.swift` (6 tests: the shared constants,
  ten segments across all five real caps, the floored partial, both ends of the rounding rule, the
  overshoot/negative clamp, the absent economy). `ActionControlsTests` gained a US-212 section (the
  map ring off the strip's steps, the no-map-selected silence, the spoken step value, and all five
  rings at half their own caps lighting the same five segments). `MainReadingBarsTests` was rewritten
  down to what is left of that view; `MapStripTests`' US-210 "the reading no longer names the map"
  test followed the reading onto `ActionControls.mapValue`.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A demo flag that credits map steps owes a wild encounter, and its dialog covers the grid.**
  US-201 raises an encounter every 500 recorded steps and `checkForWildEncounter` runs on appear, so
  `-mapListPartialDemo` + `-chargesDemo` screenshots as "A wild Swimmon!" over the action row — the
  flag hides the exact thing it seeds. The fix is to move the map's `encounterMarker` to the same
  total the demo banks: that is what a RESOLVED encounter does, so the save is left in a state the
  game itself can reach rather than an impossible one. Any future flag that banks steps needs the
  same line. (`-mapListDemo`/`-mapListPartialDemo` have this bug today, and additionally push the map
  list, so neither can stand in for a main-screen shot.)
- **When a ring's segment count stops following its cap, the caps become free to retune.** Meat 20,
  train 10, battle 10, clean 8 gave three different tick densities in one row of five. Fixing the
  count at 10 decouples the LOOK from `consumption.json`, so a later balance change cannot silently
  restyle the grid — and `testAllFiveRingsInTheRowShareTheirSegments` reads the real bundled caps, so
  it keeps proving that after they change.
- **Delete the per-instance knob, not just the divergence.** `DashRing.gapDegrees` was a `var` with a
  default nobody overrode. Leaving it while adding `DashRingLayout.gapDegrees` would have left two
  sources for one AC ("the SAME divider spacing"); removing it makes the criterion unbreakable rather
  than merely currently-true. One test (`testTheMeatRingIsTheSameRingTheChargesUse`) referenced it and
  was simply shortened.
- **A `let` binding is legal inside a `ViewBuilder` block** — `ContentView` now reads `model.mapStrip`
  (which rebuilds a `MapStrip` on every access) once per body pass instead of twice, without
  restructuring the branch.
- Screenshot recipe unchanged; `sips -c H W --cropOffset Y X` takes HEIGHT then WIDTH and the offset
  as TOP then LEFT — getting that backwards crops the inside of a button and looks like a bug in the
  view. Row 1 of the grid sits at y≈345-405 in a 416x496 46mm shot; the five ring centres are near
  x = 73, 141, 209, 277, 345.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-213 (A Sleep button, ringed with the Zz reading, opens the Sleep Time view)
- `placesRow` gained a ninth circle: `bed.double.fill`, `.indigo`, a `NavigationLink` (not a
  `Button`) because sleep is a place you go and look at rather than an action you spend.
  `ActionControls.buttonCount` 8 -> 9, so `rowCounts` chunks [5, 4] and the scroll cap stays 64pt —
  the sprite's slot did not move and no `SpriteScale` band shifted. Exactly the two edits US-211's
  learnings predicted, plus the ring and the destination.
- The ring is `DashRing(filled: sleepHours, total: sleepHoursCap, tint: .indigo)` off new
  `sleepHours`/`sleepHoursCap` properties (defaulted 0/0, so every pre-existing call site draws no
  ring). `sleepValue` speaks "6 of 16 hours slept" — WORD FOR WORD what the Zz `DashBar` spoke, so a
  VoiceOver user who learnt the old phrasing does not have to learn a new one. Clamped and silent at
  cap 0, exactly like `mapValue`.
- `Sources/MainReadingBars.swift` is DELETED, with `MainReadingBarLayout` and `ReadingRow`. It held
  one line; US-212 took the map line, this took the Zz line, and a view with no readings is not a
  view. Nothing between the name row and the grid draws any more — every reading on the main screen
  now sits on the button it is about.
- New `Sources/SleepTimeView.swift`: the total, as the headline hours, "of 16 h", the same `DashBar`
  re-housed (indigo, so the number, the bar and the ring on the button that opened it are one
  colour), and a "Fully rested." / "Slept so far." caption. `ScrollView` + `navigationTitle("Sleep")`.
  **This is US-213's half of the screen — US-214 adds the per-Digimon bedtime / wake / nap beneath
  it**, which is why the body is a `VStack` of rows in a `ScrollView` rather than a centred hero.
- `ActionControls` is now generic over FOUR destinations. Five test fixtures and three explicit
  `ActionControls<EmptyView, EmptyView, EmptyView>` annotations across three files needed the fourth
  arg; nothing else did.
- New `-sleepTimeDemo` flag: `ContentView` pushes `SleepTimeView` onto the same stack the map list
  uses, and `seedSleepBarDemoIfRequested` banks the same 6 hours `-sleepBarDemo` does, so ONE launch
  gives both a ringed button and the screen behind it.
- Files: Sources/ActionControls.swift, Sources/SleepTimeView.swift (new), Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Sources/MapStrip.swift (comments), Sources/PartyView.swift
  (comment), Sources/MainReadingBars.swift (deleted), Tests/ActionControlsTests.swift,
  Tests/SleepTimeViewTests.swift (new), Tests/MainReadingBarsTests.swift (deleted),
  Tests/MapStripTests.swift, Tests/FeedingTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2723 tests, 0 failures** (+6: 5 new in `ActionControlsTests`,
  3 new in `SleepTimeViewTests`, 2 deleted with `MainReadingBarsTests`). Screenshots:
  /tmp/us213/ring46.png and /tmp/us213/ring42.png — nine circles, Sleep last on the staggered row,
  nothing clipped at either edge on either watch, and no Zz bar left above the grid;
  /tmp/us213/sleepbtn.png — the button zoomed, three of ten arcs lit, which is `floor(6/16*10)`;
  /tmp/us213/view46.png — the pushed Sleep screen reading "6 h / of 16 h / Slept so far."
- Tests: `testTheGridGrewANinthCircleForSleep`, `testTheSleepRingIsDrivenByTheModelsSleepHours`,
  `testTheSleepRingFloorsAndClampsLikeTheOthers`, `testSleepAnnouncesSleptAgainstGoal`,
  `testARowBuiltWithoutSleepCarriesNoRing`; `SleepTimeViewTests` drives the screen through the very
  `model.sleepHours`/`model.sleepHoursCap` expressions `ContentView` hands it and asserts the screen
  and the ring are the same fraction.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **Two flags for one story is one flag too many.** A pushed-screen demo needs BOTH the push and the
  seed, and requiring `-sleepTimeDemo -sleepBarDemo` together is a trap the next iteration will fall
  into (it reads as one flag doing nothing). Adding the new flag to the EXISTING seed's guard costs
  one `||` and makes the screenshot command a single argument. Do this for any future pushed screen
  whose content is seeded elsewhere.
- **Deleting a view means grepping for its NAME in comments, not just its call sites.** The compiler
  is silent about a doc comment that says "for `MainReadingBarLayout`'s reason"; four such references
  (PartyView, ContentView, MapStrip ×2, MainScreenModel) survived the delete and would have pointed
  at nothing. `MainReadingBarLayout`'s own doc said it was free-standing "for `EnergyBarLayout`'s
  reason", so the repointing was mechanical — a chain of reasons is worth keeping unbroken.
- **A new generic parameter on `ActionControls` costs five test fixtures.** Three files build it, and
  three places spell `ActionControls<EmptyView, EmptyView, EmptyView>` explicitly (two private helper
  return types and one `buttonCount` reference wrapped over two lines). If a tenth button ever needs
  a tenth destination, budget for that, or collapse the destinations into one `AnyView`-free protocol
  first.
- **The 42mm is the shot that matters for a row that grew.** Row 2 at four buttons is
  `staggerOffset + 4*30 + 3*4 = 17 + 132 = 149pt` inside a 166pt row, so it was never going to clip —
  but that is exactly the arithmetic `testTheStaggeredRowStaysInsideAFullRowsWidth` already loops
  over up to `columns - 1`, which is why no new layout test was needed for the ninth circle.
- **`.indigo` is free in this palette.** The grid now runs orange, red, brown, purple, green / teal,
  yellow, blue, indigo. Indigo next to blue (Dex) is the closest pair on the screen and is still
  legible at 30pt because the glyphs differ completely; a tenth button should take a hue from the
  warm end rather than adding a third blue.

## 2026-07-24 - US-214 (The Sleep Time view: total sleep and a per-Digimon sleep / wake / nap schedule)
- New `Sources/SleepRoutine.swift`: `WatchTime` (minutes since midnight, normalised into `0..<1440`,
  `formatted` = zero-padded 24-hour, `adding(minutes:)` and `minutes(until:)` both wrapping midnight)
  and `SleepRoutine` (bedtime, wakeTime, napStart, napEnd, nightMinutes, napMinutes, totalMinutes).
- **The derivation is FNV-1a over the id's UTF-8 bytes -> `SeededGenerator` (SplitMix64) -> four
  draws**, each a count of quarter-hour slots inside an authored band (`SleepRoutine.Bands`): bedtime
  20:00–24:00, night 7–10 h, nap start 12:00–16:00, nap 30–90 m. 18,785 possible routines; measured
  996 distinct across the 1,022 bundled roster ids, the rest being the birthday bound.
- **Not `String.hashValue`, and the test says so out loud.** Swift seeds that per process, so a
  routine built on it looks right in one run and changes on the next launch — which is precisely what
  AC3 forbids. `testTheSeedIsAFixedFunctionOfTheIdAndNotSwiftsHash` pins three literal seeds, and
  `testTwoShippedDigimonHaveTheirTimesPinned` pins agumon's and gabumon's four times.
- **`SleepSchedule` ALREADY EXISTS and means something else** — the user's HealthKit-inferred sleep
  window, which decides whether the Digimon is actually asleep (`isAsleep(at:wokenUntil:)`). The new
  type is `SleepRoutine`: the Digimon's own habit, display-only, driving nothing in the simulation.
  Both doc comments now point at each other so nobody wires the flavour into the sleep gate.
- `SleepTimeView` gained `digimonId` (defaulted `""`, so every pre-existing call site still compiles)
  and a `routine` computed property. Under the existing total: a `Divider`, a "SCHEDULE" header,
  three `scheduleRow`s (moon/sun/zzz, monospaced-digit trailing times, `.accessibilityElement(
  children: .combine)` so VoiceOver says "Bed, 22:30"), then "7 h 30 m a day" and the split
  "7 h night + 30 m nap" — AC4's labelling, the nap counted INTO the day rather than beside it.
- `MainScreenModel.activeDigimonId` (`state?.currentDigimonId ?? ""`) is what both `ContentView` call
  sites pass. A String, not an optional, because `SleepRoutine.forDigimon(id:)` is total.
- New `-sleepBottomDemo`: pushes the screen AND banks the 6 hours AND scrolls to the last line, off
  `ScrollViewReader` + a keyed `.task` — `SettingsView`'s `-settingsBottomDemo` hook, copied whole.
  One flag, per US-213's learning.
- Files: Sources/SleepRoutine.swift (new), Sources/SleepTimeView.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift,
  Sources/MainScreenModel.swift, Tests/SleepRoutineTests.swift (new), Tests/SleepTimeViewTests.swift.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2736 tests, 0 failures** (+13: 11 `SleepRoutineTests`, 2 in
  `SleepTimeViewTests`). Screenshots /tmp/us214/sleep46.png, sleep42.png (top: "6 h / of 16 h / Slept
  so far." then Bed 23:15, Wake 06:15, Nap 14:15 – 14:45) and bottom46.png, bottom42.png (scrolled:
  "7 h 30 m a day", "7 h night + 30 m nap"). Agumon is out in all four, and every time on screen is
  the number `testTwoShippedDigimonHaveTheirTimesPinned` asserts — the screen and the pure function
  are provably the same one.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A per-Digimon derived value is a seed function, and the seed function must be PINNED to literals.**
  Determinism-within-one-run is what `XCTAssertEqual(f(id), f(id))` proves, and it passes for
  `hashValue` too. The failure this feature can actually have — times that change between launches —
  is only caught by a pinned literal. Any future "derive something per Digimon" story should copy
  `SleepRoutine.seed(for:)` rather than reach for `Hasher`.
- **`SleepSchedule` was taken.** Two things in this codebase are "when the Digimon sleeps": the health
  window (real, gating) and the routine (flavour, display). Grep for the name before adding a type in
  a domain this old — the collision was found by the compiler, but naming the new one `SleepSchedule2`
  or, worse, merging them, would have put a cosmetic bedtime in charge of the sleep gate.
- **`simctl launch` needs `com.digivpet.DigiVPet`, NOT `com.example.DigiVPet`.** Half an hour went to
  `FBSOpenApplicationServiceErrorDomain code=4` before `xcrun simctl listapps <id> | grep Bundle`
  settled it. The install succeeds and only the launch fails, so it reads like a crash on launch.
- **A "scrolls on the 42mm" AC is a `-xBottomDemo` flag, not an argument.** `simctl` can neither tap
  nor scroll, so the only proof is a `ScrollViewReader` + a DEBUG `.task` that scrolls to a `.id()`d
  last row after a 500 ms beat (the beat matters — `.task` runs before the rows are measured).
  `SettingsView` and `PartyView` both already carry this exact hook; copy one.
- **Screenshot recipe, corrected end to end** (one Bash call, `DEVELOPER_DIR` exported in it):
  `xcrun simctl bootstatus <id> -b` -> `install` -> `launch <id> com.digivpet.DigiVPet -healthAnswered
  -noNotificationPrompt -<flag>` -> `sleep 20` -> `io <id> screenshot`. A `shutdown`/`erase`/`boot`
  cycle needs ~30 s AND the app reinstalled after it; `bootstatus` on an already-booted device is
  instant and skips all of that.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-215 (Settings shows the data-collection status)
- New `Sources/HealthCollectionStatus.swift`: `HealthCollectionStatus` (.collecting / .notCollecting /
  .unavailable / .checking) with `init(phase: HealthAuthorizationModel.Phase)`, `title`, `detail`,
  `symbolName`, `tint` — plus `HealthCopy.neverLeavesTheWatch`, the one privacy string both the
  onboarding screen and Settings now say. `HealthAuthorizationModel.collectionStatus` is the bridge.
- **It is a VIEW of the gate's phase, not a second authorization source.** `HealthAuthorizationGate`'s
  content closure now takes a `HealthCollectionStatus` (`(HealthCollectionStatus) -> Content`), which
  `DigiVPetApp` forwards into `ContentView(model:healthStatus:)` and on into
  `SettingsView(settings:healthStatus:)`. A plain VALUE, not the model: the gate observes the model,
  so a phase change re-renders and pushes a fresh status down, and nothing below the gate has to know
  HealthKit exists. `.ready` -> collecting; `.explaining`/`.requesting`/`.denied` -> not collecting;
  `.unavailable` -> unavailable.
- **`-settingsDemo` now also waves the gate through, in DEBUG only.** Two of the three statuses are
  states the gate NEVER runs the app in, so `-healthDenied` / `-healthUnavailable` alone photograph
  the onboarding and unavailable screens and can never reach the Settings row. The flag that already
  pushes Settings does the bypass too (US-213's one-flag rule); `showsContentRegardless(_:)` is a
  static pure function so a test can pin that it cannot fire without the argument. Nothing else moves
  — the status shown is still what the real state machine computed from the injected authorizer.
- Files: Sources/HealthCollectionStatus.swift (new), Sources/HealthAuthorizationView.swift,
  Sources/SettingsView.swift, Sources/ContentView.swift, Sources/DigiVPetApp.swift,
  Tests/SettingsHealthStatusTests.swift (new).
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2744 tests, 0 failures** (+8, all in `SettingsHealthStatusTests`).
  Screenshots on BOTH watches, `-settingsDemo -noNotificationPrompt -<flag>`:
  /tmp/us215/healthAnswered-{46,42}.png (green heart, "Collecting health data", "Your Digimon is
  earning energy."), healthDenied-{46,42}.png (orange slashed heart, "Not collecting", "Your Digimon
  can't earn energy without it."), healthUnavailable-{46,42}.png (grey triangle, "Unavailable", "This
  device has no Health data."). "Never leaves this watch." is on all six.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A `Label` will not wrap inside a watchOS list row, whatever line limit you give it.**
  "Collecting health data" truncated to "Collecting health…" on the 42mm — losing the only word that
  says what is collected — with `.lineLimit(2)` set on the `Label`. The fix is an
  `HStack(alignment: .firstTextBaseline) { Image; Text.lineLimit(2).fixedSize(horizontal: false,
  vertical: true) }`. Budget ~40 characters for a single-line caption row on a 42mm screen; that is
  also why the collecting detail says "earning energy" instead of naming the four metrics.
- **A stale system permission alert survives terminate, uninstall AND reinstall on a booted
  simulator.** The 46mm sat behind the notification alert from an earlier session, so all three of
  the first screenshots photographed the alert; `-noNotificationPrompt` cannot help, because the
  alert was already up. `shutdown` + `erase` + `boot` (~90 s, and the app must be reinstalled after)
  is the only thing that cleared it. Check the device with a bare `simctl io <id> screenshot` BEFORE
  launching — if something is already on screen, the other watch is the cheaper fix.
- **A screenshot AC can ask for a state the app's own gating makes unreachable.** Two of US-215's
  three statuses are exactly that. The honest fix is a DEBUG bypass on the flag that already opens
  the screen, pinned by a test that it needs its argument — not weakening the gate, and not
  photographing a preview and calling it the screen.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-216: The Digimon paces at one steady speed, wall to wall, no sprinting
- Rewrote `MovementModel` as a deterministic ping-pong. The step function has NO randomness left:
  `Heading`/`SeededGenerator`/`decide()` are gone, `facing` IS the direction of travel, and one
  stride is always `stepDistance` (7.5pt). The seed's only remaining job is the opening direction —
  `seed.isMultiple(of: 2) ? .right : .left` — which is all that is needed to stop two Digimon on one
  screen pacing in lockstep. RESTING was removed outright and the choice documented on
  `advanceOneStep()`: a pause mid-floor reads as hesitation, and nothing on this screen needs it.
- Catch-up: `maximumCatchUp: TimeInterval = 60` became `maximumCatchUpSteps = 2` (with
  `maximumCatchUp` kept as a derived `TimeInterval`). `advance(to:)` applies `min(due, cap)` steps;
  when it truncates it restamps `updatedAt` to `now` so the surplus is FORGIVEN, not banked.
  `hold(at:)` and the `>=` wall behaviour are untouched.
- Added a `guard bound > 0` to `advanceOneStep()`: with no floor to walk on the two wall checks
  used to flip `facing` on every single step and the sprite shimmered on the spot.
- Files: Sources/Movement.swift, Tests/MovementTests.swift, prd.json, progress.txt.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2746 tests, 0 failures** (+2 net; MovementTests 15 -> 17).
  New/rewritten tests: `testThePaceIsConstantAndTurnsOnlyAtAWall` (every stride identical, a reversal
  only ever standing on a wall), `testALongGapMovesNoFurtherThanTheCap` (0.75s / 10s / 1h / 24h all
  move <= 15pt), `testALongGapIsNotRepaidOnLaterAdvances`, `testAdvancesChoppedWithinTheCapAgree`,
  `testTheSeedChoosesTheOpeningDirection`. Simulator: 42mm with `-wanderDemo`, screenshots 2s apart
  (/tmp/paced_1..6.png) show right wall -> centre -> left wall and back, facing matching travel.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A CAPPED CATCH-UP TRADES AWAY "ANY CHOPPING OF TIME AGREES".** The old model's headline invariant
  — forty 0.25s advances land where one 10s advance does — is not just weakened by US-216, it is the
  thing US-216 deletes, because paying back a gap in full IS the sprint. What survives is agreement
  up to the cap (`testAdvancesChoppedWithinTheCapAgree`: twenty 0.5s ticks == forty 0.25s ticks),
  and four existing tests had to stop driving the model with multi-second jumps. If you add another
  capped simulation, expect its "any cadence agrees" test to need this same narrowing.
- **THE COST OF THE CAP IS THAT A STARVED RENDER LOOP CRAWLS RATHER THAN CATCHING UP.** Taking eight
  `simctl io screenshot`s back to back starves the app's `TimelineView`, and the sprite then moves
  ~2 steps per delivered frame instead of 4/second — it looked frozen and I nearly filed it as a bug.
  It is not: idle the simulator between captures (`sleep 2` per shot) and the full edge-to-edge pace
  is there. **Pace wander/animation screenshots at least 2s apart, and never judge motion from a
  burst.**
- **`isMultiple(of: 2)` ON THE SEED IS ENOUGH WHEN THE ONLY CHOICE IS BINARY.** The pinned-seed-
  function rule (US-214) exists because `hashValue` is per-process; a seed the caller already owns
  has no such problem, so a whole `SeededGenerator` for one bit is ceremony. It also let the model
  drop its RNG field entirely, which is what makes "there is no randomness in the walk" literally
  true rather than a comment.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-217: A Digitama does not walk
- `MainScreenModel.isWandering` gained ONE leading clause, `state?.stage != .digitama`. It is an
  added condition, not a replacement: an egg's resting animation is the ordinary `.idle` loop, so
  every other clause was happily true while it paced, and asleep/eating/sick/dead/overlay still turn
  the walk off through exactly the reasons they always did.
- The suspension rides the existing `isMoving: false` -> `MovementModel.hold(at:)` path, so the
  walk's clock keeps up and hatching costs one step of travel rather than the whole incubation.
- AC2 (the egg sits at CENTRE, not where the last Digimon fell) needed one new thing:
  `MovementModel.recentre()`, plus `SpriteWanderer.position(at:bound:isMoving:holdsAtCentre:)` which
  calls it alongside the hold. `WanderingSpriteView` reads `holdsAtCentre` off its own `stage`
  (`stage == Stage.digitama.rawValue` — `stage` IS the sprite subfolder name), so nothing new is
  threaded through `ContentView`. Asserted on EVERY call rather than on the transition into egg-ness,
  so no frame can draw the egg at the dead Digimon's spot.
- Files: Sources/{MainScreenModel,Movement,WanderingSpriteView}.swift,
  Tests/{MovementTests,WanderingTests}.swift, prd.json, progress.txt.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2752 tests, 0 failures** (+6). New tests —
  `WanderingTests.testAnUnhatchedDigitamaDoesNotWander` (driven off a real `loadOrCreate` egg save,
  and it asserts `animation == .idle` first so the reason the stage must be named is on the record),
  `testHatchingOutOfTheDigitamaResumesTheWalk`, `testTheEggRuleDoesNotReplaceTheOtherSuspensions`;
  `MovementTests.testAModelOnlyEverHeldNeverLeavesTheCentre` (600 held seconds, offset 0),
  `testRecentringPutsTheSpriteBackInTheMiddle`, and
  `testAnEggHeldAtCentreDoesNotInheritThePreviousDigimonsPosition` (the rebirth, through
  `SpriteWanderer`: walk off centre -> egg at 0 -> still 0 after 10 min -> one step of time is
  exactly one `stepDistance` of travel).
- SIMULATOR, 42mm (46mm had a stale notification alert up, so it was skipped — see US-215): fresh
  save via uninstall+install, 6 screenshots paced 2s apart, on the PRE-story build and the POST-story
  build. Lit-pixel centroid of the sprite band (rows 140-265, luma > 40) on a 374px-wide screen:
      before  196.5  76.5  191.5  301.5  166.5  101.5   <- 225px of travel
      after   186.5 186.5  186.5  186.5  186.5  186.5   <- dead centre, every frame
  The bounding box still breathes between frames (139-234 vs 147-226) because the egg's idle/wobble
  loop animates in place. That is the pose, not travel.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **MEASURE "DID THE SPRITE MOVE" BY LIT-PIXEL CENTROID, NEVER BY BOUNDING BOX.** Every sprite in
  this game animates in place — the egg wobbles, the Digimon's two walk frames differ in width — so
  `xmin`/`xmax` change from frame to frame with zero travel and a bbox comparison reports motion that
  is not there. The centroid of `luma > 40` over the sprite band is stable to three decimals across
  a pose change and moves by exactly the travel. **numpy is NOT installed; PIL 12.3.0 is** — a plain
  `im.convert('L').load()` double loop over ~125 rows costs well under a second per shot.
- **THE CHEAPEST BEFORE/AFTER IS `git stash push -- Sources Tests`, REBUILD, CAPTURE, `stash pop`.**
  ~90s per side on this project and it produces the only evidence that actually settles a "does it
  still X" acceptance criterion. The install must be `uninstall` + `install` when the story is about
  a FRESH save, or the previous run's hatched Digimon is still in the store.
- **`SpriteWanderer` IS `@State` AND SURVIVES A REBIRTH.** The view's identity does not change when
  the Digimon dies and an egg replaces it, so the new sprite inherits the dead one's offset. Anything
  that must reset a `@State` model on a game event has to say so declaratively on every call (as
  `holdsAtCentre` does) rather than via `.onChange`, which would leave one frame drawn at the old
  value.
- **US-218 SEAM:** the egg is `state?.stage == .digitama` on the model and
  `stage == Stage.digitama.rawValue` in the sprite view. US-218 wants the same fact on
  `ActionControls`; put it on `MainScreenModel` as a named `isEgg` property and let both this clause
  and the action guards read it, rather than adding a third spelling.
---

## 2026-07-24 - US-218 - Feed, Train and Battle are refused while it is still an egg
- Took US-217's own advice and made the egg ONE named fact: `MainScreenModel.isEgg`
  (`state?.stage == .digitama`) plus `MainScreenModel.eggActionReason = "It is still an egg."`.
  `isWandering` now reads `!isEgg` instead of respelling the stage comparison, so there are two
  readers of one property rather than two comparisons.
- `ActionControls` gained `var isEgg: Bool = false`, declared right after `lightState` (memberwise
  init order — ContentView passes it there). `.disabled(isFeedDisabled)` on Feed,
  `.disabled(isTrainDisabled)` on Train, and `isBattleDisabled` became
  `!canAffordBattle || isEgg`. All three grey through the existing `ActionButtonFace`
  `@Environment(\.isEnabled)` path; no second source of truth, nothing removed from the grid.
  Feed and Train are disabled by the EGG ONLY — an empty larder or no train charges is still a
  message from the model, not a greyed circle.
- `feed()`, `train()` and `battle()` each guard `!isEgg` FIRST: before `wakeIfAsleep()`, before
  `FeedAction`/`TrainAction`, before battle's death/charge/energy guards and before matchmaking.
  So a blocked egg action spends no meat, no charge and no energy, counts no care mistake, opens no
  minigame and plays no pose and no motion — `show(nil, message:)`, exactly like every other block.
- Files: Sources/{MainScreenModel,ActionControls,ContentView}.swift,
  Tests/{EggActionsTests(new),ActionControlsTests,DeathTests}.swift, prd.json, progress.txt.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2764 tests, 0 failures** (+12). New `EggActionsTests` (8) is
  built on a `Ledger` struct that snapshots meat, both charges, all four energies,
  `careMistakeCount`, `stageOverfeeds`, `stageTrainingSessions` and `stageSleepDisturbances` in one
  value, so each blocked case asserts `Ledger(model) == before` rather than six separate reads — an
  egg guard that showed the message but still spent the charge would fail. Its fixture stocks
  EVERYTHING (meat, charges, 40 in each energy, hunger 3) so the only possible reason for a block is
  the stage, and each `.digitama` case has a `.babyI` twin proving the action still works today.
  4 new `ActionControlsTests` cover the three disabled buttons, the six untouched ones, the
  unchanged `[5, 4]` grid, and that the egg does not hijack the unaffordable-energy caption.
- Broke and fixed ONE pre-existing test: `DeathTests.testADeadDigimonNeitherHatchesNorEats` pinned
  `.blocked(reason: "It cannot eat.")` on a fixture that is a dead EGG. Still blocked, still eats
  nothing; the egg guard now runs ahead of `FeedAction`'s death arm, so the reason shown is the egg
  one. Updated the expectation to `MainScreenModel.eggActionReason` with a comment saying why.
- SIMULATOR, 42mm (46mm still had the stale notification alert up from an earlier session — see
  US-215; the bare probe screenshot found it in a second):
    /tmp/us218/before42.png — the pre-story build on a fresh egg: Feed orange, Train red, Battle
      already grey (0 energy), Clean already grey (0 poop).
    /tmp/us218/buttons42.png + buttons42-zoom.png — after: Feed, Train and Battle all grey, Map
      green, Party teal, Light yellow, Dex blue, Sleep indigo, nine circles in a 5-and-4 grid.
    /tmp/us218/feed-message42.png — Feed tapped on the egg: "It is still an egg." on one line in the
      orange name row, egg sprite unchanged, no pose.
- Added a debug-only `-eggFeedDemo` seed (`seedEggFeedDemoIfRequested`) beside the other seeds: it
  is the ONLY one that does not move off the starting egg, stocks the larder so an empty one cannot
  be the reason, sets `actionDuration = 60` and calls `feed()`.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **A NEW GUARD PLACED "FIRST" STEALS THE MESSAGE FROM AN OLDER GUARD, AND A TEST SOMEWHERE PINS
  THAT STRING.** A fixture can be in two refusing states at once (`DeathTests`' dead EGG), and the
  only symptom is one `XCTAssertEqual` on a reason. Before adding a guard ahead of the existing ones,
  `grep -rn '<the old reason string>' Tests` — and when it fires, fix it by re-pinning to the NEW
  reason with a comment, never by loosening the assertion to "some block".
- **A "SPENDS NOTHING" ACCEPTANCE CRITERION IS ONE `Equatable` SNAPSHOT STRUCT, NOT SIX ASSERTIONS.**
  `EggActionsTests.Ledger` reads the whole economy off the model in an `init(_ model:)` (marked
  `@MainActor`, since `MainScreenModel`'s properties are), and every blocked case is then
  `XCTAssertEqual(Ledger(model), before)`. It costs ten lines and it catches the currency the story
  did not think to name. Copy it for any future "the tap must cost nothing" story.
- **`EnergyType` IS THE ENUM'S NAME, NOT `Energy`** — `EnergyType.allCases` over
  `state.stageEnergy[$1]` is how you snapshot all four at once.
- **A DEMO SEED IS HOW YOU SCREENSHOT AN ACTION'S MESSAGE, BECAUSE `simctl` CANNOT TAP.** The shape
  is fixed: a `#if DEBUG` `seedXDemoIfRequested()` called from the block at the end of `start()`,
  guarded on a `-xDemo` launch argument, ending in `actionDuration = 60` (the 2s hold does not
  survive boot + install + launch + `sleep 20`) and then the real action call. Never stage the
  outcome by hand — call the shipped method, or the screenshot proves nothing.

## 2026-07-24 - US-219: The play area and the map behind it are 80 percent of their old height
- `MainScreenLayout` gained `playAreaHeightFraction = 0.8` and `playAreaHeight(in:) -> floor(available
  * 0.8)`, free-standing exactly like `SpriteScale.fitting` so a test reads the arithmetic without a
  view graph.
- The sprite's `GeometryReader` STILL claims the whole flexible row — that is what keeps the stats
  strip, the name row and the action grid byte-for-byte where they were — but the content inside it
  is now `.frame(width: geometry.size.width, height: band, alignment: sick ? .bottom : .center)`,
  wrapped in a plain `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity, maxHeight: .infinity)` that CENTRES that band in
  the row. The reclaimed fifth is left empty and splits evenly above and below.
- `SpriteSlotBoundsKey`'s `anchorPreference` MOVED off the row and onto the shortened band (it now
  sits between the sick-badge overlay and the centring frame). That one move is the entire
  implementation of "the map, the scrim and the poop pile shrink with it" — all three are placed off
  that anchor, so there is no second rect anywhere. `SpriteScale.fitting` is likewise handed `band`
  rather than `geometry.size.height`.
- Files: Sources/ContentView.swift (constant + fn, the band frame, the anchor move, two comments),
  Tests/MainScreenLayoutTests.swift (+4 tests, re-measured evidence), prd.json, progress.txt.
- Verified: build green; FULL suite **2768 tests, 0 failures** (+4).

- **RE-MEASURED SLOTS — AND THE OLD PINNED NUMBERS WERE STALE BY HALF.** Method: the map is painted
  off `SpriteSlotBoundsKey`, so the band that changes between `-mapDemo=01_grassland` and
  `-mapDemo=none` IS the play area, measured directly instead of inferred from a sprite. Baseline
  built in a `git worktree` at HEAD; all three sims `simctl erase`d first; both builds launched
  `-healthAnswered -noNotificationPrompt -wanderDemo -mapDemo=...`.
      screen        row (before)   band (after)   floor(row*0.8)   sprite scale
      41mm  S9       63.5pt         50.0pt         50.0  exact      3 -> 3
      42mm  S11      66.5pt         53.0pt         53.0  exact      4 -> 3
      46mm  S11      76.0pt         60.0pt         60.0  exact      4 -> 3
  All three match the shipped arithmetic to the point. `MainScreenLayoutTests` pinned 41.5 (41mm) and
  56.0 (46mm) from US-194 — those were **arithmetic, not measurement** (49.5-8, 64.0-8), and US-196,
  US-199, US-208, US-210, US-211 and US-213 have since deleted the currency row, the map strip and
  both reading bars, every point of which went silently back into the one flexible row. The tests now
  pin the three measured bands with the rows beside them for comparison.
- Scale confirmed independently by Agumon's ink WIDTH on the `-mapDemo=none` shots (13 sprite pixels,
  so 78px at @2x is scale 3 and 104px is scale 4): before 78/104/104, after 78/78/78 on 41/42/46mm.
  Ink heights 72px = 12 rows x 6, inside a 96px (48pt) sprite box inside a 100/106/120px band — the
  sprite never overflows. `SpriteScale.minimum` (2) never binds: the smallest band is 50pt.
- Margins measured off the band rows: 46mm before 146-297, after 162-281 — 16px reclaimed at the top
  and 16px at the bottom, an even split. 41mm 130-256 -> 144-243 (14/13px), 42mm 134-266 -> 148-253
  (14/13px). Odd totals split as evenly as whole pixels allow.
- SCREENSHOTS /tmp/us219 (not committed): after42_map.png, after46_map.png against before42_map.png,
  before46_map.png. Visibly shorter map band with black margin above and below, the map still filling
  it edge to edge with no letterboxing, the Digimon inside it, and all nine action circles, the name
  row and the stats strip untouched and on screen.
- NOTE for whoever ships US-221: the sick badge's `clearanceFloor` (50pt) now sits right ON the 41mm
  band and above the 42mm one, so an ILL Digimon's badge overlaps the sprite on those screens. That
  is the documented behaviour of a short slot (`SickBadgeLayout.clearanceFloor`'s own comment says the
  badge cannot fix it), not a regression this story introduced — 41mm was already below it — but
  US-221 shrinks the sprite again and will make the overlap disappear on its own.

**Learnings for future iterations:**
- **THE MAP BAND DIFF IS THE ONLY HONEST WAY TO MEASURE THE SPRITE SLOT, AND IT TAKES ONE MINUTE.**
  `-mapDemo=<asset>` vs `-mapDemo=none`, then find the longest run of rows where the two shots differ.
  **Use a 0.5 width threshold, not 0.75:** the grassland asset has dark rows that differ from black in
  only ~73% of the width, and a 0.75 cut silently truncates the band by 16px (it reported 62pt on a
  76pt slot). Print the per-row profile before trusting any single number.
- **A PINNED "MEASURED" NUMBER THAT WAS ACTUALLY ARITHMETIC ROTS SILENTLY, AND EVERY LATER STORY
  INHERITS IT.** US-194 published 41.5/56.0 as `49.5 - 8` / `64.0 - 8`; six row-deleting stories later
  the real rows were 63.5/76.0 and nothing failed, because the tests only asserted what those numbers
  map to. **Any story that adds OR REMOVES a row in `ContentView`'s VStack must re-measure the slot** —
  removal is the dangerous direction, because a bigger Digimon looks like a nice surprise rather than
  a bug. US-221's PRD arithmetic is built on the stale numbers; re-measure before trusting it.
- **TO SHORTEN A BAND WITHOUT MOVING ANYTHING ELSE, KEEP THE FLEXIBLE ROW AND SHRINK ITS CONTENT.**
  `GeometryReader { let band = f(geometry.size.height); content.frame(height: band).anchorPreference(...)
  .frame(maxHeight: .infinity) }`. The row still claims the leftover height so no sibling moves; the
  inner fixed frame is the band; the trailing infinite frame centres it; and putting the anchor
  BETWEEN them is what makes every layer placed off that anchor track the band rather than the row.
  Anchors resolve after placement, so the centring frame does not have to be accounted for by hand.
- **`git worktree add /tmp/<name> HEAD` + `-derivedDataPath` is the clean baseline** (the stash recipe
  races on DerivedData). Build it in the BACKGROUND while capturing the "after" shots — the two
  halves of a before/after are independent and this iteration cost ~90s instead of ~4 minutes.
